# Master Interview Q&A ‚Äî Vol 2
> Deep-dive answers with ELI5, flowcharts, step-by-step code, and complexity analysis.

---

## REACT ‚Äî Core Hooks

---

### Q1. What is the difference between `useState` and `useReducer`? When would you choose one over the other?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> **`useState`** is like a light switch ‚Äî you flip it ON or OFF. Simple. One thing changes at a time.
>
> **`useReducer`** is like a TV remote ‚Äî you press a *named button* (action), and the TV (state) changes in a predictable way based on what button you pressed. You have a rulebook (reducer) that says "if you press VOLUME_UP, do this; if you press MUTE, do that."

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî How Each Works

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                        useState Flow                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   Component                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  [useState(initialValue)]                                           ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ returns: [value, setValue]                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  User event ‚Üí setValue(newValue)                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  React schedules re-render with new value                           ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                       useReducer Flow                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ   Component                                                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  [useReducer(reducerFn, initialState)]                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ returns: [state, dispatch]                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  User event ‚Üí dispatch({ type: 'ACTION', payload })                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  reducerFn(currentState, action) ‚Üí newState                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚ñº                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  React re-renders with newState                                     ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

---

#### When to Use Which

```
Decision Tree:
                     ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
                     ‚îÇ  How complex is your  ‚îÇ
                     ‚îÇ       state?          ‚îÇ
                     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
                                ‚îÇ
              ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
              ‚ñº                 ‚ñº                  ‚ñº
     1-2 simple values   Multiple fields     Multiple fields
     (toggle, count,     tightly coupled    + complex logic
      input string)       (form with 5+     + multiple actions
                          fields)           + transitions between
                                             states
              ‚îÇ                 ‚îÇ                  ‚îÇ
              ‚ñº                 ‚ñº                  ‚ñº
         useState          useState or         useReducer
                            useReducer         (strongly prefer)
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî `useState` Example (simple counter)

```jsx
import { useState } from 'react';

function Counter() {
  // WHY useState: we have ONE piece of state ‚Äî the count. Simple.
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);
  //    ‚îî‚îÄ current value    ‚îî‚îÄ updater fn    ‚îî‚îÄ initial value

  return (
    <div>
      <p>{count}</p>
      {/* WHY direct call: no derived logic, just "set to count + 1" */}
      <button onClick={() => setCount(count + 1)}>+</button>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(count - 1)}>-</button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step:**
1. `useState(0)` ‚Äî React creates a state cell in memory holding `0`
2. Each render, React reads that same cell and gives you the current value
3. `setCount(count + 1)` ‚Äî schedules a re-render with value `count + 1`
4. React re-executes the component function, `count` is now `1`

---

#### Code ‚Äî `useReducer` Example (shopping cart with multiple actions)

```jsx
import { useReducer } from 'react';

// WHY a separate reducer: all state transitions are co-located.
// If state logic lives inside the component, it becomes a mess.
// Reducer = pure function: (currentState, action) ‚Üí newState
// "Pure" means: no side effects, same input always gives same output.

const cartReducer = (state, action) => {
  switch (action.type) {
    
    case 'ADD_ITEM':
      // WHY spread (...state): we never mutate state directly in React.
      // React uses reference equality to detect changes.
      // If we mutate the existing object, React may not notice the change.
      return {
        ...state,
        items: [...state.items, action.payload],  // new array, new reference
        total: state.total + action.payload.price,
      };

    case 'REMOVE_ITEM':
      // WHY filter: creates a new array (new reference = React detects change)
      const removed = state.items.find(i => i.id === action.payload);
      return {
        ...state,
        items: state.items.filter(i => i.id !== action.payload),
        total: state.total - (removed?.price ?? 0),
      };

    case 'CLEAR_CART':
      // WHY return full object: reducer always returns the FULL state shape
      return { items: [], total: 0 };

    default:
      // WHY return state: unknown actions should be no-ops, not crashes
      return state;
  }
};

// WHY outside component: if defined inside, it gets re-created every render
// and useReducer would see a "new" reducer function reference each time
const initialState = { items: [], total: 0 };

function ShoppingCart() {
  // WHY useReducer: we have 3 different actions that each modify state
  // differently. With useState we'd need 3 setters and duplicate logic.
  const [cart, dispatch] = useReducer(cartReducer, initialState);
  //    ‚îî‚îÄ state object    ‚îî‚îÄ dispatch fn   ‚îî‚îÄ reducer  ‚îî‚îÄ initial

  const addItem = (item) => {
    // WHY dispatch with type + payload:
    // type = WHAT happened (action name)
    // payload = the data needed to perform the action
    dispatch({ type: 'ADD_ITEM', payload: item });
  };

  return (
    <div>
      <p>Items: {cart.items.length} | Total: ${cart.total}</p>
      <button onClick={() => addItem({ id: 1, name: 'Book', price: 12 })}>
        Add Book
      </button>
      <button onClick={() => dispatch({ type: 'CLEAR_CART' })}>
        Clear
      </button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step:**
1. `useReducer(cartReducer, initialState)` ‚Äî React stores `{ items: [], total: 0 }` in memory
2. `dispatch({ type: 'ADD_ITEM', payload: item })` ‚Äî React calls `cartReducer(currentState, action)`
3. The reducer computes and returns the next state (new object reference)
4. React sees the new reference ‚Üí schedules re-render ‚Üí component re-executes with new `cart`

---

#### Key Differences at a Glance

| Feature | `useState` | `useReducer` |
|---|---|---|
| Best for | 1‚Äì2 independent values | Complex / related state |
| How you update | Call setter directly | Dispatch a named action |
| Logic lives | Inline in component | In pure reducer function |
| Testability | Component-level | Reducer is pure ‚Äî easily unit-tested without React |
| Predictability | Fine for simple cases | Better for multi-step transitions |
| State shape | Single value / object | Any shape, usually object |

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| `useState` read | O(1) | Direct cell lookup in React's fiber |
| `setState` call | O(1) | Enqueues update, no heavy computation |
| `useReducer` dispatch | O(1) amortized | Calls reducer synchronously, then schedules re-render |
| Reducer function | Depends on your code | If you `.filter()` N items ‚Üí O(N); `.find()` ‚Üí O(N) |
| Memory per state | O(size of state) | React holds current + pending state in fiber node |

---

### Q2. What happens if you don't pass a dependency array to `useEffect`?

---

#### ELI5

> `useEffect` is like a helper who watches for changes and does a job.
>
> - **No array** ‚Üí the helper re-does the job *after every single render*, no matter what changed. He's very eager.
> - **Empty array `[]`** ‚Üí the helper does the job *once* when you first walk in the room, then sits down forever.
> - **Array with values `[a, b]`** ‚Üí the helper only re-does the job when `a` or `b` specifically changes. Smart and efficient.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî All 3 Variants

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ              useEffect Dependency Array Behavior                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  useEffect(() => { ... })          ‚Üê No array                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Runs after EVERY render (mount, update, anything)          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  useEffect(() => { ... }, [])      ‚Üê Empty array                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Runs ONCE after initial mount only                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  useEffect(() => { ... }, [a, b])  ‚Üê With dependencies              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Runs after mount + whenever a or b changes                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ          (React uses Object.is() to compare prev vs next value)     ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

Timeline for useEffect(() => { ... }) ‚Äî NO ARRAY:

  Mount       Update(1)   Update(2)   Update(3)
    ‚îÇ             ‚îÇ           ‚îÇ           ‚îÇ
    ‚ñº             ‚ñº           ‚ñº           ‚ñº
  Effect ‚úÖ    Effect ‚úÖ   Effect ‚úÖ   Effect ‚úÖ
  runs here   runs here   runs here   runs here
  
  ‚öÝ Cleanup from previous run fires BEFORE next effect runs
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Demonstrating All 3 Cases

```jsx
import { useState, useEffect } from 'react';

function Demo() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);
  const [name, setName]   = useState('Alice');

  // ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 1: No dependency array ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  // WHY you'd accidentally write this: you forget the second arg.
  // WHAT happens: runs after EVERY render ‚Äî even if count didn't change.
  // DANGER: if this effect calls setCount, it causes an INFINITE LOOP.
  //         effect runs ‚Üí state changes ‚Üí re-render ‚Üí effect runs ‚Üí ‚àû
  useEffect(() => {
    console.log('Runs after every render');
    // ‚ùå NEVER do: setCount(c => c + 1)  ‚Üê infinite loop!
  });

  // ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 2: Empty array ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  // WHY use []: you want one-time setup (fetch initial data, set up socket).
  // WHAT happens: runs once after the component first mounts.
  // Think of it as: componentDidMount in class components.
  useEffect(() => {
    console.log('Runs only once ‚Äî on mount');
    // Good for: fetch initial data, subscribe to external store, set up timers
    return () => {
      // WHY cleanup: runs when component unmounts.
      // Without cleanup: subscriptions/timers persist after component is gone ‚Üí memory leak
      console.log('Cleanup on unmount');
    };
  }, []); // ‚Üê empty array = "I depend on nothing, never re-run"

  // ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 3: Specific dependencies ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  // WHY list deps explicitly: React only re-runs if `count` actually changed.
  // The ESLint rule `exhaustive-deps` will warn if you miss any dep.
  useEffect(() => {
    console.log(`count changed to: ${count}`);
    // React compares previous count vs current count using Object.is()
    // Object.is(1, 1) = true ‚Üí skip   |   Object.is(1, 2) = false ‚Üí run
  }, [count]); // ‚Üê only re-run when count changes; name changes are ignored

  return (
    <div>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>
      <button onClick={() => setName('Bob')}>Change Name</button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step (Case 3 `[count]`):**
1. Component mounts ‚Üí effect runs once (initial run always happens)
2. `setCount` fires ‚Üí React re-renders ‚Üí React compares `prevCount` vs `newCount`
3. `Object.is(0, 1)` = `false` ‚Üí count changed ‚Üí React runs the effect again
4. `setName('Bob')` fires ‚Üí React compares `prevCount` vs `newCount` = same ‚Üí **skips** effect

---

#### Common Mistakes

```
Mistake 1: Object/Array in deps creates infinite loop
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  const options = { limit: 10 };           // ‚Üê new object reference every render
  useEffect(() => { fetch(options) }, [options]);
  // Object.is({limit:10}, {limit:10}) = false (different references!)
  // ‚Üí runs on every render ‚Üí INFINITE LOOP
  
  FIX: useMemo or move `options` outside the component or use primitives

Mistake 2: Missing dependency (stale closure ‚Äî see Q6)
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  useEffect(() => {
    console.log(count);  // reads count
  }, []);                // but count NOT listed ‚Üí reads stale value from mount
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Scenario | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| React comparing deps | O(N) where N = number of deps | Loops through each dep, `Object.is()` per item |
| Without array | O(renders) total | Runs effect on every render |
| With `[]` | O(1) | Runs exactly once |
| With `[a, b, c]` | O(changes to a/b/c) | Runs only when one of those changes |

---

### Q3. How do you handle race conditions in `useEffect` when fetching data?

---

#### ELI5

> Imagine you order 2 pizzas at different times. Pizza #2 gets delivered FIRST by accident (faster driver). Then pizza #1 arrives and you display it ‚Äî but you actually wanted pizza #2 (the latest order)!
>
> A race condition is when an **older async request resolves AFTER a newer one**, and you accidentally display stale data. The fix is: **when a newer request starts, cancel or ignore all previous ones.**

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî The Problem vs The Fix

```
THE PROBLEM (no cleanup):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types "re"               User types "react"
       ‚îÇ                               ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº                               ‚ñº
  fetch("/search?q=re")        fetch("/search?q=react")
       ‚îÇ                               ‚îÇ
       ‚îÇ                      responds in 100ms ‚úÖ
       ‚îÇ                               ‚îÇ
       ‚îÇ                        setResults("react results")
       ‚îÇ                               ‚îÇ
  responds in 500ms ‚ùå            [correct data shown]
       ‚îÇ
  setResults("re results")   ‚Üê OVERWRITES correct data! üí•
       ‚îÇ
  [stale/wrong data shown]

THE FIX (cleanup with ignore flag):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types "react"
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  useEffect runs
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ let ignore = false        ‚Üê flag starts as "don't ignore"
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  fetch("/search?q=react")
       ‚îÇ
  [user types "reactjs" ‚Üí new effect runs]
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ cleanup of previous effect: ignore = true  ‚Üê flag flipped!
       ‚îÇ
  [previous fetch resolves]
       ‚îÇ
  if (!ignore) setResults(...)   ‚Üê ignored! flag is true
       ‚îÇ
  ‚úÖ Only latest fetch's result is used
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Race Condition Problem

```jsx
// ‚ùå BAD: race condition possible
function SearchBad() {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('');
  const [results, setResults] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY this is dangerous:
    // If query changes quickly (user typing fast), multiple fetches can be
    // in-flight simultaneously. The LAST to RESOLVE wins, not last to START.
    fetch(`/api/search?q=${query}`)
      .then(res => res.json())
      .then(data => setResults(data)); // ‚Üê could be an OLD response!
  }, [query]);
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Fix 1: Ignore Flag (Simplest, Recommended)

```jsx
// ‚úÖ GOOD: ignore flag pattern
function SearchGood() {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('');
  const [results, setResults] = useState([]);
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY this variable: it's a "flag" scoped to THIS specific effect run.
    // Each time the effect re-runs (query changes), a fresh `ignore = false` is created.
    let ignore = false;

    const fetchData = async () => {
      setLoading(true);
      try {
        const res  = await fetch(`/api/search?q=${encodeURIComponent(query)}`);
        // WHY encodeURIComponent: prevents injection of special chars into URL
        const data = await res.json();

        // WHY this check: if `ignore` was flipped to true (cleanup ran),
        // this effect is "stale" ‚Äî a newer effect already started.
        // We skip setting state to avoid overwriting fresher data.
        if (!ignore) {
          setResults(data);
          setLoading(false);
        }
      } catch (err) {
        if (!ignore) {
          // WHY same guard here: error handling for stale effects should also be ignored
          console.error(err);
          setLoading(false);
        }
      }
    };

    if (query) fetchData();

    // WHY return a cleanup function:
    // React calls this cleanup when:
    //   1. `query` changes (before re-running the effect)
    //   2. Component unmounts
    // Flipping `ignore = true` tells any pending async work to stand down.
    return () => {
      ignore = true;
    };
  }, [query]); // ‚Üê re-run only when query changes

  return (
    <ul>{results.map(r => <li key={r.id}>{r.name}</li>)}</ul>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step:**
1. User types `"re"` ‚Üí effect runs, `ignore = false`, fetch starts
2. User types `"react"` ‚Üí React calls cleanup of previous effect ‚Üí `ignore = true` for `"re"` fetch
3. New effect runs for `"react"`, its own `ignore = false`, its own fetch starts
4. `"re"` fetch eventually resolves ‚Üí checks `if (!ignore)` ‚Üí `ignore` is `true` ‚Üí **state NOT set**
5. `"react"` fetch resolves ‚Üí checks `if (!ignore)` ‚Üí `ignore` is `false` ‚Üí **state IS set** ‚úÖ

---

#### Code ‚Äî Fix 2: AbortController (Cancels the Network Request Itself)

```jsx
// ‚úÖ BETTER for large responses: actually cancels the HTTP request
function SearchAbort() {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('');
  const [results, setResults] = useState([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY AbortController: instead of just ignoring the response,
    // we cancel the actual in-flight HTTP request ‚Äî saves bandwidth!
    const controller = new AbortController();

    const fetchData = async () => {
      try {
        const res = await fetch(`/api/search?q=${encodeURIComponent(query)}`, {
          signal: controller.signal,  // ‚Üê link fetch to this controller
        });
        const data = await res.json();
        setResults(data);
      } catch (err) {
        // WHY check AbortError: when we abort, fetch throws an error.
        // We only want to log REAL errors, not intentional aborts.
        if (err.name !== 'AbortError') {
          console.error('Fetch failed:', err);
        }
      }
    };

    if (query) fetchData();

    return () => {
      // WHY abort in cleanup: when query changes, this runs BEFORE the
      // next effect. It cancels the in-flight request immediately.
      controller.abort();
    };
  }, [query]);

  return <ul>{results.map(r => <li key={r.id}>{r.name}</li>)}</ul>;
}
```

---

#### Comparison: Ignore Flag vs AbortController

```
                  ignore flag          AbortController
                  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ       ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Network request   Still completes      Cancelled (saves bandwidth)
Complexity        Simple               Slightly more (catch AbortError)
Browser support   Universal            All modern browsers
Best for          Small payloads       Large payloads, file downloads
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Aspect | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Ignore flag check | O(1) | Boolean check per async resolution |
| Cleanup execution | O(1) | Just flips a boolean / calls abort() |
| In-flight requests | O(N) calls simultaneously | N = how fast user triggers re-renders before any resolve |
| Memory per effect | O(1) | Just 1 boolean or 1 AbortController ref per effect run |

---

### Q4. What is the difference between `useRef` for DOM access vs storing mutable values?

---

#### ELI5

> `useRef` gives you a **special box** (`{ current: ... }`) that React never loses between renders.
>
> - **DOM access:** You hand the box to a `<div ref={myRef}>` and React fills it in with the real HTML element ‚Äî so you can call `.focus()`, `.scrollIntoView()`, measure size, etc.
>
> - **Mutable value storage:** You use it like a notebook that survives between renders but writing in it does **NOT** cause a re-render. Unlike state, React doesn't watch this notebook. Great for timers, interval IDs, previous values, and flags.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Two Use Cases

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                   useRef: Two Distinct Jobs                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê    ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  USE CASE 1: DOM Access  ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  USE CASE 2: Mutable Storage     ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ                          ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ                                  ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  const ref = useRef(null)‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  const timerRef = useRef(null)   ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  <input ref={ref} />     ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ                                  ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ                          ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  timerRef.current = setInterval()‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  After mount:            ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ                                  ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ref.current = <input>   ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  clearInterval(timerRef.current) ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  (the real DOM node)     ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ                                  ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ                          ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  ‚úÖ Persists across renders       ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ref.current.focus() ‚úÖ ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  ‚úÖ Change does NOT re-render    ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ref.current.value   ‚úÖ ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  ‚úÖ Not tracked by React         ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Both share: { current: ... } object that React preserves forever   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Both differ from state: updating .current never triggers re-render  ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

Comparison:
                    useState        useRef
                    ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ       ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Re-renders on     YES ‚úÖ          NO ‚ùå
  change?
  Persists across   YES ‚úÖ          YES ‚úÖ
  renders?
  Accessible via    value           ref.current
  Typical use       UI state        DOM / timers / flags / prev-values
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Use Case 1: DOM Access

```jsx
import { useRef, useEffect } from 'react';

function AutoFocusInput() {
  // WHY useRef(null): null is the safe initial value because
  // the DOM element doesn't exist yet when this line first runs.
  // React will fill `.current` once the DOM is mounted.
  const inputRef = useRef(null);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY inside useEffect: DOM is only available AFTER mount.
    // If we tried ref.current.focus() during render, `.current` is still null.
    inputRef.current.focus();
    //               ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ .focus() is a native DOM method, not React
  }, []); // ‚Üê [] = run once on mount, exactly when DOM is ready

  return <input ref={inputRef} placeholder="I auto-focus!" />;
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Real Use: Uncontrolled Input (read value without re-rendering) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function UncontrolledForm() {
  // WHY uncontrolled: we don't need React to re-render on every keystroke.
  // We only need the value at submit time. useRef is perfect for this.
  const usernameRef = useRef(null);

  const handleSubmit = (e) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    // WHY .value: inputRef.current is the DOM <input> element,
    // and .value is the native property holding the current text.
    console.log('Submitted:', usernameRef.current.value);
  };

  return (
    <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
      <input ref={usernameRef} type="text" />
      <button type="submit">Submit</button>
    </form>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step (AutoFocusInput):**
1. `useRef(null)` ‚Üí React creates `{ current: null }` and stores it in fiber
2. React renders `<input>` to the DOM
3. React sees `ref={inputRef}` ‚Üí sets `inputRef.current = <the real input DOM node>`
4. `useEffect` fires ‚Üí `inputRef.current` is now the real `<input>` ‚Üí `.focus()` works ‚úÖ
5. On next re-renders: `inputRef.current` always points to that same DOM node (stable reference)

---

#### Code ‚Äî Use Case 2: Storing Mutable Values (Interval Timer)

```jsx
import { useState, useRef, useEffect } from 'react';

function StopWatch() {
  const [seconds, setSeconds]  = useState(0);
  const [running, setRunning]  = useState(false);

  // WHY useRef for intervalId (not useState):
  // We don't NEED React to re-render when the interval ID changes.
  // The interval ID is implementation detail ‚Äî it's just a number we
  // need to pass to clearInterval() later. Storing in state would
  // cause a useless re-render every time we start/stop.
  const intervalRef = useRef(null);

  const start = () => {
    if (running) return; // guard: don't create 2 intervals
    setRunning(true);

    // WHY store return value of setInterval in .current:
    // setInterval returns a numeric ID we MUST keep to cancel it later.
    // ref.current is the perfect place: persistent, mutable, no re-render.
    intervalRef.current = setInterval(() => {
      setSeconds(s => s + 1); // ‚Üê functional update: safe even inside setInterval
      // WHY functional form `s => s + 1` instead of `seconds + 1`:
      // setInterval captures `seconds` at creation time (stale closure).
      // Functional form always receives the LATEST state value from React.
    }, 1000);
  };

  const stop = () => {
    setRunning(false);
    // WHY clearInterval here: we MUST cancel the interval or it keeps
    // firing forever even after component unmounts ‚Üí memory leak!
    clearInterval(intervalRef.current);
    intervalRef.current = null; // ‚Üê clean up, prevents double-clear bugs
  };

  // WHY this cleanup useEffect: if the component unmounts while running,
  // we still need to clear the interval to avoid memory leaks.
  useEffect(() => {
    return () => clearInterval(intervalRef.current);
  }, []);

  return (
    <div>
      <p>{seconds}s</p>
      <button onClick={start}>Start</button>
      <button onClick={stop}>Stop</button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Use Case 2b: Tracking Previous Value

```jsx
import { useEffect, useRef } from 'react';

// WHY this pattern: sometimes you need to compare current vs previous value
// (e.g., animate only when value increases, not on first render).
function usePreviousValue(value) {
  // WHY useRef(undefined): starts as undefined, only updates AFTER current render
  const prevRef = useRef();

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY inside useEffect: this runs AFTER render.
    // So during THIS render, prevRef.current still holds the PREVIOUS value.
    // Perfect for comparison inside the component body.
    prevRef.current = value;
  });
  // WHY no dep array: runs after every render ‚Äî always tracks the last value

  return prevRef.current; // returns value from the PREVIOUS render
}

function PriceTracker({ price }) {
  const prevPrice = usePreviousValue(price);
  // During render: prevPrice = previous render's price, price = current price
  const direction = price > prevPrice ? '‚Üë' : price < prevPrice ? '‚Üì' : '‚Äì';
  return <p>{price} {direction}</p>;
}
```

---

#### Key Gotchas

```
Gotcha 1: Reading ref.current during render is unsafe
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  During rendering, ref.current may not yet be set (or may be stale).
  Always read ref.current inside useEffect or event handlers, not render body.

Gotcha 2: Changing ref.current does NOT trigger re-render
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  This is by design. If you need the UI to update, use useState instead.
  Ref = "invisible to React's update system".

Gotcha 3: Don't use refs as a workaround for missing dependencies
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  const countRef = useRef(count);
  useEffect(() => { ... countRef.current ... }, []); // ‚Üê anti-pattern
  This hides a stale-closure bug. Better to list the dep correctly.
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| `useRef()` creation | O(1) | Allocates a tiny `{ current }` object once |
| Reading `ref.current` | O(1) | Direct property access |
| Writing `ref.current` | O(1) | Direct property mutation, no React overhead |
| DOM operations via ref | Depends on DOM operation | `.focus()` = O(1), layout reads = browser cost |

---

### Q5. Why does `useContext` cause performance issues and how do you fix it?

---

#### ELI5

> Imagine a school announcement system. A teacher makes **one** announcement to the whole school ‚Äî and **every single student** stops what they are doing and listens, even if the message was only meant for Grade 5.
>
> `useContext` works the same way. When the context value changes, **every component that calls `useContext(MyContext)`** re-renders ‚Äî even if the specific data it cares about didn't change. This is the performance problem.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî The Problem

```
Context value: { user: { name }, theme }
                        ‚îÇ
           ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
           ‚îÇ                           ‚îÇ
    ThemeButton                   UserProfile
    useContext(AppCtx)            useContext(AppCtx)
    reads: theme                  reads: user.name
           ‚îÇ                           ‚îÇ
           ‚îÇ  user.name changes        ‚îÇ
           ‚îÇ  (theme unchanged)        ‚îÇ
           ‚ñº                           ‚ñº
    RE-RENDERS ‚ùå                 RE-RENDERS ‚úÖ
    (doesn't care about           (actually needed)
     user.name but re-renders
     anyway!)

WHY: Context compares values with Object.is().
     If the provider re-renders with a new object reference,
     ALL consumers re-render regardless of which field changed.
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî The Problem in Action

```jsx
import { createContext, useContext, useState } from 'react';

const AppContext = createContext(null);

function AppProvider({ children }) {
  const [user, setUser]   = useState({ name: 'Alice' });
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState('dark');

  // ‚ùå WHY this causes over-rendering:
  // Every render of AppProvider creates a NEW object `{ user, theme, setUser, setTheme }`.
  // Object.is(newObj, oldObj) = false (different references) ‚Üí ALL consumers re-render.
  return (
    <AppContext.Provider value={{ user, theme, setUser, setTheme }}>
      {children}
    </AppContext.Provider>
  );
}

// This component only cares about `theme`, but will ALSO re-render when `user` changes!
function ThemeButton() {
  const { theme } = useContext(AppContext); // ‚Üê reads ALL of AppContext
  console.log('ThemeButton rendered'); // fires even when user.name changes
  return <button style={{ background: theme === 'dark' ? '#333' : '#fff' }}>Click</button>;
}
```

---

#### Fix 1: Split Contexts (Best Solution)

```jsx
// WHY split: each context only notifies its own consumers.
// theme change ‚Üí only ThemeButton re-renders.
// user change  ‚Üí only UserProfile re-renders.

const UserContext  = createContext(null);
const ThemeContext = createContext(null);

function AppProvider({ children }) {
  const [user, setUser]   = useState({ name: 'Alice' });
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState('dark');

  return (
    // WHY nest providers: each provides its own isolated value.
    // React evaluates them independently.
    <UserContext.Provider value={{ user, setUser }}>
      <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme }}>
        {children}
      </ThemeContext.Provider>
    </UserContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚úÖ Now ThemeButton ONLY re-renders when theme changes
function ThemeButton() {
  const { theme } = useContext(ThemeContext); // ‚Üê scoped to theme only
  return <button>Theme: {theme}</button>;
}

// ‚úÖ UserProfile ONLY re-renders when user changes
function UserProfile() {
  const { user } = useContext(UserContext);   // ‚Üê scoped to user only
  return <p>{user.name}</p>;
}
```

---

#### Fix 2: `useMemo` on Context Value (When You Can't Split)

```jsx
import { createContext, useContext, useState, useMemo } from 'react';

const AppContext = createContext(null);

function AppProvider({ children }) {
  const [user, setUser]   = useState({ name: 'Alice' });
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState('dark');

  // WHY useMemo here: memoize the context value object.
  // The object reference only changes when user OR theme actually changes.
  // If AppProvider re-renders for some OTHER reason, consumers won't re-render.
  // WARNING: this does NOT prevent re-renders when user or theme changes ‚Äî
  //           it only prevents re-renders caused by unrelated parent re-renders.
  const value = useMemo(
    () => ({ user, theme, setUser, setTheme }),
    [user, theme]  // ‚Üê only create new object when these change
  );

  return (
    <AppContext.Provider value={value}>
      {children}
    </AppContext.Provider>
  );
}
```

---

#### Fix 3: `React.memo` on Consumer Components

```jsx
import { memo, useContext } from 'react';

// WHY memo: even if context re-renders the parent tree,
// memo prevents re-render if the component's OWN props haven't changed.
// But note: useContext bypass memo ‚Äî if the context value changes, memo can't stop it.
// Memo + split context together is the gold standard.
const ThemeButton = memo(function ThemeButton() {
  const { theme } = useContext(ThemeContext);
  return <button>Theme: {theme}</button>;
});
```

---

#### Fix 4: Use a State Management Library (Zustand / Jotai)

```jsx
// WHY Zustand: its subscriptions are selector-based.
// Components only re-render when the SPECIFIC slice they subscribed to changes.
import { create } from 'zustand';

const useStore = create((set) => ({
  user:     { name: 'Alice' },
  theme:    'dark',
  setTheme: (t) => set({ theme: t }),
}));

// ‚úÖ Only re-renders when `theme` changes ‚Äî user changes are ignored
function ThemeButton() {
  const theme = useStore(state => state.theme); // ‚Üê selector = precise subscription
  return <button>Theme: {theme}</button>;
}
```

---

#### Decision Flowchart ‚Äî Which Fix to Use?

```
Context causing perf issues?
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
Is the context mixing unrelated data?   ‚îÄ‚îÄYES‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∫  Split into separate contexts
         ‚îÇ
        NO
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
Is the parent re-rendering unnecessarily? ‚îÄ‚îÄYES‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∫ useMemo on context value
         ‚îÇ
        NO
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
Is the state complex with many slices? ‚îÄ‚îÄYES‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∫ Migrate to Zustand / Jotai
         ‚îÇ
        NO
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
Wrap consumers in React.memo as a targeted fix
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Scenario | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Context value comparison | O(1) | `Object.is()` ‚Äî reference equality check |
| Notifying consumers on change | O(N) | N = number of components subscribed to that context |
| `useMemo` on context value | O(D) | D = number of deps compared (usually 1-2) |
| Split context approach | O(N/K) per context | N consumers split across K contexts |
| Zustand selector subscription | O(1) per component | Uses pub/sub with per-selector equality checks |

---

### Q6. What is stale closure in React hooks? Give a real example.

---

#### ELI5

> Imagine you take a **photograph** of a whiteboard that says "score = 0". You put the photo in your pocket.
>
> Later, someone updates the whiteboard to say "score = 5". But when you look at your **photo**, it still says "score = 0". Your photo is **stale** ‚Äî it captured the value at a specific moment and never updated.
>
> A stale closure is a function that **captured** a variable from an outer scope at creation time, and now that variable has changed ‚Äî but the function is still using the **old** captured value, not the new one.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî How Stale Closures form

```
Render 1:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  count = 0
  const handleClick = () => console.log(count); // ‚Üê closes over count=0
  setTimeout(handleClick, 3000); // ‚Üê schedules the RENDER-1 version

Render 2 (count changes to 5):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  count = 5                            ‚Üê React re-renders, new count=5
  const handleClick = () => console.log(count); // ‚Üê NEW closure, count=5
  // but the OLD setTimeout still has the RENDER-1 handleClick!

3 seconds later:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Render-1's handleClick fires ‚Üí logs 0 ‚Üê STALE! Not 5!

WHY: The old setTimeout callback holds a reference to the OLD closure.
     JavaScript doesn't update captured variables retroactively.
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Classic Stale Closure Bug

```jsx
import { useState, useEffect } from 'react';

function BuggyCounter() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY this is buggy: this effect runs ONCE (empty []).
    // The closure captures `count = 0` at mount time.
    // Even as count increases, this interval always sees count=0.
    const intervalId = setInterval(() => {
      console.log('Current count:', count); // ‚Üê ALWAYS logs 0! Stale closure!
      // If we tried: setCount(count + 1), it would ALWAYS set to 0+1=1
      // because `count` is forever 0 in this closure.
    }, 1000);

    return () => clearInterval(intervalId);
  }, []); // ‚Üê empty dep array = closure captures initial values only

  return (
    <div>
      <p>{count}</p>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>+</button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Fix 1: Add the Dependency (Correct Deps Array)

```jsx
function FixedByDeps() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  useEffect(() => {
    const intervalId = setInterval(() => {
      // WHY this now works: each time count changes, the OLD effect cleans up,
      // a NEW effect runs, and the new closure captures the LATEST count.
      console.log('Current count:', count); // ‚Üê always fresh!
    }, 1000);

    return () => clearInterval(intervalId); // ‚Üê cleans up old interval
  }, [count]); // ‚Üê NOW count is in deps; effect re-runs when count changes

  return (
    <div>
      <p>{count}</p>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>+</button>
    </div>
  );
  // Trade-off: interval restarts on every count change.
  // For an interval that must NEVER restart, use the ref approach below.
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Fix 2: Functional Updater (For setState)

```jsx
// WHY functional updater: React passes the LATEST state value as argument.
// This bypasses the closure entirely ‚Äî you don't NEED to read `count`.
function FixedByFunctionalUpdate() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  useEffect(() => {
    const intervalId = setInterval(() => {
      // ‚úÖ `c` is ALWAYS the latest count ‚Äî React provides it fresh every call
      // We never "capture" count; we let React hand it to us at call time.
      setCount(c => c + 1); // ‚Üê works correctly even with [] deps!
    }, 1000);

    return () => clearInterval(intervalId);
  }, []); // ‚Üê safe with empty deps because we don't READ count

  return <p>{count}</p>;
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Fix 3: useRef to Hold Latest Value (General Pattern)

```jsx
import { useState, useEffect, useRef } from 'react';

// WHY this pattern: when you need to READ a value inside a long-lived
// callback (setTimeout, socket listener, etc.) AND keep the callback stable.
function FixedByRef() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  // WHY useRef: ref.current is NOT captured at closure time.
  // It's a mutable object; reading ref.current always gives the current value.
  const countRef = useRef(count);

  // WHY this effect: keeps the ref in sync with state on every render.
  // This runs after every render, so countRef.current is always fresh.
  useEffect(() => {
    countRef.current = count;
  });

  useEffect(() => {
    const intervalId = setInterval(() => {
      // ‚úÖ Reading .current = always the LATEST value, no stale closure!
      // The ref object reference is stable; only .current changes.
      console.log('Current count:', countRef.current);
    }, 1000);

    return () => clearInterval(intervalId);
  }, []); // ‚Üê safe: we read countRef.current, not count

  return (
    <div>
      <p>{count}</p>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>+</button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step (Fix 3):**
1. Mount: `countRef.current = 0`, interval created, closure captures `countRef` object (stable reference)
2. User clicks: `count ‚Üí 1`, component re-renders
3. Sync effect fires: `countRef.current = 1` (ref updated to latest)
4. Interval fires: reads `countRef.current` ‚Üí gets `1` ‚úÖ ‚Äî no stale value!

---

#### Real Production Example ‚Äî Event Listener + Stale Closure

```jsx
// Real stale closure bug: "why does my modal close at the wrong count?"
function Modal({ onClose }) {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  useEffect(() => {
    const handleKeyDown = (e) => {
      if (e.key === 'Escape') {
        // BUG: count is captured from the render when this effect ran.
        // If count changes, this handler still sees the OLD count.
        console.log('Closing at count:', count); // might be stale!
        onClose();
      }
    };

    window.addEventListener('keydown', handleKeyDown);
    return () => window.removeEventListener('keydown', handleKeyDown);
  }, []); // ‚Üê only runs once; count is stale after first render!
  
  // FIX: add count to deps, OR use a ref, OR use useCallback with deps
}
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Aspect | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Closure creation | O(1) | JS engine captures variable references at function creation |
| Ref-based stale fix | O(1) per read | Direct `.current` property access |
| Dep-array fix | O(D) per re-run check | D = number of deps compared by React |
| Memory per stale closure | O(variables captured) | Each closure in memory retains refs to all captured vars |

---

### Q7. How does React 18 batch state updates differently from React 17?

---

#### ELI5

> **Batching** = React waits until you finish all your "set state" calls at once, then does a SINGLE re-render instead of many.
>
> **React 17:** The waiter only groups your orders if you're sitting at the restaurant table (inside React event handlers). If you phone in, walk up to the counter, or send a carrier pigeon (setTimeout, Promises, native events), he processes each order one at a time.
>
> **React 18:** The waiter **always** batches every order together, no matter HOW it arrives ‚Äî table, phone, carrier pigeon, all of it. This is called **Automatic Batching**.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî React 17 vs React 18

```
REACT 17 ‚Äî Manual Batching:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  Inside React event handler (onClick, onChange...):      ‚îÇ
    setA(1)   ‚îÄ‚îê                                          ‚îÇ
    setB(2)   ‚îÄ‚î§‚îÄ‚îÄ batched ‚úÖ  ‚Üí 1 re-render              ‚îÇ
    setC(3)   ‚îÄ‚îò                                          ‚îÇ
                                                          ‚îÇ
  Inside setTimeout / Promise / native event:             ‚îÇ
    setA(1) ‚Üí re-render #1 ‚ùå                             ‚îÇ
    setB(2) ‚Üí re-render #2 ‚ùå   3 separate re-renders!    ‚îÇ
    setC(3) ‚Üí re-render #3 ‚ùå                             ‚îÇ
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ--‚îò

REACT 18 ‚Äî Automatic Batching:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  Inside React event handler:                             ‚îÇ
    setA(1)   ‚îÄ‚îê                                          ‚îÇ
    setB(2)   ‚îÄ‚î§‚îÄ‚îÄ batched ‚úÖ  ‚Üí 1 re-render              ‚îÇ
    setC(3)   ‚îÄ‚îò                                          ‚îÇ
                                                          ‚îÇ
  Inside setTimeout / Promise / native event:             ‚îÇ
    setA(1)   ‚îÄ‚îê                                          ‚îÇ
    setB(2)   ‚îÄ‚î§‚îÄ‚îÄ ALSO batched ‚úÖ  ‚Üí 1 re-render üéâ       ‚îÇ
    setC(3)   ‚îÄ‚îò                                          ‚îÇ
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî React 17 Behavior (3 re-renders in async)

```jsx
// React 17 ‚Äî async context triggers 3 separate re-renders
function React17Problem() {
  const [a, setA] = useState(0);
  const [b, setB] = useState(0);
  const [c, setC] = useState(0);

  const handleClick = () => {
    // ‚úÖ INSIDE onClick ‚Äî React 17 batches these: 1 re-render
    setA(1);
    setB(2);
    setC(3);
  };

  const handleAsyncClick = () => {
    fetch('/api/data').then(() => {
      // ‚ùå INSIDE Promise.then ‚Äî React 17 does NOT batch: 3 re-renders
      // WHY: React 17's batching only works by wrapping in ReactDOM.unstable_batchedUpdates()
      //      for async contexts. Promises take execution outside React's event loop wrapper.
      setA(1); // re-render 1
      setB(2); // re-render 2
      setC(3); // re-render 3
    });
  };
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî React 18 Behavior (Always 1 re-render)

```jsx
// React 18 ‚Äî automatic batching works EVERYWHERE
// Requires: ReactDOM.createRoot() in your index.js (not ReactDOM.render())

// index.js ‚Äî MUST use createRoot for React 18 features
import { createRoot } from 'react-dom/client';
const root = createRoot(document.getElementById('root'));
// WHY createRoot: it opts your app into React 18's concurrent features,
// including automatic batching outside React event handlers.
root.render(<App />);

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ In any component ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

function React18Component() {
  const [a, setA] = useState(0);
  const [b, setB] = useState(0);
  const [c, setC] = useState(0);

  const handleAsyncClick = async () => {
    const data = await fetch('/api/data');
    // ‚úÖ React 18: ALL THREE are batched ‚Üí only 1 re-render! üéâ
    setA(1);
    setB(2);
    setC(3);
    // WHY: React 18 uses a scheduler that accumulates all synchronous
    // state updates within the same "microtask" and flushes them together.
  };

  const handleTimeout = () => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      // ‚úÖ React 18: also batched ‚Üí 1 re-render!
      setA(1);
      setB(2);
      setC(3);
    }, 1000);
  };

  const handleNativeEvent = () => {
    // Subscribe to a native DOM event (not a React synthetic event)
    document.addEventListener('click', () => {
      // ‚úÖ React 18: also batched!
      setA(1);
      setB(2);
    }, { once: true });
  };
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Opt Out of Batching (`flushSync`)

```jsx
import { flushSync } from 'react-dom';

// WHY you'd want to opt out:
// If you need a DOM measurement AFTER a specific state update
// but BEFORE other state updates apply ‚Äî you force an immediate flush.
function Example() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);
  const [flag, setFlag]   = useState(false);

  const handleClick = () => {
    // WHY flushSync: forces React to flush this update IMMEDIATELY
    // and synchronously re-render before continuing.
    flushSync(() => {
      setCount(c => c + 1); // ‚Üê React re-renders RIGHT NOW
    });
    // DOM is updated here ‚Äî you can measure layout:
    const el = document.getElementById('counter');
    console.log(el.getBoundingClientRect()); // ‚Üê reads updated DOM

    // This runs in the NEXT batch (after the flushSync completes)
    setFlag(true);
  };
}
```

---

#### Key Differences Summary

```
Feature                  React 17            React 18
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ   ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Batching in onClick      ‚úÖ yes              ‚úÖ yes
Batching in setTimeout   ‚ùå no               ‚úÖ yes (automatic)
Batching in Promises     ‚ùå no               ‚úÖ yes (automatic)
Batching in native events‚ùå no               ‚úÖ yes (automatic)
Opt out                  N/A                 flushSync()
Requires                 ReactDOM.render()   ReactDOM.createRoot()
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Scenario | React 17 | React 18 |
|---|---|---|
| 3 setState in async | 3 renders ‚Üí O(3√órenderCost) | 1 render ‚Üí O(1√órenderCost) |
| Diffing work | O(tree size √ó renders) | O(tree size √ó 1) |
| Memory (state queue) | O(N updates) | O(N updates, batched flush) |
| `flushSync` overhead | N/A | O(1 forced flush) |

---

### Q8. What is `useTransition` and when would you use it over `useState`?

---

#### ELI5

> Imagine you're at a post office. There are two lines:
> - **Urgent line** (passport renewal, time-sensitive)
> - **Non-urgent line** (change of address, can wait)
>
> `useTransition` lets you tell React: *"These state updates are non-urgent ‚Äî put them in the slow lane. Keep the UI responsive for urgent things first."*
>
> Regular `useState` treats ALL updates equally ‚Äî every update blocks the screen until it's done. `useTransition` lets React **pause and resume** non-urgent renders if something more important comes in.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Without vs With `useTransition`

```
WITHOUT useTransition (React 17 / plain useState):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types "react"
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  setQuery("react")                  ‚Üê BLOCKS until done
       ‚îÇ
  Expensive render of 10,000 items   ‚Üê UI FREEZES here
  (takes 500ms)
       ‚îÇ                             ‚Üê User can't type during this!
       ‚ñº
  UI updates finally

WITH useTransition:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types "react"
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  setQuery("react")                  ‚Üê Immediate, urgent ‚úÖ
       ‚îÇ                               (input stays responsive)
       ‚ñº
  startTransition(() => {
    setFilteredList(newItems)        ‚Üê Non-urgent, deferred
  })
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User types next char?
       ‚îÇ    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ React INTERRUPTS the transition render ‚Üí re-starts with new input
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  Transition renders when no urgent work is pending ‚Üí UI updates ‚úÖ
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Problem Without `useTransition`

```jsx
import { useState } from 'react';

// Simulating an expensive list (e.g., rendering 10,000 items)
const ALL_ITEMS = Array.from({ length: 10_000 }, (_, i) => `Item ${i + 1}`);

function SearchListBad() {
  const [query, setQuery]   = useState('');
  const [results, setResults] = useState(ALL_ITEMS);

  const handleChange = (e) => {
    const val = e.target.value;
    setQuery(val); // updates input display

    // ‚ùå WHY this causes jank: this filter runs synchronously during the event.
    // React won't paint the input's new value UNTIL the filter is done.
    // With 10,000 items this takes ~200-500ms ‚Üí input feels laggy!
    const filtered = ALL_ITEMS.filter(item =>
      item.toLowerCase().includes(val.toLowerCase())
    );
    setResults(filtered);
  };

  return (
    <>
      <input value={query} onChange={handleChange} placeholder="Search..." />
      <ul>{results.map(r => <li key={r}>{r}</li>)}</ul>
    </>
  );
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Fixed With `useTransition`

```jsx
import { useState, useTransition } from 'react';

const ALL_ITEMS = Array.from({ length: 10_000 }, (_, i) => `Item ${i + 1}`);

function SearchListGood() {
  const [query,   setQuery]   = useState('');
  const [results, setResults] = useState(ALL_ITEMS);

  // WHY useTransition:
  // `isPending` = true while the transition render is still in progress
  // `startTransition` = the wrapper that marks updates as "non-urgent"
  const [isPending, startTransition] = useTransition();

  const handleChange = (e) => {
    const val = e.target.value;

    // WHY setQuery OUTSIDE startTransition:
    // Updating the input value is URGENT ‚Äî user needs to see what they typed immediately.
    // This gets the highest rendering priority.
    setQuery(val);

    // WHY startTransition here:
    // Filtering 10,000 items is EXPENSIVE but not urgent.
    // React can pause this render mid-way if the user types another character.
    // "Interruptible rendering" = React 18's Concurrent Mode.
    startTransition(() => {
      const filtered = ALL_ITEMS.filter(item =>
        item.toLowerCase().includes(val.toLowerCase())
      );
      setResults(filtered); // ‚Üê deferred, won't block input
    });
  };

  return (
    <>
      <input value={query} onChange={handleChange} placeholder="Search..." />

      {/* WHY show isPending: gives visual feedback that results are loading */}
      {isPending && <p>Updating list...</p>}

      {/* WHY opacity trick: visually indicates stale results while new ones load */}
      <ul style={{ opacity: isPending ? 0.5 : 1 }}>
        {results.map(r => <li key={r}>{r}</li>)}
      </ul>
    </>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step:**
1. User types `"r"` ‚Üí `setQuery("r")` runs at highest priority ‚Üí input updates immediately
2. `startTransition` enqueues `setResults(...)` at low priority
3. React starts rendering the filtered list...
4. User types `"re"` ‚Üí React **interrupts** the low-priority render (throws it away)
5. `setQuery("re")` runs at high priority ‚Üí input updates immediately again
6. New transition enqueued with `"re"` filter ‚Äî React renders it when idle ‚úÖ

---

#### Code ‚Äî `useTransition` for Page Navigation (Next.js / Router)

```jsx
import { useTransition } from 'react';
import { useRouter }     from 'next/router';

function NavButton({ href, children }) {
  const [isPending, startTransition] = useTransition();
  const router = useRouter();

  const handleClick = () => {
    startTransition(() => {
      // WHY inside transition: page navigation can be slow.
      // Marking it as non-urgent keeps the current page responsive
      // while the new page's data/components are loading.
      router.push(href);
    });
  };

  return (
    <button onClick={handleClick} disabled={isPending}>
      {isPending ? 'Loading...' : children}
    </button>
  );
}
```

---

#### `useTransition` vs `useState` ‚Äî Decision Guide

```
                  useState                  useTransition
                  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ                  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Priority          All updates equal         Marks updates as LOW priority
Blocking?         Yes ‚Äî blocks paint        No ‚Äî interruptible by urgent updates
isPending         No built-in flag          ‚úÖ isPending flag included
Best for          Urgent UI updates         Expensive, non-urgent state changes
                  (input, toggle, modal)    (large list filter, route change,
                                            tab switch with heavy content)
Requirement       Any React version         React 18+ with createRoot
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Scenario | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| `startTransition` dispatch | O(1) | Enqueues update with low-priority lane |
| Interrupted render (user types) | O(work done so far, discarded) | React stops and discards partial render trees |
| Full transition render | O(component tree √ó filter work) | Same as normal render after all ‚Äî just interruptible |
| `isPending` check | O(1) | Boolean derived from React's scheduler state |

---

### Q9. What is `useDeferredValue` and how does it differ from debouncing?

---

#### ELI5

> Imagine you're watching a painter paint a live portrait of you while you move around.
>
> - **Debouncing** = the painter **refuses to start** until you stand still for 300ms. If you keep moving, he waits. He starts fresh once you stop.
>
> - **`useDeferredValue`** = the painter **always shows you the last completed portrait** while constantly working on the latest one in the background. He never stops; he just shows you finished work until the new one is ready.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Debounce vs `useDeferredValue`

```
DEBOUNCING:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types: r ‚Üí re ‚Üí rea ‚Üí reac ‚Üí react
                ‚Üë    ‚Üë    ‚Üë
        timer resets each time (300ms delay)

  Only fires ONCE after 300ms of silence:
  r   (ignore)
  re  (ignore)
  rea (ignore)
  reac(ignore)
  react ‚Üí FIRES filter after 300ms ‚úÖ

  Problem: 300ms built-in lag even on a fast device.
  Arbitrary constant ‚Äî too short = perf issue, too long = feels slow.

useDeferredValue:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types: r ‚Üí re ‚Üí react
                  ‚Üë
  React renders IMMEDIATELY, but at LOW priority

  Render 1 (urgent):   input shows "react"
  Render 2 (deferred): list re-filters with "react"

  React decides when to do the deferred render based on device speed.
  Fast device  ‚Üí deferred render starts almost immediately
  Slow device  ‚Üí deferred render waits longer, but never blocks input
  
  No arbitrary timer. React adapts to the device automatically. üéâ
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Debounce Approach (for comparison)

```jsx
import { useState, useEffect } from 'react';

function SearchWithDebounce() {
  const [input,         setInput]         = useState('');
  const [debouncedVal,  setDebouncedVal]  = useState('');

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY setTimeout: delays the expensive update by 300ms.
    // If input changes before 300ms, the old timer is cleared and a new one starts.
    const timer = setTimeout(() => {
      setDebouncedVal(input); // ‚Üê only fires after 300ms of no new input
    }, 300);

    return () => clearTimeout(timer); // ‚Üê cleanup: cancel pending timer on each new input
  }, [input]);

  // debouncedVal is used to drive the expensive render
  const filtered = ALL_ITEMS.filter(i =>
    i.toLowerCase().includes(debouncedVal.toLowerCase())
  );

  return (
    <>
      <input value={input} onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)} />
      <ul>{filtered.map(r => <li key={r}>{r}</li>)}</ul>
    </>
  );
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî `useDeferredValue` Approach

```jsx
import { useState, useDeferredValue, memo } from 'react';

const ALL_ITEMS = Array.from({ length: 10_000 }, (_, i) => `Item ${i + 1}`);

// WHY memo here: MemoizedList only re-renders when `query` prop actually changes.
// Combined with useDeferredValue, React renders the list with the PREVIOUS deferred
// value first (stale but fast), then queues a low-priority render with the new value.
const MemoizedList = memo(function ItemList({ query }) {
  // WHY memo: prevents re-renders when the parent renders for urgent reasons
  // (like updating the input), but query (deferred value) hasn't changed yet.
  const filtered = ALL_ITEMS.filter(i =>
    i.toLowerCase().includes(query.toLowerCase())
  );
  return <ul>{filtered.map(r => <li key={r}>{r}</li>)}</ul>;
});

function SearchWithDeferredValue() {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('');

  // WHY useDeferredValue:
  // `deferredQuery` lags behind `query` when the UI is busy.
  // It always holds either the current value (if React has time) or
  // the last "committed" stable value (if React is still working on a render).
  const deferredQuery = useDeferredValue(query);

  // WHY compare query vs deferredQuery:
  // When they differ, it means we're mid-transition ‚Äî results are stale.
  // Visually indicate this so the user knows fresh results are coming.
  const isStale = query !== deferredQuery;

  return (
    <>
      {/* WHY setQuery directly (not deferred): input MUST update immediately */}
      <input
        value={query}
        onChange={e => setQuery(e.target.value)}
        placeholder="Search..."
      />

      {/* WHY wrap in div with opacity: visual feedback of staleness */}
      <div style={{ opacity: isStale ? 0.5 : 1, transition: 'opacity 0.2s' }}>
        {/* WHY pass deferredQuery (not query): the expensive component
            only re-renders with the DEFERRED (possibly lagging) value */}
        <MemoizedList query={deferredQuery} />
      </div>
    </>
  );
}
```

**Step-by-step:**
1. User types `"r"` ‚Üí `query = "r"` ‚Üí urgent render ‚Üí input shows `"r"` immediately
2. `deferredQuery` might still be `""` (React hasn't had time to update it yet)
3. `MemoizedList` renders with `deferredQuery = ""` (old list, stale) ‚Äî shows with 50% opacity
4. React finds idle time ‚Üí defers priority render ‚Üí `deferredQuery = "r"` ‚Üí list re-filters ‚úÖ
5. `query === deferredQuery` ‚Üí opacity goes back to 100%

---

#### Side-by-side Comparison

```
                  debounce              useDeferredValue
                  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ      ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Mechanism         timer-based           React scheduler-based
Delay type        Fixed (e.g. 300ms)    Adaptive (depends on device load)
Shows old value   Only after delay      Immediately (stale-while-revalidate)
Interrupts input? Yes (during delay)    No (input always urgent)
Required React    Any                   React 18+ (Concurrent Mode)
Extra dep?        Custom hook / lib     Built-in hook
Best for          API calls (save network bandwidth)    Expensive in-mem renders
Cancel on change  Yes (clearTimeout)    Yes (React discards deferred render)
```

---

#### When to Use Which

```
Has network call? (API search)
       ‚îÇ
      YES ‚Üí Use DEBOUNCE  (save API calls ‚Äî don't fire on every keystroke)
       ‚îÇ
      NO
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
Expensive in-memory computation? (filter large array, complex chart)
       ‚îÇ
      YES ‚Üí Use useDeferredValue (keep input responsive, adapt to device speed)
       ‚îÇ
      NO ‚Üí Plain useState is fine
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| `useDeferredValue` read | O(1) | Just returns one of two state values |
| Deferred render trigger | O(component subtree) | Re-renders only the deferred subtree |
| Debounce timer setup | O(1) | `setTimeout` + `clearTimeout` |
| Combined with `memo` | O(1) per skipped render | Memo prevents render when deferred val unchanged |
| Staleness check `q !== dq` | O(1) | String equality comparison |

---

### Q10. How do you implement `useDebounce` as a custom hook?

---

#### ELI5

> Imagine you shout at your smart home speaker. Every time you say a word it starts to respond, but you're still talking ‚Äî so it waits. Only when you **pause for a moment** does it actually respond.
>
> `useDebounce` is that "wait for a pause" logic extracted into a reusable hook. Give it a value and a delay ‚Äî it only updates after you stop changing the value for that many milliseconds.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî How useDebounce Works Internally

```
value changes rapidly: "r" ‚Üí "re" ‚Üí "rea" ‚Üí "reac" ‚Üí "react"
                          ‚îÇ     ‚îÇ     ‚îÇ       ‚îÇ
                    timer ‚îÇ     ‚îÇ     ‚îÇ       ‚îÇ reset each time
                    reset ‚îÇ‚óÑ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÇ‚óÑ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÇ‚óÑ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÇ
                          ‚îÇ
                         300ms of silence...
                          ‚îÇ
                          ‚ñº
                  debouncedValue = "react"  ‚úÖ  (only fires once)

Internal state machine:
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ  value = "react", delay = 300                            ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ                                                          ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  useEffect(() => {                                        ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ    const timer = setTimeout(() => {                       ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ      setDebouncedValue(value)  ‚Üê fires after 300ms       ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ    }, delay)                                             ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ                                                          ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ    return () => clearTimeout(timer) ‚Üê canceled if        ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ                                       value changes      ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  }, [value, delay])                                      ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Simple `useDebounce` Implementation

```jsx
import { useState, useEffect } from 'react';

/**
 * useDebounce ‚Äî delays updating a value until changes stop for `delay` ms
 *
 * @param {T}      value  ‚Äî the value to debounce (string, number, object, etc.)
 * @param {number} delay  ‚Äî milliseconds to wait after last change before updating
 * @returns {T}           ‚Äî the debounced (lagging) value
 */
function useDebounce(value, delay = 300) {
  // WHY separate state: we need TWO values simultaneously:
  // 1. `value` ‚Äî always mirrors what parent passes (fresh, changes fast)
  // 2. `debouncedValue` ‚Äî only updates after `delay` ms of no new `value`
  const [debouncedValue, setDebouncedValue] = useState(value);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WHY setTimeout: delay applying the new value.
    // Each time `value` changes, this effect re-runs (due to [value, delay] deps).
    // Before re-running, React calls the cleanup (return below) which CANCELS
    // the previous pending timer. So if value changes before delay expires,
    // the previous setDebouncedValue never fires!
    const timer = setTimeout(() => {
      // WHY functional form not needed here: `value` is a closure capture,
      // but this is fine ‚Äî it's the WHOLE POINT. We WANT the captured value
      // from this specific render. It's not a stale-closure bug here.
      setDebouncedValue(value);
    }, delay);

    // WHY return cleanup: React calls this before the next effect run
    // AND when the component unmounts. Clearing prevents:
    // 1. Stale debounced updates firing after unmount (memory leak)
    // 2. Old timer overwriting a newer one when value changes rapidly
    return () => {
      clearTimeout(timer);
    };
  }, [value, delay]); // ‚Üê re-run when value OR delay changes

  return debouncedValue;
}

export default useDebounce;
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Usage in a Component

```jsx
import { useState } from 'react';
import useDebounce from './useDebounce';

function SearchInput() {
  const [query,   setQuery]   = useState('');
  // WHY 400ms: balances responsiveness vs performance.
  // 200ms = too few skipped renders, doesn't help much
  // 500ms+ = feels sluggish
  const debouncedQuery = useDebounce(query, 400);

  // WHY useEffect with debouncedQuery:
  // Only triggers the API call AFTER the user pauses typing.
  // Without debounce, every keystroke = 1 API call ‚Üí expensive!
  useEffect(() => {
    if (!debouncedQuery) return;
    // WHY guard: skip empty query ‚Äî no point fetching nothing

    fetch(`/api/search?q=${encodeURIComponent(debouncedQuery)}`)
      .then(res => res.json())
      .then(data => console.log(data));
  }, [debouncedQuery]); // ‚Üê only fires after user stops typing

  return (
    <input
      value={query}
      onChange={e => setQuery(e.target.value)}
      placeholder="Search..."
    />
    // query = always in sync with input (immediate)
    // debouncedQuery = only updates after 400ms of silence
  );
}
```

---

#### Code ‚Äî Enhanced Version: `useDebounce` with Callback (Not Just Value)

```jsx
import { useRef, useCallback } from 'react';

/**
 * useDebouncedCallback ‚Äî debounces a FUNCTION instead of a value.
 * Use this when you want to debounce a callback, not a state value.
 *
 * @param {Function} fn    ‚Äî the function to debounce
 * @param {number}   delay ‚Äî milliseconds delay
 * @returns {Function}     ‚Äî debounced version of fn
 */
function useDebouncedCallback(fn, delay = 300) {
  // WHY useRef for timerRef: we need to persist the timer ID across renders
  // without causing re-renders when the timer ID changes.
  const timerRef = useRef(null);

  // WHY useCallback: stabilize the returned function reference.
  // Without it, every render returns a NEW debounced function, which could
  // break child components relying on reference equality (memo, useEffect deps).
  const debouncedFn = useCallback((...args) => {
    // WHY clearTimeout first: cancel any pending invocation before scheduling new one
    clearTimeout(timerRef.current);

    timerRef.current = setTimeout(() => {
      // WHY fn(...args): forward ALL original arguments to the real function
      fn(...args);
    }, delay);
  }, [fn, delay]); // ‚Üê re-creates only if fn or delay changes

  return debouncedFn;
}

// Usage:
function SearchWithCallback() {
  const [results, setResults] = useState([]);

  // WHY this pattern: when you want the handler itself to be debounced,
  // not a state value. Useful for form handlers, resize handlers, etc.
  const handleSearch = useDebouncedCallback(async (val) => {
    const data = await fetch(`/api/search?q=${val}`).then(r => r.json());
    setResults(data);
  }, 400);

  return (
    <input
      onChange={e => handleSearch(e.target.value)}
      placeholder="Search..."
    />
  );
}
```

---

#### Gotchas and Edge Cases

```
Gotcha 1: Changing `delay` at runtime resets the debounce timer
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  const debouncedVal = useDebounce(query, isDev ? 100 : 400);
  // Fine ‚Äî `delay` is a dep, so changing it re-runs the effect correctly.

Gotcha 2: Object/Array `value` always triggers (new reference)
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  const debouncedFilter = useDebounce({ min: 0, max: 100 }, 300);
  // ‚ùå Creates new object every render ‚Üí effect re-runs every render!
  // FIX: pass primitives, or use JSON.stringify() as the dep, or useMemo.

Gotcha 3: Async-safety ‚Äî stale debounced call can overwrite newer state
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  // Combine with ignore flag (Q3) when the debounced fn makes HTTP requests.
  // debounce prevents multiple calls, but you still need ignore/AbortController
  // in case network responds out of order.
```

---

#### Full Production-Ready `useDebounce` with Abort

```jsx
function useDebounceWithAbort(query, delay = 300) {
  const [results,  setResults]  = useState([]);
  const [loading,  setLoading]  = useState(false);
  const debouncedQuery = useDebounce(query, delay); // ‚Üê uses our hook from above

  useEffect(() => {
    if (!debouncedQuery.trim()) {
      setResults([]);
      return;
    }

    let ignore = false;
    const controller = new AbortController();

    setLoading(true);

    fetch(`/api/search?q=${encodeURIComponent(debouncedQuery)}`, {
      signal: controller.signal,
    })
      .then(res => res.json())
      .then(data => { if (!ignore) setResults(data); })
      .catch(err => { if (err.name !== 'AbortError') console.error(err); })
      .finally(() => { if (!ignore) setLoading(false); });

    return () => {
      ignore = true;
      controller.abort(); // ‚Üê cancel request if debouncedQuery changes
    };
  }, [debouncedQuery]);

  return { results, loading };
}
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Timer creation (`setTimeout`) | O(1) | Browser-native, constant time |
| Timer cancellation (`clearTimeout`) | O(1) | Direct timer ID lookup |
| State update when timer fires | O(1) | Single `setState` call |
| Memory per hook instance | O(1) | 1 state value + 1 timer ID ref |
| Network debouncing savings | O(K/N) calls | K = calls that fire, N = total keystrokes |

---

## End of Section: REACT ‚Äî Core Hooks (Q1‚ÄìQ10)

---

## REACT ‚Äî Performance

---

### Q11. When does `React.memo` NOT prevent a re-render even when props look the same?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine you're a bouncer at a club. Your rule is: "Only let in new guests." You check by comparing **ID cards**.
>
> `React.memo` is that bouncer ‚Äî it compares old and new props. If they look the **same**, it blocks the re-render.
>
> BUT ‚Äî if the ID card is a **photocopy** (a new object/function created fresh every render), even though the *content* is the same, the bouncer sees it as a **different card** and lets the re-render through.
>
> The bouncer uses **reference equality** (`===`), not deep equality.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî When React.memo Fails

```
Parent re-renders
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ  React.memo checks: prevProps === nextProps ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SAME reference? ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚Üí ‚úÖ SKIP re-render
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ DIFFERENT reference? ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚Üí ‚ùå RE-RENDER happens
                    ‚îÇ
         Even if the VALUES look identical!
         
CASES WHERE REFERENCE CHANGES EVERY RENDER:
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ  1. Inline objects     ‚Üí <Comp style={{ color: 'red' }} />  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ     ‚Ä¢ New {} created every render = new reference      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  2. Inline functions   ‚Üí <Comp onClick={() => {}} />   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ     ‚Ä¢ New function created every render = new ref      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  3. Inline arrays      ‚Üí <Comp items={[1, 2, 3]} />    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ     ‚Ä¢ New [] created every render = new reference      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  4. Context changes    ‚Üí if component reads context,   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ     context update BYPASSES memo entirely              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                        ‚îÇ
```
