```
‚îÇ  5. Custom comparator wrong ‚Üí if you pass a bad        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ     areEqual() function, it may always return false    ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî 5 Ways React.memo Fails + Fixes

```jsx
import React, { useState, useCallback, useMemo } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ The memoized child ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const Child = React.memo(({ onClick, style, items, data }) => {
  console.log('Child rendered!');
  return <div style={style} onClick={onClick}>{items.length} items</div>;
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 1: Inline function ‚Äî BREAKS memo ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ParentBroken() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>
      {/* ‚ùå New function created every render ‚Üí Child always re-renders */}
      <Child onClick={() => console.log('clicked')} />
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ FIX 1: useCallback stabilises the function reference ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ParentFixed1() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  // ‚úÖ Same reference between renders (no dependencies change)
  const handleClick = useCallback(() => {
    console.log('clicked');
  }, []); // empty dep array = created once, reference never changes

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>
      <Child onClick={handleClick} /> {/* ‚úÖ memo works */}
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 2: Inline object ‚Äî BREAKS memo ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ParentBroken2() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>
      {/* ‚ùå New {} on every render */}
      <Child style={{ color: 'red', fontWeight: 'bold' }} items={[1, 2]} />
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ FIX 2: useMemo stabilises object/array references ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ParentFixed2() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  // ‚úÖ Same object reference unless dependencies change
  const style  = useMemo(() => ({ color: 'red', fontWeight: 'bold' }), []);
  const items  = useMemo(() => [1, 2], []);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>
      <Child style={style} items={items} /> {/* ‚úÖ memo works */}
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 3: Context ‚Äî BYPASSES memo entirely ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const ThemeContext = React.createContext('light');

const ChildWithContext = React.memo(() => {
  const theme = React.useContext(ThemeContext); // ‚Üê reads context
  console.log('ChildWithContext rendered!');
  return <div>{theme}</div>;
  // ‚ùå Even with React.memo ‚Äî ANY context update re-renders this
  // React.memo only blocks prop changes, NOT context changes
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ CASE 4: Custom areEqual returning wrong result ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const ChildCustom = React.memo(
  ({ data }) => <div>{data.value}</div>,
  (prevProps, nextProps) => {
    // This function should return TRUE if props are EQUAL (skip re-render)
    // ‚ùå Common mistake: returning false always = always re-renders
    return false; // BAD: "props are never equal" ‚Üí always re-renders
    // ‚úÖ Correct: return prevProps.data.value === nextProps.data.value
  }
);
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `React.memo(Child)` | Wraps Child; React will shallowly compare props before re-rendering |
| 2 | `onClick={() => {}}` inline | JavaScript creates a **new function object** each render ‚Äî `() => {} !== () => {}` is always `true` |
| 3 | `useCallback(fn, [])` | Memoizes the function; same reference returned on every render as long as deps don't change |
| 4 | `useMemo(() => obj, [])` | Memoizes an object/array; same reference until deps change |
| 5 | `useContext(ctx)` | Context bypasses `React.memo`‚Äî context changes propagate to ALL consumers regardless |
| 6 | `areEqual(prev, next)` | Custom comparator: return `true` = equal = skip render; `false` = different = render |

---

#### The Shallow Comparison Rule

```
React.memo uses Object.is() for each prop:

  Object.is(42, 42)            ‚Üí true  ‚úÖ
  Object.is('hello', 'hello')  ‚Üí true  ‚úÖ
  Object.is({}, {})            ‚Üí false ‚ùå  (different references)
  Object.is([], [])            ‚Üí false ‚ùå  (different references)
  Object.is(fn, fn)            ‚Üí false ‚ùå  (if recreated each render)
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Prop comparison (shallow) | O(P) | P = number of props ‚Äî each checked with `Object.is` |
| Re-render skipped | O(1) | No work done if comparison returns equal |
| `useCallback` memoization | O(1) | Stores one function reference, returns it on reuse |
| `useMemo` memoization | O(1) | Stores one value reference |
| Context propagation | O(C) | C = all consumers ‚Äî cannot be stopped by memo |

---

### Q12. What is the difference between `useMemo` and `useCallback`? Can you implement one using the other?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine you have a magic notebook that remembers answers so you don't have to calculate them again.
>
> **`useMemo`** memorizes a **result** ‚Äî "the answer to 100 √ó 99 is 9900, I'll remember that."
>
> **`useCallback`** memorizes a **recipe (function)** ‚Äî "the recipe for chocolate cake is X, I'll remember that recipe."
>
> The key insight: a function IS a value in JavaScript. So `useCallback(fn, deps)` is literally just `useMemo(() => fn, deps)`. One memoizes values, the other memoizes functions ‚Äî but functions are values, so one is a special case of the other.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî useMemo vs useCallback

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                          useMemo                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Deps change?                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      YES ‚Üí re-run factory fn ‚Üí store & return NEW VALUE        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      NO  ‚Üí return CACHED VALUE (skip factory fn entirely)      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Usage: memoize expensive calculations, derived data, objects  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Returns: the VALUE the factory function produces              ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                        useCallback                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Deps change?                                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      YES ‚Üí create NEW function reference                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      NO  ‚Üí return SAME function reference as before            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Usage: stabilize event handlers passed to memoized components ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Returns: the FUNCTION ITSELF (not its return value)           ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

Key difference visualised:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  useMemo(() => computeValue(), [dep])
           ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^           ‚Üê factory is called, RESULT stored
  
  useCallback(() => doSomething(), [dep])
              ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^        ‚Üê factory NOT called, FUNCTION stored
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  useCallback(fn, deps)
  ‚â°
  useMemo(() => fn, deps)  ‚Üê 100% equivalent!
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Both Hooks + Implementing Each via the Other

```jsx
import React, { useState, useMemo, useCallback } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Sample data ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const products = Array.from({ length: 10_000 }, (_, i) => ({
  id: i,
  name: `Product ${i}`,
  price: Math.random() * 100,
  category: i % 3 === 0 ? 'A' : i % 3 === 1 ? 'B' : 'C',
}));

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ useMemo: memoize an EXPENSIVE CALCULATION ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ProductList({ category, discount }) {
  // ‚ùå Without useMemo: re-filters 10,000 items on EVERY render
  // const filtered = products.filter(p => p.category === category);

  // ‚úÖ With useMemo: only re-filters when `category` changes
  const filtered = useMemo(
    () => products.filter(p => p.category === category),
    [category]                // dep array ‚Äî re-run only if category changes
    // Step 1: React checks ‚Äî did `category` change since last render?
    // Step 2: If NO  ‚Üí return cached `filtered` array (same reference!)
    // Step 3: If YES ‚Üí run the .filter(), cache the new result, return it
  );

  // ‚úÖ useMemo for derived data (avoids new object on every render)
  const stats = useMemo(() => ({
    count: filtered.length,
    avgPrice: filtered.reduce((s, p) => s + p.price, 0) / filtered.length,
  }), [filtered]); // depends on filtered ‚Üí naturally cascades

  return (
    <div>
      <p>{stats.count} products, avg ${stats.avgPrice.toFixed(2)}</p>
      {filtered.map(p => <div key={p.id}>{p.name}</div>)}
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ useCallback: memoize a FUNCTION REFERENCE ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const Row = React.memo(({ product, onDelete }) => {
  console.log(`Row ${product.id} rendered`);
  return (
    <div>
      {product.name}
      <button onClick={() => onDelete(product.id)}>Delete</button>
    </div>
  );
});

function ProductTable() {
  const [items, setItems] = useState(products.slice(0, 20));
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0); // unrelated state

  // ‚ùå Without useCallback: new function every render
  //    ‚Üí onDelete reference changes ‚Üí ALL Row components re-render
  // const onDelete = (id) => setItems(prev => prev.filter(p => p.id !== id));

  // ‚úÖ With useCallback: stable function reference
  //    ‚Üí React.memo on Row can actually work
  const onDelete = useCallback(
    (id) => setItems(prev => prev.filter(p => p.id !== id)),
    [] // setItems from useState is stable ‚Äî no deps needed
    // Step 1: React checks deps [] ‚Äî nothing in deps that changes
    // Step 2: Returns the SAME function reference every render
    // Step 3: Row's React.memo sees same `onDelete` ‚Üí skips re-render
  );

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>
        Unrelated: {count}  {/* clicking this won't re-render Rows */}
      </button>
      {items.map(p => <Row key={p.id} product={p} onDelete={onDelete} />)}
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ IMPLEMENTING useCallback USING useMemo ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// This is how React actually implements useCallback internally!
function myUseCallback(fn, deps) {
  // useMemo stores the factory's return value
  // the factory just returns fn itself (the function, not its result)
  return useMemo(() => fn, deps);
  //             ^^^^^^ factory returns the function
  //                    useMemo stores that function as the "value"
}

// Proof it works:
function Demo() {
  const [x, setX] = useState(0);

  // These two are 100% equivalent:
  const cb1 = useCallback(() => console.log(x), [x]);
  const cb2 = useMemo(() => () => console.log(x), [x]);
  //                  ^^^ outer fn is factory, inner fn is the callback

  return <button onClick={cb1}>Go</button>;
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ WHEN TO USE WHICH ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// useMemo  ‚Üí when you want to memoize a COMPUTED VALUE
//            e.g., filtered list, total price, sorted array
//
// useCallback ‚Üí when you want to memoize a FUNCTION REFERENCE
//               e.g., event handlers passed to memoized children
//
// Rule of thumb:
//   useMemo(() => fn, deps)      = memoize function as a value
//   useMemo(() => fn(), deps)    = memoize function's RETURN value
//   useCallback(fn, deps)        = shorthand for first case
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `useMemo(() => products.filter(...), [category])` | Factory runs expensive filter, result cached. Re-runs only if `category` changes |
| 2 | Dep array `[category]` | React uses `Object.is` to compare old vs new `category` |
| 3 | `useCallback((id) => setItems(...), [])` | Stores the function itself. Empty deps = function reference never recreated |
| 4 | `React.memo` on `Row` | Now that `onDelete` ref is stable, memo's shallow comparison works |
| 5 | `useMemo(() => fn, deps)` | Implementing useCallback: factory returns **the function itself**, not its return value |
| 6 | `useMemo(() => () => console.log(x), [x])` | Double arrow: outer `() =>` is the factory, inner `() =>` is the memoized callback |

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| `useMemo` dep check | O(D) | D = number of dependencies, each compared with `Object.is` |
| `useMemo` factory (skipped) | O(1) | Just a reference return from cache |
| `useMemo` factory (run) | O(N) | N = cost of your computation (e.g., filter of N items) |
| `useCallback` dep check | O(D) | Same dep comparison |
| Memory per `useMemo`/`useCallback` | O(1) | Stores one cached value/reference + dep array |

---

### Q13. How does React's reconciliation algorithm work? What role does the `key` prop play?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine you have a LEGO house and you want to change it. You have two choices:
> 1. **Demolish everything and rebuild** ‚Äî slow, wasteful.
> 2. **Find what changed and only swap those pieces** ‚Äî fast!
>
> React uses option 2. It makes a "before" picture of your UI (the old Virtual DOM) and an "after" picture (the new Virtual DOM), then **diffs them** to find what actually changed, and only updates those real DOM nodes.
>
> The `key` prop is like a **name tag** on each LEGO piece. Without name tags, React has to guess which piece moved. With name tags, it knows exactly which piece is which ‚Äî even if you rearrange them.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Full Reconciliation Pipeline

```
State/Props change
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ  React calls render() / function     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  component ‚Üí produces new            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  React Element tree (Virtual DOM)    ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
                   ‚îÇ
                   ‚ñº
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ         DIFFING (Reconciliation)     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Compare old tree vs new tree        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  using 3 heuristic rules:            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Rule 1: Different element TYPE?     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ   YES ‚Üí destroy old subtree,      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ         mount new subtree         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ   NO  ‚Üí keep DOM node, diff attrs ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Rule 2: Same type, same level?      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ   ‚Üí update only changed props     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Rule 3: Lists ‚Äî use KEY prop        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      KEY exists ‚Üí map by key         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ      No KEY     ‚Üí map by position    ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
                   ‚îÇ
                   ‚ñº
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ  Commit Phase                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Apply minimal DOM mutations to      ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  the real DOM                        ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

KEY PROP IN LISTS (the critical detail):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Without keys (position-based):
OldList: [A, B, C]         ‚Üí keys by position: 0, 1, 2
NewList: [X, A, B, C]      ‚Üí keys by position: 0, 1, 2, 3
Result:  Pos0=A‚ÜíX (update), Pos1=B‚ÜíA (update), Pos2=C‚ÜíB (update), +insert C
         ‚Üí 3 updates + 1 insert  ‚ùå wasteful!

With keys (identity-based):
OldList: [A(key=a), B(key=b), C(key=c)]
NewList: [X(key=x), A(key=a), B(key=b), C(key=c)]
Result:  key=x ‚Üí insert X at position 0
         key=a, b, c ‚Üí just MOVE them, no re-render!  ‚úÖ
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Reconciliation in Practice

```jsx
import React, { useState } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ RULE 1: Changing element type destroys the subtree ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function TypeChangeDemo() {
  const [isDiv, setIsDiv] = useState(true);

  // When you toggle, React sees: div ‚Üí span (different type)
  // ‚Üí It UNMOUNTS the entire div subtree (loses all state inside!)
  // ‚Üí It MOUNTS a fresh span subtree
  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setIsDiv(b => !b)}>Toggle</button>
      {isDiv
        ? <div><input defaultValue="type here" /></div>   // ‚Üê loses value on toggle!
        : <span><input defaultValue="type here" /></span> // ‚Üê fresh mount
      }
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ RULE 3: The KEY prop in lists ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ListWithoutKeys() {
  const [items, setItems] = useState(['Alice', 'Bob', 'Charlie']);

  const addToFront = () => setItems(prev => ['Zara', ...prev]);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={addToFront}>Add Zara to front</button>
      <ul>
        {items.map(name => (
          // ‚ùå No key ‚Äî React uses index
          // When Zara is added at front:
          // index 0 was "Alice" ‚Üí now "Zara" ‚Üí React updates text
          // index 1 was "Bob"   ‚Üí now "Alice" ‚Üí React updates text
          // All 3 existing items re-render unnecessarily!
          <li key={name}> {/* ‚úÖ use stable identity as key */}
            <input placeholder={name} />
            {/* With index key: input value would shift/misalign! */}
          </li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ KEY as a RESET mechanism ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// KEY's superpower: changing the key forces a full remount
// Use this deliberately to reset component state!

function UserProfile({ userId }) {
  const [note, setNote] = useState('');

  // Problem: switching between users keeps the old `note` state
  // because React reuses the same UserProfile instance (same type, same position)
  return (
    <div>
      <p>User: {userId}</p>
      <textarea value={note} onChange={e => setNote(e.target.value)} />
    </div>
  );
}

function App() {
  const [userId, setUserId] = useState(1);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setUserId(2)}>Switch to User 2</button>

      {/* ‚ùå Without key: note state persists when switching users */}
      {/* <UserProfile userId={userId} /> */}

      {/* ‚úÖ With key=userId: React sees key changed ‚Üí unmount + remount
           ‚Üí fresh state for each user automatically! */}
      <UserProfile key={userId} userId={userId} />
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ BAD KEY: using array index ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function BadKeyExample() {
  const [items, setItems] = useState([
    { id: 1, text: 'First' },
    { id: 2, text: 'Second' },
  ]);

  const removeFirst = () => setItems(prev => prev.slice(1));

  return (
    <ul>
      {items.map((item, index) => (
        // ‚ùå key=index: when first item removed, index 0 now points
        //    to "Second" ‚Äî React THINKS it updated item, but actually
        //    the item component still has stale internal state!
        <li key={index}>{item.text} <input /></li>
      ))}

      {/* ‚úÖ key=item.id: React correctly identifies which item
           was removed, unmounts only that one */}
      {/* <li key={item.id}>{item.text} <input /></li> */}
    </ul>
  );
}
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | Virtual DOM diff starts | React compares element type first ‚Äî cheapest check |
| 2 | `div ‚Üí span` | Different type ‚Üí full unmount + remount of subtree ‚Äî state is lost |
| 3 | `key={name}` on list | React uses key as identity for each element in the list |
| 4 | Adding to front without keys | React maps by position: pos 0 now has different text ‚Üí updates each DOM text node |
| 5 | Adding to front with stable keys | React sees key="Zara" is new ‚Üí insert; key="Alice" etc unchanged ‚Üí skip |
| 6 | `key={userId}` on `UserProfile` | Deliberately changing key forces remount ‚Üí cleans up stale state |
| 7 | `key={index}` (bad) | If list reorders/removes, index-based key causes React to reuse wrong component instance |

---

#### The 3 Diffing Rules Summary

```
React's O(n) diffing uses 3 assumptions (heuristics):

1. Elements of different types produce different trees
   ‚Üí If type changes, tear down and rebuild

2. Keys hint at stable identity across renders
   ‚Üí If key is the same, React REUSES the component instance

3. Sibling comparisons only (no cross-level diffing)
   ‚Üí React never compares across different depth levels
   ‚Üí This is what makes diffing O(n) instead of O(n¬≥)
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| React's diffing algorithm | O(n) | n = nodes in tree. Heuristics avoid full O(n¬≥) tree comparison |
| List diff without keys | O(n) updates | May update every node even if only one changed |
| List diff with stable keys | O(k) | k = actual changes (inserts/removes/moves) |
| DOM mutations | O(m) | m = number of actual DOM operations React schedules |
| Virtual DOM memory | O(n) | Keeps two trees in memory: current + work-in-progress |

---

### Q14. What is virtualization? When would you use `@tanstack/react-virtual`?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine a library with 100,000 books. Instead of putting ALL books on the shelves at once, the librarian only puts out the **30 books you can see right now**. As you walk (scroll), she swaps books out ‚Äî removing the ones behind you, adding the ones ahead.
>
> That's **virtualization**: only rendering the items **currently visible** on screen. A list of 100,000 rows becomes a list of ~20 DOM nodes.
>
> `@tanstack/react-virtual` is that super-efficient librarian.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî How Virtualization Works

```
Full DOM (no virtualization):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <ul>
    <li>Item 0</li>      ‚Üê all in DOM
    <li>Item 1</li>
    <li>Item 2</li>
    ...
    <li>Item 9999</li>   ‚Üê 10,000 real DOM nodes!
  </ul>
  ‚Üí Page scroll: SLOW (layout, paint for all 10k nodes)
  ‚Üí Memory: bloated


Virtualized list:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Scroll container (height = 10,000 * rowHeight = fixed)
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Inner container (height = total scroll height)
         ‚îÇ       Acts as a "spacer" to create correct scrollbar
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Only VISIBLE items rendered:
                 <li>Item 15</li>   ‚Üê user scrolled to ~item 15
                 <li>Item 16</li>
                 <li>Item 17</li>
                 ...
                 <li>Item 35</li>   ‚Üê ~20 items visible at once
                 (positioned absolutely using top: offset)


Scroll event flow:
  User scrolls ‚Üí onScroll fires
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  Calculate: scrollTop / rowHeight = first visible index
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  Calculate: first + overscan = range to render
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  React renders ONLY that slice ‚Üí rest are unmounted
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  Items positioned with: transform: translateY(offset)
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî `@tanstack/react-virtual` in Action

```jsx
import React, { useRef } from 'react';
import { useVirtualizer } from '@tanstack/react-virtual';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Sample data: 50,000 rows ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const allItems = Array.from({ length: 50_000 }, (_, i) => ({
  id: i,
  name: `User #${i}`,
  email: `user${i}@example.com`,
}));

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Basic virtualised list ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function VirtualList() {
  // Step 1: ref on the SCROLL CONTAINER (the element that scrolls)
  const parentRef = useRef(null);

  // Step 2: set up the virtualizer
  const virtualizer = useVirtualizer({
    count: allItems.length,           // total number of items
    getScrollElement: () => parentRef.current, // tell it which element scrolls
    estimateSize: () => 50,           // estimated row height in px
    overscan: 5,                      // render 5 extra rows above/below viewport
    // overscan prevents blank flash on fast scroll
  });

  return (
    // Step 3: scroll container has a FIXED height
    <div
      ref={parentRef}
      style={{
        height: '600px',   // viewport height
        overflow: 'auto',  // enables scrolling
      }}
    >
      {/* Step 4: inner div height = TOTAL virtual height
           This is what creates the correct scrollbar length */}
      <div
        style={{
          height: `${virtualizer.getTotalSize()}px`,
          // e.g., 50,000 * 50px = 2,500,000px tall
          // Only ~14 screenfulls actually exist, but scroll FEELS like 50k rows
          position: 'relative',
        }}
      >
        {/* Step 5: render only VIRTUAL ITEMS (the visible slice) */}
        {virtualizer.getVirtualItems().map(virtualItem => (
          <div
            key={virtualItem.key}
            data-index={virtualItem.index}     // needed for dynamic sizing
            ref={virtualizer.measureElement}   // measure actual size (for variable heights)
            style={{
              position: 'absolute',
              top: 0,
              left: 0,
              width: '100%',
              // Step 6: position each item using transform (GPU-accelerated)
              transform: `translateY(${virtualItem.start}px)`,
              // virtualItem.start = this item's pixel offset from top
            }}
          >
            {/* Step 7: render actual content for this index only */}
            <div style={{ padding: '8px', borderBottom: '1px solid #eee' }}>
              <strong>{allItems[virtualItem.index].name}</strong>
              <span>{allItems[virtualItem.index].email}</span>
            </div>
          </div>
        ))}
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Variable height rows ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// When rows have different heights, use measureElement + dynamic sizing
function VariableHeightList() {
  const parentRef = useRef(null);

  const virtualizer = useVirtualizer({
    count: allItems.length,
    getScrollElement: () => parentRef.current,
    estimateSize: () => 60,     // initial estimate; corrected after first render
    overscan: 3,
  });

  return (
    <div ref={parentRef} style={{ height: '500px', overflow: 'auto' }}>
      <div style={{ height: `${virtualizer.getTotalSize()}px`, position: 'relative' }}>
        {virtualizer.getVirtualItems().map(vItem => (
          <div
            key={vItem.key}
            ref={virtualizer.measureElement}  // ‚Üê actual DOM measurement
            data-index={vItem.index}
            style={{
              position: 'absolute',
              top: 0,
              width: '100%',
              transform: `translateY(${vItem.start}px)`,
            }}
          >
            {/* rows with different heights */}
            <p style={{ margin: 0, padding: 8 }}>
              {allItems[vItem.index].name}
              {vItem.index % 5 === 0 && <br />} {/* some rows taller */}
              {vItem.index % 5 === 0 && 'Extra line here'}
            </p>
          </div>
        ))}
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ When to use ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚úÖ Use virtualization when:
//   - List has > 200 items (noticeable perf benefit)
//   - Items are repeated UI (tables, feeds, logs)
//   - Mobile devices (low memory)
//
// ‚ùå Don't virtualize when:
//   - List has < 100 items
//   - Each item is unique/complex layout (hard to measure height)
//   - You need Cmd+F text search to work (virtualized items aren't in DOM)
//   - You need accurate printing
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `useRef(null)` on scroll container | Virtualizer needs to listen to this element's scroll events |
| 2 | `count: allItems.length` | Total items ‚Äî used to calculate total scrollable height |
| 3 | `estimateSize: () => 50` | Approximate row height for initial total height estimation |
| 4 | `overscan: 5` | Renders 5 rows above/below viewport ‚Äî prevents blank rows during fast scroll |
| 5 | `getTotalSize()` on inner div | Makes scrollbar behave as if all 50k rows exist |
| 6 | `getVirtualItems()` | Returns only the ~20 rows currently visible + overscan |
| 7 | `translateY(start)` | Absolutely positions each row at its scroll offset ‚Äî GPU-accelerated |
| 8 | `measureElement` ref | For variable heights: measures actual rendered DOM size and updates offsets |

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| DOM nodes rendered | O(V) | V = visible rows (~20-30), not total count N |
| Scroll recalculation | O(log N) | Binary search to find first visible index from scroll offset |
| Total height calculation | O(N) | Sum all estimated/measured heights once, then cached |
| Memory usage | O(V) | Only V DOM nodes + offset cache for measured items |
| Without virtualization | O(N) | N DOM nodes always in memory ‚Äî O(50,000) for 50k list |

---

### Q15. How does code splitting with `React.lazy()` and `Suspense` work under the hood?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine ordering a pizza. Instead of ordering 10 pizzas when you arrive (slow, expensive), you order only the **one pizza you want right now**. If you decide you want dessert later, you order that then.
>
> Without code splitting: the browser downloads ALL your JavaScript at once ‚Äî even pages the user might never visit.
>
> With code splitting: only the code for the **current page** is downloaded. When the user navigates to a new page, that page's code downloads **on demand**.
>
> `React.lazy()` is the waiter who fetches the right pizza. `Suspense` is the "Please wait..." message shown while the pizza is being prepared.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Code Splitting Under the Hood

```
BUILD TIME (webpack/vite):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  import('./pages/Dashboard')
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  Bundler creates SEPARATE chunk:
    main.js          ‚Üê loads immediately
    dashboard.js     ‚Üê loads ON DEMAND (code split here)
    profile.js       ‚Üê loads ON DEMAND
    settings.js      ‚Üê loads ON DEMAND


RUNTIME (user navigates to Dashboard):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  React.lazy(() => import('./pages/Dashboard'))
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îÇ  First render of <Dashboard />
         ‚ñº
  React: "This is lazy ‚Äî I need to LOAD IT first"
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  React throws a PROMISE (Suspense protocol)
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  Nearest <Suspense> boundary catches the promise
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Renders fallback UI (spinner/skeleton)
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  Promise resolves ‚Üí module loaded
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  React re-renders ‚Üí replaces fallback with real component
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  Component is now in a MODULE CACHE
  ‚Üí subsequent renders: instant (no network call)


The "Throwing a Promise" protocol (how Suspense works):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Component renders
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data ready? ‚Üí Render normally
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Data NOT ready? ‚Üí throw promise
                 ‚îÇ
                 ‚ñº
         Suspense catches the throw
         Shows fallback
         Waits for promise to settle
         Re-renders component
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Full Code Splitting Setup

```jsx
import React, { Suspense, lazy, useState } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 1: Use lazy() to declare code-split components ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// lazy() takes a function that returns a dynamic import()
// The function is NOT called immediately ‚Äî only when component is first needed

const Dashboard  = lazy(() => import('./pages/Dashboard'));
//                           ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
//                           Webpack/Vite sees this dynamic import
//                           and splits it into a separate JS chunk

const Profile    = lazy(() => import('./pages/Profile'));
const Settings   = lazy(() => import('./pages/Settings'));
// Each of these creates its OWN bundle chunk
// None of them download until the user actually navigates there

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 2: Wrap lazy components in Suspense ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function App() {
  const [page, setPage] = useState('dashboard');

  return (
    <div>
      <nav>
        <button onClick={() => setPage('dashboard')}>Dashboard</button>
        <button onClick={() => setPage('profile')}>Profile</button>
        <button onClick={() => setPage('settings')}>Settings</button>
      </nav>

      {/* Step 3: Suspense provides a fallback while chunk loads */}
      <Suspense fallback={<LoadingSpinner />}>
        {page === 'dashboard' && <Dashboard />}
        {page === 'profile'   && <Profile />}
        {page === 'settings'  && <Settings />}
        {/* First time each is rendered: network request fires
            Subsequent renders: instant from cache */}
      </Suspense>
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ With React Router ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { Routes, Route } from 'react-router-dom';

// Lazy-load route components ‚Äî very common pattern
const Home    = lazy(() => import('./routes/Home'));
const About   = lazy(() => import('./routes/About'));
const Contact = lazy(() => import('./routes/Contact'));

function AppRouter() {
  return (
    // Single Suspense wraps all routes
    // Shows fallback whenever a route chunk is loading
    <Suspense fallback={<div>Loading page...</div>}>
      <Routes>
        <Route path="/"        element={<Home />} />
        <Route path="/about"   element={<About />} />
        <Route path="/contact" element={<Contact />} />
      </Routes>
    </Suspense>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Nested Suspense boundaries ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// You can have multiple Suspense boundaries for granular control
const HeavyChart   = lazy(() => import('./components/HeavyChart'));
const DataTable    = lazy(() => import('./components/DataTable'));

function Dashboard() {
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Dashboard</h1>

      {/* Each section has its own fallback ‚Äî they load independently */}
      <Suspense fallback={<div>Loading chart...</div>}>
        <HeavyChart /> {/* chart.js chunk loads independently */}
      </Suspense>

      <Suspense fallback={<div>Loading table...</div>}>
        <DataTable />  {/* table chunk loads independently */}
      </Suspense>
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Preloading chunks (advanced) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Problem: user clicks button ‚Üí waits for download ‚Üí slow feel
// Solution: preload the chunk on HOVER (anticipate user intent)

const AdminPanel = lazy(() => import('./AdminPanel'));

// Trigger the import() on hover ‚Äî chunk starts downloading
// before user actually clicks ‚Üí instant when they do click
const preloadAdminPanel = () => import('./AdminPanel');

function NavBar() {
  return (
    <button
      onMouseEnter={preloadAdminPanel} // preload on hover
      onClick={() => navigate('/admin')}
    >
      Admin
    </button>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ What lazy() wraps must export a DEFAULT export ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// pages/Dashboard.jsx:
export default function Dashboard() { // ‚Üê must be DEFAULT export
  return <h1>Dashboard Page</h1>;
}
// If the module uses named exports only, wrap it:
const NamedComp = lazy(() =>
  import('./NamedExport').then(module => ({ default: module.NamedExport }))
  //                     ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
  //                     Force it to look like a default export
);
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `lazy(() => import('./Page'))` | Factory function defers the `import()` call until component is needed |
| 2 | `import('./Page')` | Dynamic import ‚Äî signals bundler to create a separate JS chunk at build time |
| 3 | Component renders for first time | React detects it's lazy ‚Üí calls the factory ‚Üí `import()` fires ‚Üí network request |
| 4 | Promise thrown | React.lazy throws the pending Promise up to the nearest Suspense boundary |
| 5 | `Suspense` catches the throw | Shows `fallback` while awaiting the Promise |
| 6 | Module downloads + resolves | Suspense re-triggers render ‚Äî now the component exists ‚Üí renders it |
| 7 | Subsequent renders | Module is cached ‚Üí `import()` resolves instantly from module cache |
| 8 | `export default` requirement | `React.lazy` reads `module.default` ‚Äî named exports need manual mapping |

---

#### Bundle Size Impact

```
WITHOUT code splitting:
  main.js  ‚Üí  2.4MB  (entire app in one file)
  
  User visits homepage:
  ‚Üí Downloads 2.4MB even if they only use 10% of the app

WITH code splitting:
  main.js      ‚Üí  350KB  (core + current route)
  dashboard.js ‚Üí  280KB  (lazy)
  profile.js   ‚Üí  95KB   (lazy)
  settings.js  ‚Üí  120KB  (lazy)
  
  User visits homepage:
  ‚Üí Downloads only 350KB immediately ‚úÖ
  ‚Üí dashboard.js downloads only when /dashboard is visited
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Chunk load (first render) | O(1) network | One HTTP request per chunk; browser caches it |
| Chunk load (subsequent) | O(1) | Module registry cache ‚Äî no network; instant |
| `lazy()` factory call | O(1) | Just creates a wrapper object |
| Suspense boundary check | O(1) | React checks up the tree for nearest Suspense |
| Initial bundle size savings | O(N ‚Üí K) | N = full app size; K = only what's needed for current route |

---

### Q16. What causes unnecessary re-renders and how do you diagnose them using React DevTools?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine your whole office stands up every time ANYONE gets an email. That's a terrible office.
>
> Good offices: only the **person who got the email** stands up.
>
> Unnecessary re-renders are your whole office standing up. React DevTools' Profiler is the camera that shows you **who stood up, why, and how often**.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Root Causes of Unnecessary Re-renders

```
TOP CAUSES:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. UNSTABLE REFERENCES
     Parent re-renders
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Creates new {} or [] or () => {} inline
                    ‚îÇ
                    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Child gets "new" prop every time
                              ‚îÇ
                              ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ React.memo can't help
                                  ‚Üí Child always re-renders

  2. CONTEXT OVER-SHARING
     Single large context value changes
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ALL consumers re-render
              even if they only use one tiny slice

  3. STATE TOO HIGH
     State lives in a parent/grandparent
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Every state change re-renders the entire subtree
              not just the component that "owns" the data

  4. MISSING MEMOIZATION
     Expensive derived data re-computed every render
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Component does heavy work unnecessarily

  5. WRONG useEffect DEPS
     useEffect with wrong/missing deps
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Effect re-runs ‚Üí triggers setState ‚Üí triggers re-render
              causing render loops or excessive renders

  6. THIRD-PARTY SUBSCRIPTION TRIGGERS
     Redux / Zustand selector re-renders component
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Selector returns new object {} each time
              even if the DATA inside is the same
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Causes + Fixes

```jsx
import React, { useState, useCallback, useMemo, createContext, useContext, memo } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ CAUSE 1: Inline functions and objects ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const Item = memo(({ onClick, style }) => {
  console.log('Item rendered');
  return <div style={style} onClick={onClick}>Click me</div>;
});

function BadParent() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);
  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>

      {/* ‚ùå New function + new object on EVERY render */}
      <Item
        onClick={() => console.log('clicked')}  // new fn every render
        style={{ color: 'blue' }}               // new obj every render
      />
    </>
  );
}

function GoodParent() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  // ‚úÖ Stable references
  const handleClick = useCallback(() => console.log('clicked'), []);
  const itemStyle   = useMemo(() => ({ color: 'blue' }), []);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Count: {count}</button>
      <Item onClick={handleClick} style={itemStyle} /> {/* ‚úÖ memo works */}
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ CAUSE 2: Context over-sharing ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚ùå BAD: everything in one context ‚Äî any change re-renders ALL consumers
const AppContext = createContext(null);

function BadApp() {
  const [user, setUser]     = useState({ name: 'Alice' });
  const [theme, setTheme]   = useState('light');
  const [cart, setCart]     = useState([]);

  return (
    // One big context ‚Äî cart update ‚Üí UserDisplay re-renders (unnecessarily)
    <AppContext.Provider value={{ user, setUser, theme, setTheme, cart, setCart }}>
      <UserDisplay />
      <ThemeToggle />
      <CartIcon />
    </AppContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚úÖ GOOD: split contexts ‚Äî each consumer only re-renders for its own data
const UserContext  = createContext(null);
const ThemeContext = createContext(null);
const CartContext  = createContext(null);

function GoodApp() {
  const [user, setUser]   = useState({ name: 'Alice' });
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState('light');
  const [cart, setCart]   = useState([]);

  return (
    <UserContext.Provider value={{ user, setUser }}>
      <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme }}>
        <CartContext.Provider value={{ cart, setCart }}>
          {/* Now UserDisplay only re-renders on user changes */}
          <UserDisplay />
          <ThemeToggle />
          <CartIcon />
        </CartContext.Provider>
      </ThemeContext.Provider>
    </UserContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ CAUSE 3: State too high ‚Äî lift down or colocate ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚ùå BAD: modal open state in App ‚Üí whole tree re-renders on open/close
function BadApp2() {
  const [modalOpen, setModalOpen] = useState(false);
  return (
    <div>
      <HeavyDashboard /> {/* ‚Üê re-renders whenever modalOpen changes */}
      <button onClick={() => setModalOpen(true)}>Open</button>
      {modalOpen && <Modal onClose={() => setModalOpen(false)} />}
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚úÖ GOOD: colocate state with the component that owns it
function GoodApp2() {
  return (
    <div>
      <HeavyDashboard /> {/* never re-renders due to modal */}
      <ModalController /> {/* state lives HERE, only this subtree re-renders */}
    </div>
  );
}

function ModalController() {
  const [open, setOpen] = useState(false);
  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setOpen(true)}>Open</button>
      {open && <Modal onClose={() => setOpen(false)} />}
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ DIAGNOSIS: Using React DevTools Profiler ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// No code to write ‚Äî but here's the SEQUENCE:
// 
// 1. Open React DevTools ‚Üí "Profiler" tab
// 2. Click "Record" (circle icon)
// 3. Interact with your app (click buttons, type, etc.)
// 4. Click "Stop"
// 5. See the FLAME GRAPH:
//    - Grey bars = didn't re-render
//    - Coloured bars = DID re-render (darker = slower)
// 6. Click any coloured bar ‚Üí see WHY it re-rendered:
//    "Why did this render?" panel shows:
//    ‚Üí "Props changed: onClick"
//    ‚Üí "State changed"
//    ‚Üí "Context changed"
// 7. Look for components that re-render on EVERY interaction
//    when they shouldn't ‚Üí those are your targets

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ DIAGNOSIS: "Why did you render" library ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// npm install @welldone-software/why-did-you-render
// Add to entry file (development only):
import './wdyr'; // wdyr.js:

// wdyr.js:
import React from 'react';
import whyDidYouRender from '@welldone-software/why-did-you-render';
if (process.env.NODE_ENV === 'development') {
  whyDidYouRender(React, {
    trackAllPureComponents: true,
    // Logs to console: "Re-rendered because props.onClick changed"
    // Shows old vs new value for each changed prop
  });
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ DIAGNOSIS: console.count trick ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function MyComponent({ data }) {
  console.count('MyComponent render'); // quick way to count renders
  return <div>{data.value}</div>;
}
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Diagnosis Flow

```
PROFILER WORKFLOW:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Step 1: Record  ‚Üí  interact with feature  ‚Üí  Stop

Step 2: Flame graph ‚Äî find dark/wide bars (= slow + many renders)
         ‚Üì
Step 3: Click the component bar
         ‚Üì
Step 4: Check "Why did this render?"
         ‚Üì
Step 5: Match cause to fix:

  "Props changed: onClick"     ‚Üí useCallback for that handler
  "Props changed: style"       ‚Üí useMemo for that object
  "Context changed"            ‚Üí split context or memoize value
  "State changed: parentState" ‚Üí colocate that state lower
  "Hook 2 changed"             ‚Üí check useEffect deps causing loop
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Unnecessary re-render | O(subtree) | React renders the whole subtree below the re-rendering component |
| Profiler recording | O(n renders) | Collects timing for each render during recording |
| `React.memo` comparison | O(P) | P = number of props ‚Äî prevents the O(subtree) cost |
| Context split (K contexts) | O(K) | Each context update only propagates to its consumers |
| `useCallback`/`useMemo` dep check | O(D) | D = dependencies ‚Äî cheap prevention of expensive re-renders |

---

### Q17. What is the difference between `React.memo` and `PureComponent`?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Both are bouncers at a party who check: "Did anything actually change? If not, don't let a re-render in."
>
> **`PureComponent`** is the old-school bouncer ‚Äî only works for **class components**. He checks: "Did any props or state change?" (shallow compare both).
>
> **`React.memo`** is the modern bouncer ‚Äî only works for **function components**. She checks: "Did any props change?" (shallow compare props only).
>
> Both use shallow equality. Neither does deep comparison.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Comparison

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                       PureComponent                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Type: Class component                                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Compares: props AND state (both shallow)                       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  How: implements shouldComponentUpdate automatically            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Re-render if:                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    prevProps !== nextProps (shallow)  OR                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    prevState !== nextState (shallow)                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Skip re-render if:                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    prevProps === nextProps (shallow) AND                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    prevState === nextState (shallow)                            ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                        React.memo                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Type: Function component wrapper (HOC)                         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Compares: props ONLY (doesn't know about internal state)       ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  How: wraps the component, runs comparison before render        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Re-render if:                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    prevProps !== nextProps (shallow)                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    OR parent triggers with same props (always re-renders        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    if no memo)                                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    OR internal state/context changes (always re-render)         ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  Skip re-render if:                                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    prevProps === nextProps (shallow)                            ‚îÇ
‚îÇ    (internal state/context changes still cause re-render)       ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

Side-by-side:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Feature                 PureComponent       React.memo
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ   ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ   ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Component type          Class               Function
  Compares props          ‚úÖ (shallow)        ‚úÖ (shallow)
  Compares state          ‚úÖ (shallow)        ‚ùå (state is internal)
  Custom comparison       shouldComponentUpdate  areEqual() param
  Context changes bypass  ‚úÖ bypasses both    ‚úÖ bypasses both
  React 18 compatible     ‚úÖ (but discouraged) ‚úÖ (preferred)
  Can use hooks           ‚ùå                  ‚úÖ
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Both in Action

```jsx
import React, { Component, PureComponent, memo, useState } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ CLASS: Regular Component vs PureComponent ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

class RegularComponent extends Component {
  render() {
    console.log('RegularComponent rendered');
    // ‚ùå Re-renders EVERY TIME parent re-renders
    // Even if props.name hasn't changed
    return <div>{this.props.name}</div>;
  }
}

class PureComp extends PureComponent {
  render() {
    console.log('PureComp rendered');
    // ‚úÖ Skips re-render if props.name AND state haven't changed
    // PureComponent auto-implements shouldComponentUpdate with shallow compare
    return <div>{this.props.name}</div>;
  }
}

// Equivalent of PureComponent using shouldComponentUpdate manually:
class ManualOptimized extends Component {
  shouldComponentUpdate(nextProps, nextState) {
    // PureComponent does exactly this ‚Äî shallow compare of all keys
    return (
      nextProps.name !== this.props.name ||
      nextState.count !== this.state.count
    );
    // return true  = DO re-render
    // return false = SKIP re-render
  }
  render() {
    return <div>{this.props.name}</div>;
  }
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ FUNCTION: React.memo ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

// Basic usage
const MemoizedFn = memo(function UserCard({ name, age }) {
  console.log('UserCard rendered');
  return <div>{name} ‚Äî {age}</div>;
});
// Re-renders if name or age reference changes (shallow compare)
// Skips re-render if name and age are same primitive values

// With custom comparison (like shouldComponentUpdate for function components)
const SmartMemoized = memo(
  function ComplexCard({ user, metadata }) {
    return <div>{user.name}</div>;
  },
  (prevProps, nextProps) => {
    // Return TRUE  ‚Üí props are EQUAL ‚Üí SKIP re-render
    // Return FALSE ‚Üí props DIFFER   ‚Üí DO re-render
    // Only re-render if user.id or user.name changed
    // (ignore metadata changes entirely)
    return (
      prevProps.user.id   === nextProps.user.id &&
      prevProps.user.name === nextProps.user.name
    );
    // ‚öÝÔ∏è Custom comparator is powerful but risky:
    // If you miss a prop that SHOULD cause re-render, you get stale UI
  }
);

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Demonstrating the difference in state comparison ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
class PureWithState extends PureComponent {
  state = { count: 0 };
  render() {
    return (
      <div>
        <p>Count: {this.state.count}</p>
        <p>Prop: {this.props.label}</p>
        {/* PureComponent also shallow-compares STATE
            ‚Üí this.setState({ count: 0 }) when count is already 0
            ‚Üí PureComponent skips re-render! */}
        <button onClick={() => this.setState({ count: this.state.count + 1 })}>
          Increment
        </button>
      </div>
    );
  }
}

function MemoWithState({ label }) {
  // React.memo does NOT compare internal state
  // Internal state change ‚Üí ALWAYS triggers re-render
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0);

  return (
    <div>
      <p>Count: {count}</p>
      <p>Prop: {label}</p>
      {/* setCount(0) when count is already 0?
          ‚Üí React.memo cannot help ‚Äî state is internal
          ‚Üí React 18 actually optimises this: bails out of re-render
            if new state === old state (for primitive values) */}
      <button onClick={() => setCount(c => c + 1)}>Increment</button>
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Why PureComponent is DISCOURAGED in modern React ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// 1. Class components can't use hooks (useState, useEffect, etc.)
// 2. Class components have more boilerplate
// 3. React team recommends function components for all new code
// 4. React.memo + useCallback/useMemo achieves the same and more

// Rule: Use React.memo for function components (modern)
//       PureComponent only if maintaining legacy class component code
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `extends PureComponent` | React auto-implements `shouldComponentUpdate` with shallow prop + state compare |
| 2 | `shouldComponentUpdate(nextProps, nextState)` | Manual version of PureComponent; `return false` to skip render |
| 3 | `memo(Component)` | Wraps function component; adds prop comparison before each render |
| 4 | `memo(Comp, areEqual)` | Custom comparator: `true` = equal = skip render; `false` = render |
| 5 | Internal state changes | `React.memo` never blocks internal state/context changes ‚Äî both still re-render |
| 6 | Shallow comparison | Only top-level keys are compared with `Object.is` ‚Äî nested objects by reference |

---

#### The Shallow Compare Visualized

```
props = { user: { name: 'Alice' }, count: 5 }

Shallow compare checks:
  props.user  ‚Üí same reference? (Object.is)
  props.count ‚Üí same value? (Object.is)

  Object.is({ name: 'Alice' }, { name: 'Alice' }) ‚Üí FALSE ‚ùå
  (different objects, even if content is identical)

  Object.is(5, 5) ‚Üí TRUE ‚úÖ

So: if parent does <Comp user={{ name: 'Alice' }} count={5} />
    on every render (inline object), PureComponent / memo BOTH fail.
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Shallow comparison (P props) | O(P) | Each prop key checked with `Object.is` |
| Re-render skipped | O(1) | No work done if comparison says equal |
| `shouldComponentUpdate` | O(P + S) | P props + S state keys ‚Äî also compares state |
| `React.memo` areEqual | O(custom) | Depends on your comparator logic |
| Memory overhead | O(P) | Previous props stored for next comparison |

---

## End of Section: REACT ‚Äî Performance (Q11‚ÄìQ17)

---

## REACT ‚Äî Patterns

---

### Q18. Explain the Container/Presentational pattern. Is it still relevant with hooks?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine a restaurant. The **waiter** (Presentational) just takes your order and brings your food ‚Äî they don't cook anything. The **kitchen** (Container) does all the cooking and logic.
>
> Container/Presentational splits React components the same way:
> - **Presentational** = "dumb" UI components ‚Äî just receive props, know nothing about data fetching or business logic.
> - **Container** = "smart" data components ‚Äî handle API calls, state, and pass data down.
>
> With hooks, you can pull the "kitchen logic" into a custom hook instead of a container component ‚Äî so the pattern is less mandatory, but the *principle* (separate concerns) is still very relevant.

---

#### Flowchart

```
WITHOUT hooks (classic pattern):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <UserListContainer>               ‚Üê Container: fetches data,
       ‚îÇ                               manages loading/error state
       ‚îÇ  passes: { users, loading, error }
       ‚ñº
  <UserList users={...} />          ‚Üê Presentational: pure UI
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ <UserCard user={...} />  ‚Üê Also Presentational
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ <Spinner />              ‚Üê Also Presentational


WITH hooks (modern evolution):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  useUserList()                     ‚Üê Custom hook replaces Container
       ‚îÇ  returns: { users, loading, error }
       ‚îÇ
  <UserList />                      ‚Üê Component uses hook directly
       ‚îÇ                               OR receives data via props
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ <UserCard user={...} />
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ <Spinner />

  The principle (logic vs UI separation) remains.
  The "Container component" is replaced by a custom hook.
```

---

#### Code Example

```jsx
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// CLASSIC PATTERN ‚Äî Container + Presentational
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Presentational: knows ONLY about UI ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Props are its entire world. No API calls, no state (or minimal UI state).
function UserList({ users, loading, error, onSelect }) {
  // Step 1: Handle loading state with a prop ‚Äî doesn't know HOW data loads
  if (loading) return <div className="spinner">Loading...</div>;

  // Step 2: Handle error state with a prop ‚Äî doesn't know WHY it errored
  if (error) return <div className="error">Error: {error.message}</div>;

  // Step 3: Render the data it was given ‚Äî pure mapping prop ‚Üí UI
  return (
    <ul>
      {users.map(user => (
        <UserCard key={user.id} user={user} onSelect={onSelect} />
      ))}
    </ul>
  );
}

// Also presentational ‚Äî no logic, just display
function UserCard({ user, onSelect }) {
  return (
    <li onClick={() => onSelect(user.id)}>
      <img src={user.avatar} alt={user.name} />
      <span>{user.name}</span>
    </li>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Container: knows ONLY about data/logic ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Its render method is almost always just delegating to Presentational
class UserListContainer extends React.Component {
  state = { users: [], loading: true, error: null };

  async componentDidMount() {
    try {
      // Step 4: Container handles ALL data fetching
      const res  = await fetch('/api/users');
      const data = await res.json();
      this.setState({ users: data, loading: false });
    } catch (err) {
      this.setState({ error: err, loading: false });
    }
  }

  handleSelect = (userId) => {
    // Container handles business logic
    console.log('Selected:', userId);
  };

  render() {
    const { users, loading, error } = this.state;
    // Step 5: Container just passes data to Presentational
    return (
      <UserList
        users={users}
        loading={loading}
        error={error}
        onSelect={this.handleSelect}
      />
    );
  }
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// MODERN PATTERN ‚Äî Custom Hook replaces Container component
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// Step 6: Extract container logic into a custom hook
// The hook IS the "container" ‚Äî just not a component anymore
function useUserList() {
  const [users,   setUsers]   = React.useState([]);
  const [loading, setLoading] = React.useState(true);
  const [error,   setError]   = React.useState(null);

  React.useEffect(() => {
    let cancelled = false;

    fetch('/api/users')
      .then(r => r.json())
      .then(data => { if (!cancelled) { setUsers(data); setLoading(false); }})
      .catch(err => { if (!cancelled) { setError(err);  setLoading(false); }});

    return () => { cancelled = true; }; // cleanup on unmount
  }, []);

  const handleSelect = React.useCallback((userId) => {
    console.log('Selected:', userId);
  }, []);

  return { users, loading, error, onSelect: handleSelect };
}

// Step 7: Presentational component is UNCHANGED ‚Äî
// it still just renders props. Now it can get them from a hook OR a parent.
function ModernUserList() {
  // Option A: component uses hook directly (self-contained)
  const { users, loading, error, onSelect } = useUserList();

  return <UserList users={users} loading={loading} error={error} onSelect={onSelect} />;
}

// Option B: keep UserList pure (props only) for easier testing
// and have a wrapper use the hook ‚Äî same separation, cleaner
function UserListPage() {
  const data = useUserList(); // all logic in hook
  return <UserList {...data} />; // UserList stays "dumb" and testable
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Why this is still relevant ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚úÖ Testability: Presentational components are pure functions ‚Üí easy unit tests
// ‚úÖ Reusability: Same UserList can be fed by REST, GraphQL, or mock data
// ‚úÖ Separation: UI designers can work on Presentational without touching logic
// ‚úÖ Storybook: Presentational components are trivial to document/preview
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1‚Äì3 | `UserList` receives props only | Pure function of props ‚Äî deterministic, trivially testable |
| 4 | `componentDidMount` fetches | Container owns all side effects ‚Äî Presentational is unaware |
| 5 | Container renders `<UserList {...state}>` | Container's render is just a pass-through ‚Äî thin glue layer |
| 6 | `useUserList()` hook | Replicates all Container logic without a wrapper component in the tree |
| 7 | `<UserList {...data} />` | Presentational component unchanged ‚Äî still pure ‚Äî now consumes hook via parent |

---

#### Is It Still Relevant?

```
Classic Container component  ‚Üí  largely REPLACED by custom hooks
Presentational component     ‚Üí  still 100% relevant and recommended

The PRINCIPLE lives on:
  "Separate data/logic concerns from UI rendering concerns"
  ‚Üí Just express it with custom hooks instead of wrapper components
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Presentational render | O(N) | N = number of items to render |
| Hook data fetch | O(1) | Single async operation, cached after first load |
| Component tree depth | O(1) extra | Modern hook removes the Container wrapper component from the tree |

---

### Q19. What is a Higher Order Component? Give a real production use case.

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> A Higher Order Component (HOC) is like a **phone case factory**. You put any phone in (any component), and it comes out with extra features ‚Äî like a waterproof case or a battery pack.
>
> The factory doesn't care what phone model you put in. It just wraps it and adds features. Your phone still works exactly the same ‚Äî it just has new abilities.
>
> HOC: a function that **takes a component** and **returns a new, enhanced component**.

---

#### Flowchart

```
HOC Definition:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  withFeature(WrappedComponent)
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ returns EnhancedComponent
                  ‚îÇ
                  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Adds: extra props, lifecycle, logic
                  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Renders: <WrappedComponent {...props} {...extras} />
                  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Original component is untouched

Flow:
  <EnhancedComponent userId="123" />
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº  HOC intercepts render
  HOC logic runs (fetch, auth check, logging...)
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  <WrappedComponent userId="123" extraProp="from HOC" />
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  Original component renders normally

HOC Composition:
  const Enhanced = withAuth(withLogging(withTheme(Button)));
  ‚Üí Applied right-to-left: Theme ‚Üí Logging ‚Üí Auth ‚Üí Button
  ‚Üí Each HOC wraps the previous result
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Real Production Use Cases

```jsx
import React, { useEffect, useState, useRef } from 'react';

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// USE CASE 1: Authentication Guard (most common production HOC)
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// Step 1: HOC is a function that takes a component
function withAuth(WrappedComponent) {
  // Step 2: Returns a NEW component (never mutate WrappedComponent!)
  function AuthGuard(props) {
    const { currentUser, isLoading } = useAuthContext(); // from your auth context

    // Step 3: HOC adds logic BEFORE deciding to render WrappedComponent
    if (isLoading) return <FullPageSpinner />;

    if (!currentUser) {
      // Redirect to login ‚Äî WrappedComponent never renders
      return <Navigate to="/login" state={{ from: props.location }} replace />;
    }

    // Step 4: Pass through ALL original props unchanged
    // The wrapped component has NO idea it was guarded
    return <WrappedComponent {...props} />;
  }

  // Step 5: Set a display name for React DevTools readability
  AuthGuard.displayName = `withAuth(${WrappedComponent.displayName || WrappedComponent.name})`;

  return AuthGuard;
}

// Usage: wrap any route-level component
const ProtectedDashboard = withAuth(Dashboard);
const ProtectedProfile   = withAuth(Profile);
// Now <ProtectedDashboard /> will redirect to /login if not authenticated


// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// USE CASE 2: Feature Flag Gate
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function withFeatureFlag(WrappedComponent, flagName, Fallback = null) {
  function FeatureFlaggedComponent(props) {
    const flags  = useFeatureFlags(); // custom hook that reads from LaunchDarkly/etc.
    const isOn   = flags[flagName];

    // If flag is OFF, show fallback (or nothing)
    if (!isOn) return Fallback ? <Fallback {...props} /> : null;

    return <WrappedComponent {...props} />;
  }

  FeatureFlaggedComponent.displayName = `withFeatureFlag(${flagName})`;
  return FeatureFlaggedComponent;
}

// Usage: whole component gated by a feature flag
const NewCheckout = withFeatureFlag(CheckoutV2, 'new-checkout-flow', CheckoutV1);
// LaunchDarkly says flag is OFF ‚Üí CheckoutV1 renders
// LaunchDarkly says flag is ON  ‚Üí CheckoutV2 renders


// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// USE CASE 3: Analytics / Impression Tracking
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function withImpressionTracking(WrappedComponent, trackingId) {
  function TrackedComponent(props) {
    const ref = useRef(null);

    useEffect(() => {
      const el = ref.current;
      if (!el) return;

      // IntersectionObserver fires when element enters viewport
      const observer = new IntersectionObserver(
        ([entry]) => {
          if (entry.isIntersecting) {
            // Fire analytics event ‚Äî WrappedComponent has no idea this is happening
            analytics.track('impression', {
              component: trackingId,
              timestamp:  Date.now(),
            });
            observer.disconnect(); // fire once only
          }
        },
        { threshold: 0.5 } // 50% visible counts as an impression
      );

      observer.observe(el);
      return () => observer.disconnect();
    }, []);

    // Inject a ref ‚Äî WrappedComponent must accept a forwarded ref
    // OR wrap in a div (simpler but adds a DOM node)
    return (
      <div ref={ref}>
        <WrappedComponent {...props} />
      </div>
    );
  }

  TrackedComponent.displayName = `withImpressionTracking(${trackingId})`;
  return TrackedComponent;
}

// Usage: any promotional component gets auto-tracked
const TrackedBanner      = withImpressionTracking(PromoBanner,    'promo-banner');
const TrackedProductCard = withImpressionTracking(ProductCard,    'product-card');


// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// COMPOSING MULTIPLE HOCs
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// Manual composition ‚Äî reads right to left (confusing)
const Enhanced = withAuth(withFeatureFlag(withImpressionTracking(Dashboard, 'dash'), 'v2-dash'));

// Use a compose utility (lodash, redux, or roll your own)
const compose = (...fns) => x => fns.reduceRight((acc, fn) => fn(acc), x);

const EnhancedDashboard = compose(
  withAuth,
  comp => withFeatureFlag(comp, 'v2-dashboard'),
  comp => withImpressionTracking(comp, 'dashboard'),
)(Dashboard);
// Reads top-to-bottom: Auth ‚Üí FeatureFlag ‚Üí ImpressionTracking ‚Üí Dashboard


// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// HOC RULES (to avoid bugs)
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// ‚ùå DON'T: create HOC inside a component ‚Äî new component type every render!
function BadParent() {
  const WrappedList = withAuth(List); // ‚Üê NEW type every render ‚Üí unmounts/remounts
  return <WrappedList />;
}

// ‚úÖ DO: define HOCs at MODULE level, outside components
const WrappedList = withAuth(List); // defined once, stable type
function GoodParent() {
  return <WrappedList />;
}
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `function withAuth(WrappedComponent)` | Function that accepts a component ‚Äî this is the HOC signature |
| 2 | `function AuthGuard(props)` | Returns a new component ‚Äî the enhanced version |
| 3 | Logic before render | HOC runs checks (auth, flags) before deciding to render original |
| 4 | `<WrappedComponent {...props} />` | Pass all original props through ‚Äî original component is transparent to HOC |
| 5 | `displayName` | Makes React DevTools show `withAuth(Dashboard)` instead of `AuthGuard` |
| 6 | `compose(...)` | Applies multiple HOCs cleanly ‚Äî avoids deeply nested `withA(withB(withC(...)))` |
| 7 | HOC at module level | Creating HOC inside component == new component type every render == remount bug |

---

#### HOC vs Custom Hook ‚Äî When to Use Which

```
Use HOC when:
  ‚úÖ Need to conditionally render or redirect (auth guard)
  ‚úÖ Need to inject JSX wrapper around component (impression tracking div)
  ‚úÖ Working with class components (hooks don't work there)
  ‚úÖ Need composable component-level cross-cutting concerns

Use Custom Hook when:
  ‚úÖ Just need to share logic/state (no JSX wrapping needed)
  ‚úÖ Working exclusively with function components
  ‚úÖ Simpler to debug (hook call chain vs component tree)
  ‚úÖ TypeScript inference is better
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| HOC wrapping at module level | O(1) | Creates one new component type once |
| HOC render overhead | O(1) | Just a thin wrapper render, then delegates |
| Composed HOCs (K layers) | O(K) renders | Each HOC in the chain runs its render logic |
| `IntersectionObserver` setup | O(1) | Single observer per element |

---

### Q20. How do Compound Components share state without prop drilling?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Think of a `<select>` and `<option>` in HTML. You never pass `selectedValue` down to each `<option>`. The browser handles that internally. Yet `<option>` knows when it's selected.
>
> Compound Components copy this idea in React. A parent component holds state in a **shared Context**, and all child sub-components read from that context directly ‚Äî no prop drilling needed.
>
> It's like a walkie-talkie channel: parent sets the channel, all children tune in automatically.

---

#### Flowchart

```
WITHOUT compound components (prop drilling):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <Tabs activeTab={activeTab} onChange={setActiveTab}>
    <TabList activeTab={activeTab} onChange={setActiveTab}>  ‚Üê drilling
      <Tab id="a" activeTab={activeTab} onChange={setActiveTab} />  ‚Üê drilling
      <Tab id="b" activeTab={activeTab} onChange={setActiveTab} />
    </TabList>
    <TabPanels activeTab={activeTab}>  ‚Üê drilling
      <TabPanel id="a" activeTab={activeTab} />  ‚Üê drilling
    </TabPanels>
  </Tabs>

WITH compound components (implicit state sharing via Context):
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <Tabs defaultTab="a">           ‚Üê holds state internally
    <TabList>                     ‚Üê reads from context (no props needed)
      <Tab id="a">Tab A</Tab>     ‚Üê reads activeTab from context
      <Tab id="b">Tab B</Tab>
    </TabList>
    <TabPanels>
      <TabPanel id="a">Content A</TabPanel>
```
