```
      <TabPanel id="b">Content B</TabPanel>
    </TabPanels>
  </Tabs>
  ‚Üê Each child automatically gets what it needs
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Full Tabs Compound Component

```jsx
import React, {
  createContext, useContext, useState, useId
} from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 1: Create a Context for the shared state ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// This is the "walkie-talkie channel"
const TabsContext = createContext(null);

// Helper hook ‚Äî child components use this to read shared state
// Also throws a clear error if child is used outside <Tabs>
function useTabsContext() {
  const ctx = useContext(TabsContext);
  if (!ctx) {
    throw new Error('Tab sub-components must be used inside <Tabs>');
  }
  return ctx;
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 2: Parent component ‚Äî holds ALL shared state ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function Tabs({ children, defaultTab }) {
  const [activeTab, setActiveTab] = useState(defaultTab);

  // Step 3: Provide state + setter through context
  // All child sub-components read from here ‚Äî NO prop drilling
  return (
    <TabsContext.Provider value={{ activeTab, setActiveTab }}>
      <div className="tabs">
        {children}
      </div>
    </TabsContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 4: Sub-components read from context, not props ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function TabList({ children }) {
  // TabList doesn't need activeTab or setActiveTab as props
  // It just passes through children ‚Äî they'll read context themselves
  return (
    <div role="tablist" className="tab-list">
      {children}
    </div>
  );
}

function Tab({ id, children }) {
  // Step 5: Tab reads activeTab directly from context
  const { activeTab, setActiveTab } = useTabsContext();
  const isActive = activeTab === id;

  return (
    <button
      role="tab"
      aria-selected={isActive}       // accessibility
      tabIndex={isActive ? 0 : -1}   // keyboard nav
      className={isActive ? 'tab tab--active' : 'tab'}
      onClick={() => setActiveTab(id)} // updates shared state via context
    >
      {children}
    </button>
  );
}

function TabPanels({ children }) {
  // Passes children through unchanged ‚Äî children read context themselves
  return <div className="tab-panels">{children}</div>;
}

function TabPanel({ id, children }) {
  // Step 6: TabPanel reads activeTab to know if it should show
  const { activeTab } = useTabsContext();

  if (activeTab !== id) return null; // hide when not active

  return (
    <div role="tabpanel" className="tab-panel">
      {children}
    </div>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 7: Attach sub-components as static properties ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// This is idiomatic for compound components ‚Äî groups them under one namespace
Tabs.TabList   = TabList;
Tabs.Tab       = Tab;
Tabs.TabPanels = TabPanels;
Tabs.TabPanel  = TabPanel;

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Usage ‚Äî clean, no prop drilling ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function App() {
  return (
    <Tabs defaultTab="overview">
      <Tabs.TabList>
        <Tabs.Tab id="overview">Overview</Tabs.Tab>
        <Tabs.Tab id="reviews">Reviews</Tabs.Tab>
        <Tabs.Tab id="specs">Specs</Tabs.Tab>
      </Tabs.TabList>

      <Tabs.TabPanels>
        <Tabs.TabPanel id="overview">
          <p>Product overview content here</p>
        </Tabs.TabPanel>
        <Tabs.TabPanel id="reviews">
          <p>Customer reviews here</p>
        </Tabs.TabPanel>
        <Tabs.TabPanel id="specs">
          <p>Technical specifications here</p>
        </Tabs.TabPanel>
      </Tabs.TabPanels>
    </Tabs>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Controlled variant (parent controls active tab) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Compound Components can also be "controlled" (like controlled inputs)
function ControlledTabs({ activeTab, onTabChange, children }) {
  return (
    // If activeTab + onTabChange are provided externally ‚Üí controlled
    // If not ‚Üí fall back to internal state (see defaultTab above)
    <TabsContext.Provider value={{ activeTab, setActiveTab: onTabChange }}>
      <div className="tabs">{children}</div>
    </TabsContext.Provider>
  );
}

// Usage of controlled variant:
function Page() {
  const [tab, setTab] = useState('overview');

  // Parent now controls which tab is active ‚Äî for URL sync, etc.
  return (
    <ControlledTabs activeTab={tab} onTabChange={setTab}>
      <Tabs.TabList>
        <Tabs.Tab id="overview">Overview</Tabs.Tab>
        <Tabs.Tab id="reviews">Reviews</Tabs.Tab>
      </Tabs.TabList>
      {/* ... */}
    </ControlledTabs>
  );
}
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `createContext(null)` | Creates the shared channel all sub-components will tune into |
| 2 | `useTabsContext()` | Centralizes context access + throws clear error if used outside parent |
| 3 | `TabsContext.Provider value={...}` | Parent injects `activeTab` + `setActiveTab` into context |
| 4 | `TabList` passes children through | No props needed ‚Äî children find context themselves |
| 5 | `const { activeTab } = useTabsContext()` | Tab reads active state directly ‚Äî no prop drilling |
| 6 | `if (activeTab !== id) return null` | TabPanel renders only when it's the active tab |
| 7 | `Tabs.TabList = TabList` | Namespacing ‚Äî `<Tabs.Tab>` signals it belongs inside `<Tabs>` |

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Context read per sub-component | O(1) | Direct context lookup |
| State update (`setActiveTab`) | O(1) | Single state update triggers re-render |
| Re-renders on tab change | O(N) | N = all consumers of TabsContext ‚Äî can be optimised by splitting context |
| Component tree depth | O(1) | No extra wrapper components needed ‚Äî children access state directly |

---

### Q21. What is the Render Props pattern? When would you still use it over hooks?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine a vending machine that knows how to track what you bought ‚Äî but doesn't care what it looks like on screen. Instead of having its own display, it hands you a **blank receipt and says "you draw whatever you want."**
>
> Render Props: a component does all the complex logic and **passes the results to a function that YOU provide** to decide how to render. You're in full control of the UI.
>
> With hooks you usually just call the logic in your own component instead of needing someone to hand it to you ‚Äî but Render Props still shine in a few specific situations.

---

#### Flowchart

```
Render Props pattern:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <DataProvider render={(data, loading) => (
    <MyUI data={data} loading={loading} />
  )} />

  DataProvider:
    - owns the logic (fetch, mouse position, resize, etc.)
    - does NOT own the UI
    - calls props.render(state) inside its render method


FLOW:
  <MouseTracker render={({ x, y }) => <Cursor x={x} y={y} />} />
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº  MouseTracker tracks mouse internally
  state = { x: 240, y: 150 }
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº  calls: props.render({ x: 240, y: 150 })
  Your render function executes
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  <Cursor x={240} y={150} /> renders on screen

Alternative syntax ‚Äî "children as function":
  <MouseTracker>
    {({ x, y }) => <Cursor x={x} y={y} />}
  </MouseTracker>
  // props.children is the function ‚Äî called the same way
```

---

#### Code Example

```jsx
import React, { useState, useEffect, useRef } from 'react';

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// CLASSIC RENDER PROPS ‚Äî Mouse Position tracker
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

class MouseTracker extends React.Component {
  state = { x: 0, y: 0 };

  handleMouseMove = (e) => {
    // Step 1: Component owns logic ‚Äî tracks mouse internally
    this.setState({ x: e.clientX, y: e.clientY });
  };

  render() {
    // Step 2: Instead of rendering its own UI, calls the render prop
    // with current state ‚Äî the CALLER decides what to show
    return (
      <div onMouseMove={this.handleMouseMove} style={{ height: '100vh' }}>
        {/* Step 3: Call the function prop, pass logic results */}
        {this.props.render(this.state)}
      </div>
    );
  }
}

// Usage: MouseTracker renders whatever you tell it to
function App() {
  return (
    <MouseTracker
      render={({ x, y }) => (
        // Could be ANYTHING ‚Äî cursor, tooltip, heatmap, etc.
        <div style={{ position: 'fixed', left: x, top: y, pointerEvents: 'none' }}>
          üîµ
        </div>
      )}
    />
  );
}

// "Children as function" variant ‚Äî same pattern, different syntax
function AppChildren() {
  return (
    <MouseTracker>
      {({ x, y }) => <p>Mouse is at ({x}, {y})</p>}
    </MouseTracker>
  );
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// MODERN EQUIVALENT ‚Äî Custom Hook (replaces most render props)
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function useMousePosition() {
  const [pos, setPos] = useState({ x: 0, y: 0 });

  useEffect(() => {
    const handle = (e) => setPos({ x: e.clientX, y: e.clientY });
    window.addEventListener('mousemove', handle);
    return () => window.removeEventListener('mousemove', handle);
  }, []);

  return pos;
}

// Hook usage ‚Äî cleaner, no nesting, same result
function AppWithHook() {
  const { x, y } = useMousePosition();
  return <p>Mouse is at ({x}, {y})</p>;
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// WHEN TO STILL USE RENDER PROPS (over hooks)
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// CASE 1: Animated / transition libraries that need a renderer
// Libraries like Framer Motion, React Spring use this pattern
// because they own the animation state + need to inject props
// into whatever element YOU want to animate

import { Transition } from '@headlessui/react'; // example that uses render props

function DropdownMenu({ open }) {
  return (
    <Transition
      show={open}
      enter="transition-opacity duration-150"
      enterFrom="opacity-0"
      enterTo="opacity-100"
      leave="transition-opacity duration-150"
      leaveFrom="opacity-100"
      leaveTo="opacity-0"
    >
      {/* Render prop as children ‚Äî Transition injects transition className */}
      <div>Menu items here</div>
    </Transition>
  );
}

// CASE 2: Inversion of control ‚Äî when the logic component needs to
// wrap its output in a specific DOM structure (e.g., a scroll container)

class InfiniteScroll extends React.Component {
  state = { items: [], page: 1, loading: false };

  componentDidMount() { this.loadMore(); }

  loadMore = async () => {
    // Logic component owns: scroll detection, page tracking, loading state
    this.setState({ loading: true });
    const newItems = await fetchPage(this.state.page);
    this.setState(s => ({
      items: [...s.items, ...newItems],
      page: s.page + 1,
      loading: false,
    }));
  };

  render() {
    const { items, loading } = this.state;
    return (
      // Logic component owns the scroll container
      <div onScroll={this.handleScroll} style={{ overflow: 'auto', height: 400 }}>
        {/* Caller controls how each item renders */}
        {this.props.children({ items, loading })}
        {loading && <Spinner />}
      </div>
    );
  }
}

// Usage ‚Äî you decide how items look:
<InfiniteScroll>
  {({ items, loading }) =>
    items.map(item => <ProductCard key={item.id} product={item} />)
  }
</InfiniteScroll>

// CASE 3: Class components (before hooks existed, and legacy codebases)
// HOCs and render props are the only options for class components.
// If you maintain older React code ‚Üí render props still valid.
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `this.setState({ x, y })` | Logic component tracks mouse internally ‚Äî UI doesn't know about this |
| 2 | `{this.props.render(this.state)}` | Calls the function prop with current state ‚Äî inversion of control |
| 3 | `render={({ x, y }) => <div>}` | Caller receives state and decides what to render ‚Äî full UI flexibility |
| 4 | `children as function` | Same pattern, but uses `props.children` instead of `props.render` |
| 5 | Custom hook replaces it | For function components, hooks achieve the same without nesting |
| 6 | Render props still valid | When logic component must own the DOM wrapper (scroll, transition, etc.) |

---

#### Render Props vs Hooks Decision

```
Use Render Props when:                    Use Custom Hook when:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ         ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
‚úÖ Logic component must own DOM           ‚úÖ Just sharing logic/state
‚úÖ Transition/animation libraries         ‚úÖ Function components only
‚úÖ Maintaining class component code       ‚úÖ No DOM wrapper needed
‚úÖ Inversion of control over rendering   ‚úÖ Simpler to test and debug
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Render prop call | O(1) | One function call per render cycle |
| Nesting depth (N render props) | O(N) renders | Each render prop adds one layer of component tree |
| Custom hook equivalent | O(1) | Same logic cost, no extra tree depth |
| Event listener (mousemove) | O(1) setup | Added once, fires at browser rate (~60fps) |

---

### Q22. How does the Provider pattern work? What are its performance pitfalls?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> Imagine a school loudspeaker. The principal (Provider) broadcasts announcements (state) to everyone in the school (all Consumer components). **Every student hears every announcement** ‚Äî even math class hears the lunch menu.
>
> The problem: every announcement makes ALL classrooms "react," even if that class doesn't care. That's the performance problem ‚Äî context updates wake up ALL consumers, even irrelevant ones.

---

#### Flowchart

```
Provider Pattern:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <AppProvider>                   ‚Üê injects value into context
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ <ComponentA />         ‚Üê reads context ‚Üí re-renders on any change
       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ <ComponentB />         ‚Üê reads context ‚Üí re-renders on any change
       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ <ComponentC />         ‚Üê reads context ‚Üí re-renders on any change
                                     Even if only one value in context changed!

Performance problem ‚Äî one big context:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

  context value = { user, theme, cart, notifications }
                          ‚îÇ
             user changes (login/logout)
                          ‚îÇ
                          ‚ñº
       ALL consumers re-render ‚Äî including:
       ThemeToggle (only reads theme ‚Äî didn't change!) ‚ùå
       CartIcon    (only reads cart  ‚Äî didn't change!) ‚ùå
       UserAvatar  (reads user ‚Äî ‚úÖ correct re-render)

Fix ‚Äî split contexts:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <UserProvider>
    <ThemeProvider>
      <CartProvider>
        <App />
      </CartProvider>
    </ThemeProvider>
  </UserProvider>

  User changes ‚Üí only UserContext consumers re-render ‚úÖ
  Theme changes ‚Üí only ThemeContext consumers re-render ‚úÖ
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Provider Pattern + All Pitfalls + Fixes

```jsx
import React, {
  createContext, useContext, useState, useMemo, useCallback, memo
} from 'react';

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// PITFALL 1: Unstable context value causes all consumers to re-render
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

const CartContext = createContext(null);

// ‚ùå BAD: new object created on EVERY render of CartProvider
function BadCartProvider({ children }) {
  const [items, setItems] = useState([]);

  return (
    // { items, setItems } is a NEW object every render
    // ‚Üí every CartContext consumer ALWAYS re-renders
    <CartContext.Provider value={{ items, setItems }}>
      {children}
    </CartContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚úÖ FIX: memoize the context value
function GoodCartProvider({ children }) {
  const [items, setItems] = useState([]);

  // Step 1: Stabilise the value with useMemo
  // Only creates a new object when `items` actually changes
  const value = useMemo(() => ({ items, setItems }), [items]);
  // setItems from useState is already stable ‚Äî no dep needed for it

  return (
    <CartContext.Provider value={value}>
      {children}
    </CartContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// PITFALL 2: One big context re-renders unrelated components
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// ‚ùå BAD: all state in one context
const AppContext = createContext(null);

function BadAppProvider({ children }) {
  const [user,          setUser]          = useState(null);
  const [theme,         setTheme]         = useState('light');
  const [notifications, setNotifications] = useState([]);

  // Any change to ANY of these ‚Üí ALL consumers re-render
  return (
    <AppContext.Provider value={{ user, setUser, theme, setTheme, notifications, setNotifications }}>
      {children}
    </AppContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚úÖ FIX: split contexts by concern
const UserContext          = createContext(null);
const ThemeContext         = createContext(null);
const NotificationsContext = createContext(null);

function GoodAppProvider({ children }) {
  const [user,          setUser]          = useState(null);
  const [theme,         setTheme]         = useState('light');
  const [notifications, setNotifications] = useState([]);

  const userValue  = useMemo(() => ({ user, setUser }),                     [user]);
  const themeValue = useMemo(() => ({ theme, setTheme }),                   [theme]);
  const notifValue = useMemo(() => ({ notifications, setNotifications }),   [notifications]);

  // Step 2: Nest providers ‚Äî each only broadcasts to its own consumers
  return (
    <UserContext.Provider value={userValue}>
      <ThemeContext.Provider value={themeValue}>
        <NotificationsContext.Provider value={notifValue}>
          {children}
        </NotificationsContext.Provider>
      </ThemeContext.Provider>
    </UserContext.Provider>
  );
}

// Consumer hooks ‚Äî clean API
export const useUser          = () => useContext(UserContext);
export const useTheme         = () => useContext(ThemeContext);
export const useNotifications = () => useContext(NotificationsContext);

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// PITFALL 3: Context bypasses React.memo
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// Even if a component is wrapped in React.memo,
// if it reads from context ‚Üí it re-renders on any context change
const UserAvatar = memo(function UserAvatar() {
  const { user } = useUser(); // ‚Üê reads context
  // React.memo only checks PROPS
  // Context changes always bypass memo ‚Üí UserAvatar re-renders on user change
  return <img src={user?.avatar} alt={user?.name} />;
});

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// PITFALL 4: Reading only part of context still re-renders on all changes
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// If you're stuck with one big context (e.g., Redux-style global store),
// use a selector to avoid re-renders when irrelevant state changes

// With Zustand (handles selectors natively):
const useCartCount = () => useStore(state => state.cart.length);
// Component only re-renders when cart.length changes, not all state

// With Context: implement a "context selector" manually using useRef + subscription
// (this is complex ‚Äî better to just split contexts)

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// FULL PROVIDER SETUP ‚Äî production pattern
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

// Compose multiple providers cleanly
function AppProviders({ children }) {
  return (
    <GoodAppProvider>
      <GoodCartProvider>
        {children}
      </GoodCartProvider>
    </GoodAppProvider>
  );
}

// In index.jsx / main.jsx:
// <AppProviders><App /></AppProviders>

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ Custom hook with error guard ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function useCart() {
  const ctx = useContext(CartContext);
  if (!ctx) throw new Error('useCart must be used inside CartProvider');
  return ctx;
}
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `value={{ items, setItems }}` inline | New object reference every render ‚Üí every consumer re-renders even if items unchanged |
| 2 | `useMemo(() => ({ items, setItems }), [items])` | Stable object ‚Äî consumers only re-render when `items` actually changes |
| 3 | Single big context | One state change cascades to ALL consumers of that context |
| 4 | Split into `UserContext`, `ThemeContext`, etc. | Each context update isolated to only its consumers |
| 5 | `memo` + context read | `React.memo` cannot block context updates ‚Äî consumer always re-renders |
| 6 | Selector (Zustand) | Subscribe to only the slice you need ‚Üí no re-render for unrelated state |

---

#### Performance Pitfalls Summary

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ Pitfall                ‚îÇ Symptom                      ‚îÇ Fix                          ‚îÇ
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
‚îÇ Inline value object    ‚îÇ All consumers re-render      ‚îÇ useMemo on context value     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ One large context      ‚îÇ Unrelated components render  ‚îÇ Split contexts by concern    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ memo + context read    ‚îÇ memo doesn't help            ‚îÇ Split context or use Zustand ‚îÇ
‚îÇ Functions in context   ‚îÇ New fn ref every render      ‚îÇ useCallback for functions    ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| Context read | O(1) | Direct lookup via React internals |
| Context update propagation | O(C) | C = number of consumers ‚Äî all notified |
| `useMemo` on context value | O(D) check | Dep array comparison to decide if new object needed |
| Split contexts (K contexts) | O(C_k) per update | Only C_k consumers of the changed context re-render |

---

### Q23. What makes a good custom hook? How do you decide when to extract one?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> A custom hook is like a **power tool you build yourself**. A good power tool has one clear job (drills holes, cuts wood), is safe to use repeatedly, and doesn't break if you move it.
>
> A bad power tool does 10 different things, has side effects you don't expect, and only works in one specific workshop.
>
> Good custom hooks: one clear purpose, easy to test in isolation, predictable inputs/outputs, and usable in any component.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî When to Extract a Custom Hook

```
Decision Tree:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Is the same logic copy-pasted in 2+ components?
       YES ‚Üí Extract to custom hook ‚úÖ

  Does the logic mix concerns (fetch + timer + DOM)?
       YES ‚Üí Split into multiple focused hooks ‚úÖ

  Is the hook body longer than ~30 lines?
       YES ‚Üí Consider splitting ‚úÖ

  Does the component have > 3 useEffect / useState calls?
       YES ‚Üí likely extractable to hooks ‚úÖ

  Is this logic ONLY used once in one place and < 10 lines?
       YES ‚Üí Keep it inline, don't over-abstract ‚ùå

Rules for GOOD custom hooks:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚úÖ Name starts with "use" (React enforces this for lint rules)
  ‚úÖ Single responsibility ‚Äî one thing done well
  ‚úÖ Returns a stable, predictable interface
  ‚úÖ All side effects cleaned up (return cleanup from useEffect)
  ‚úÖ Works correctly when called multiple times (no global side effects)
  ‚úÖ Dependencies managed correctly (no stale closures)
  ‚úÖ Fully testable with renderHook() from @testing-library/react
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Bad vs Good Custom Hooks

```jsx
import { useState, useEffect, useCallback, useRef } from 'react';

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// ‚ùå BAD HOOK ‚Äî does too many things, leaks, unstable interface
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function useBadDataFetcher(url) {
  // Problem 1: no cleanup ‚Äî if component unmounts mid-fetch, sets state
  //            on unmounted component ‚Üí React warning + potential memory leak
  useEffect(() => {
    fetch(url).then(r => r.json()).then(data => setData(data));
    // ‚Üê no controller.abort(), no cancellation, no cleanup return
  }, [url]);

  // Problem 2: mixed concerns ‚Äî timers AND fetching in one hook
  useEffect(() => {
    const id = setInterval(() => fetch(url), 5000); // auto-refresh
    // ‚Üê timer never cleared! Continues after component unmounts
  }, []);

  // Problem 3: unstable return ‚Äî object recreated every call
  return { data, loading, error, retry: () => fetch(url) };
  //                                    ^^^ new fn every render
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// ‚úÖ GOOD HOOK 1 ‚Äî useFetch: focused, cleaned up, stable interface
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function useFetch(url) {
  const [data,    setData]    = useState(null);
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true);
  const [error,   setError]   = useState(null);

  useEffect(() => {
    // Step 1: Create AbortController for cancellation
    const controller = new AbortController();
    let   cancelled  = false;

    setLoading(true);

    fetch(url, { signal: controller.signal })
      .then(r => {
        if (!r.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${r.status}`);
        return r.json();
      })
      .then(data => {
        // Step 2: Guard against setting state after unmount
        if (!cancelled) { setData(data); setLoading(false); }
      })
      .catch(err => {
        if (!cancelled && err.name !== 'AbortError') {
          setError(err);
          setLoading(false);
        }
      });

    // Step 3: Return cleanup ‚Äî cancel in-flight request on unmount or url change
    return () => {
      cancelled = true;
      controller.abort();
    };
  }, [url]); // Step 4: url as dep ‚Äî re-fetch when url changes

  return { data, loading, error }; // stable return shape
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// ‚úÖ GOOD HOOK 2 ‚Äî useLocalStorage: generalised, reusable
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function useLocalStorage(key, initialValue) {
  // Step 1: Initialise from localStorage with safe fallback
  const [storedValue, setStoredValue] = useState(() => {
    try {
      const item = window.localStorage.getItem(key);
      return item ? JSON.parse(item) : initialValue;
    } catch {
      return initialValue; // if JSON.parse fails or localStorage unavailable
    }
  });

  // Step 2: Setter that syncs state AND localStorage in one call
  const setValue = useCallback((value) => {
    try {
      // Allow functional updates: setValue(prev => prev + 1)
      const valueToStore = value instanceof Function ? value(storedValue) : value;
      setStoredValue(valueToStore);
      window.localStorage.setItem(key, JSON.stringify(valueToStore));
    } catch (error) {
      console.error('useLocalStorage write failed:', error);
    }
  }, [key, storedValue]); // useCallback makes setValue reference stable

  return [storedValue, setValue]; // mirrors useState API ‚Äî easy to swap in
}

// Usage ‚Äî drop-in replacement for useState, with persistence:
function ThemeToggle() {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useLocalStorage('theme', 'light'); // persisted!
  return <button onClick={() => setTheme(t => t === 'light' ? 'dark' : 'light')}>
    {theme}
  </button>;
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// ‚úÖ GOOD HOOK 3 ‚Äî useDebounce: clear name, single purpose, composable
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function useDebounce(value, delay = 300) {
  const [debouncedValue, setDebouncedValue] = useState(value);

  useEffect(() => {
    const timer = setTimeout(() => setDebouncedValue(value), delay);
    // Cleanup: clear timer if value/delay changes before timer fires
    return () => clearTimeout(timer);
  }, [value, delay]);

  return debouncedValue;
}

// Used in composition with useFetch ‚Äî hooks compose cleanly
function SearchResults({ query }) {
  const debouncedQuery = useDebounce(query, 400); // debounce first
  const { data, loading } = useFetch(`/api/search?q=${debouncedQuery}`); // then fetch
  // Two small hooks composed ‚Äî each doing one thing
  return loading ? <Spinner /> : <ResultList items={data} />;
}

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// ‚úÖ GOOD HOOK 4 ‚Äî usePrevious: utility, pure, no side effects
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

function usePrevious(value) {
  const ref = useRef();
  useEffect(() => {
    ref.current = value; // update AFTER render ‚Äî ref holds previous value during render
  });
  return ref.current; // returns the value from the PREVIOUS render
}
```

---

#### Checklist: When to Extract a Custom Hook

```
EXTRACT when:
  ‚ñ° Same useEffect/useState pattern used in 2+ components
  ‚ñ° Logic has a clear name you can describe in 3 words
  ‚ñ° Logic can be tested independently with renderHook()
  ‚ñ° Component becomes cleaner after extraction
  ‚ñ° Logic involves side effects that need careful cleanup

DON'T extract when:
  ‚ñ° Used only once AND is < 10 lines
  ‚ñ° Would require too many parameters (hook entanglement)
  ‚ñ° Breaking it out makes it harder to understand in context
  ‚ñ° The "hook" is just a renamed copy of another hook
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| `useFetch` per call | O(1) | One fetch, one state update cycle |
| `useLocalStorage` read | O(1) | `localStorage.getItem` is O(1) |
| `useDebounce` timer | O(1) | One `setTimeout` + cleanup per value change |
| Multiple hook calls in component | O(K) | K = number of hooks ‚Äî sequential, constant per hook |

---

### Q24. How would you implement a fully accessible modal using Compound Components?

---

#### ELI5 (Explain Like I'm 5)

> An accessible modal is like a room with proper doors for **everyone** ‚Äî sighted users, screen reader users, keyboard users. The doors that matter:
> - Screen readers know it's a "dialog" (ARIA role)
> - Focus gets trapped inside while modal is open (you can't accidentally tab to background content)
> - Pressing Escape closes it
> - When it closes, focus returns to the button that opened it
>
> Building this as Compound Components means: `<Modal>`, `<Modal.Trigger>`, `<Modal.Content>`, `<Modal.Title>`, `<Modal.CloseButton>` ‚Äî all wired up automatically. Users of the component don't need to worry about ARIA or focus management.

---

#### Flowchart ‚Äî Accessibility Requirements

```
WCAG + ARIA requirements for a dialog modal:
‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. role="dialog" on the modal container
  2. aria-modal="true" ‚Äî tells AT it's a modal (background inert)
  3. aria-labelledby ‚Üí points to the modal's <h2> title
  4. aria-describedby ‚Üí optionally points to description text
  5. Focus trap ‚Äî Tab/Shift+Tab cycles ONLY within modal
  6. Escape key ‚Üí closes modal
  7. On open  ‚Üí focus moves to first focusable element OR close button
  8. On close ‚Üí focus returns to the TRIGGER element that opened it
  9. Rendered in a Portal ‚Üí modal not clipped by parent overflow:hidden

FOCUS TRAP logic:
  Modal opens
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  Find all focusable elements inside modal
  [buttons, inputs, links, [tabindex="0"]]
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  Focus first element
       ‚îÇ
  Tab pressed at LAST element  ‚Üí wrap to FIRST
  Shift+Tab at FIRST element   ‚Üí wrap to LAST
  All other Tab presses        ‚Üí normal within modal
```

---

#### Code Example ‚Äî Fully Accessible Compound Modal

```jsx
import React, {
  createContext, useContext, useState, useEffect, useRef,
  useCallback, useId
} from 'react';
import { createPortal } from 'react-dom';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 1: Shared context for modal state ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const ModalContext = createContext(null);

function useModalContext() {
  const ctx = useContext(ModalContext);
  if (!ctx) throw new Error('Modal sub-components must be inside <Modal>');
  return ctx;
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 2: Parent Modal component ‚Äî holds open state ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function Modal({ children, defaultOpen = false }) {
  const [isOpen, setIsOpen] = useState(defaultOpen);
  const triggerRef = useRef(null); // remembers the trigger for focus return
  const titleId    = useId();      // unique ID for aria-labelledby

  const open  = useCallback(() => setIsOpen(true),  []);
  const close = useCallback(() => {
    setIsOpen(false);
    // Step 3: Return focus to trigger after close
    // Without this, screen reader and keyboard user loses their place
    triggerRef.current?.focus();
  }, []);

  const value = { isOpen, open, close, triggerRef, titleId };

  return (
    <ModalContext.Provider value={value}>
      {children}
    </ModalContext.Provider>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 4: Trigger button ‚Äî records itself as the triggering element
function ModalTrigger({ children, asChild = false }) {
  const { open, triggerRef } = useModalContext();

  // Common pattern: asChild lets you use any element as trigger
  return (
    <button
      ref={triggerRef}   // save ref so we can return focus here on close
      onClick={open}
      type="button"
    >
      {children}
    </button>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 5: Overlay backdrop ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ModalOverlay({ onClick }) {
  return (
    <div
      style={{
        position: 'fixed', inset: 0,
        background: 'rgba(0,0,0,0.5)',
        zIndex: 1000,
      }}
      onClick={onClick}          // click outside ‚Üí close
      aria-hidden="true"         // backdrop is decorative ‚Äî hide from AT
    />
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 6: Modal content wrapper ‚Äî the actual dialog ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ModalContent({ children }) {
  const { isOpen, close, titleId } = useModalContext();
  const contentRef = useRef(null);

  // ‚îÄ‚îÄ Focus trap implementation ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  useEffect(() => {
    if (!isOpen) return;

    const el = contentRef.current;
    if (!el) return;

    // Step 7: Find all focusable elements inside the modal
    const focusable = el.querySelectorAll(
      'a[href], button:not([disabled]), textarea, input, select, [tabindex]:not([tabindex="-1"])'
    );
    const first = focusable[0];
    const last  = focusable[focusable.length - 1];

    // Step 8: Focus the first focusable element when modal opens
    first?.focus();

    // Step 9: Trap focus with keydown handler
    const handleKeyDown = (e) => {
      if (e.key === 'Escape') {
        // Escape ‚Üí close modal (WCAG requirement)
        close();
        return;
      }
      if (e.key !== 'Tab') return;

      if (e.shiftKey) {
        // Shift+Tab at first element ‚Üí wrap to last
        if (document.activeElement === first) {
          e.preventDefault();
          last?.focus();
        }
      } else {
        // Tab at last element ‚Üí wrap to first
        if (document.activeElement === last) {
          e.preventDefault();
          first?.focus();
        }
      }
    };

    document.addEventListener('keydown', handleKeyDown);
    return () => document.removeEventListener('keydown', handleKeyDown);
  }, [isOpen, close]);

  if (!isOpen) return null;

  // Step 10: Use createPortal ‚Äî render outside component tree
  // Prevents clipping by parent overflow:hidden / z-index stacking contexts
  return createPortal(
    <>
      <ModalOverlay onClick={close} />
      <div
        ref={contentRef}
        role="dialog"              // ARIA: identifies this as a dialog
        aria-modal="true"          // ARIA: tells AT background is inert
        aria-labelledby={titleId}  // ARIA: links to ModalTitle for AT announcement
        style={{
          position: 'fixed',
          top: '50%', left: '50%',
          transform: 'translate(-50%, -50%)',
          background: '#fff',
          borderRadius: 8, padding: 24,
          zIndex: 1001,
          minWidth: 320,
          outline: 'none',         // visual focus is handled by inner elements
        }}
      >
        {children}
      </div>
    </>,
    document.body                  // portal target
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 11: Modal title ‚Äî referenced by aria-labelledby ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ModalTitle({ children }) {
  const { titleId } = useModalContext();
  // id={titleId} connects this to aria-labelledby on the dialog
  // Screen reader announces this when modal opens
  return <h2 id={titleId} style={{ marginTop: 0 }}>{children}</h2>;
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Step 12: Close button ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function ModalCloseButton({ children = 'Close' }) {
  const { close } = useModalContext();
  return (
    <button
      onClick={close}
      type="button"
      aria-label="Close dialog"    // explicit label for screen readers
      style={{ position: 'absolute', top: 12, right: 12 }}
    >
      {children}
    </button>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Attach sub-components ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
Modal.Trigger     = ModalTrigger;
Modal.Content     = ModalContent;
Modal.Title       = ModalTitle;
Modal.CloseButton = ModalCloseButton;

// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
// USAGE ‚Äî clean API, all a11y handled automatically
// ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
function DeleteConfirmDialog({ onConfirm }) {
  return (
    <Modal>
      {/* Trigger: focus is saved here for return on close */}
      <Modal.Trigger>Delete Account</Modal.Trigger>

      <Modal.Content>
        {/* Title: read by screen reader when dialog opens */}
        <Modal.Title>Confirm Deletion</Modal.Title>
        <Modal.CloseButton>‚úï</Modal.CloseButton>

        <p id="delete-desc">This action cannot be undone. Are you sure?</p>

        <div style={{ display: 'flex', gap: 8, marginTop: 16 }}>
          <button onClick={onConfirm} style={{ background: 'red', color: '#fff' }}>
            Yes, Delete
          </button>
          {/* Both buttons inside modal ‚Äî Tab cycles between them */}
          <Modal.CloseButton>Cancel</Modal.CloseButton>
        </div>
      </Modal.Content>
    </Modal>
  );
}
```

---

#### Step-by-Step Explanation

| Step | Code | Why |
|------|------|-----|
| 1 | `ModalContext` | Shared channel for `isOpen`, `open`, `close`, `titleId` ‚Äî no prop drilling |
| 2 | `triggerRef` | Saved reference to trigger element ‚Äî enables focus return on close |
| 3 | `triggerRef.current?.focus()` on close | WCAG 2.1 SC 3.2.2 ‚Äî focus must return to triggering element |
| 4 | `ref={triggerRef}` on trigger | Captures the DOM node of the opener before modal is shown |
| 5 | `focusable` selector | Finds all keyboard-reachable elements inside the modal |
| 6 | `first?.focus()` on mount | ARIA pattern ‚Äî focus must move into dialog when it opens |
| 7 | `keydown` ‚Üí Escape | ARIA dialog pattern requirement ‚Äî Escape closes the dialog |
| 8 | Tab wrapping (first/last) | Focus trap ‚Äî prevents tabbing into background content |
| 9 | `createPortal(‚Ä¶, document.body)` | Avoids CSS stacking context issues ‚Äî modal always on top |
| 10 | `role="dialog"` + `aria-modal="true"` | Screen readers announce it as a dialog; `aria-modal` hides background |
| 11 | `aria-labelledby={titleId}` | Screen reader reads title immediately when dialog opens |
| 12 | `useId()` for `titleId` | React 18 ‚Äî generates stable unique ID safe for SSR |

---

#### ARIA Attributes Summary

```
  role="dialog"          ‚Üí "This is a dialog" to screen readers
  aria-modal="true"      ‚Üí "Background content is inert"
  aria-labelledby="id"   ‚Üí "Title of this dialog is element with this ID"
  aria-describedby="id"  ‚Üí "Description of this dialog" (optional)
  aria-label="Close"     ‚Üí Explicit label for icon-only buttons
```

---

#### Time & Space Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Why |
|-----------|-----------|-----|
| `querySelectorAll` for focusable | O(N) | N = DOM nodes inside modal ‚Äî typically very small |
| `keydown` listener | O(1) per event | Just checks `activeElement` === first/last |
| `createPortal` | O(1) | Inserts one child into `document.body` |
| Focus trap setup/teardown | O(1) | One `addEventListener` / `removeEventListener` |

---

## End of Section: REACT ‚Äî Patterns (Q18‚ÄìQ24)

---

# REACT ‚Äî Advanced (Q25‚ÄìQ31)

---

## Q25: What is Isomorphic / Universal React? How does hydration work?

### üßí ELI5
Imagine a chef (server) prepares a beautiful cake and takes a photo of it (HTML). That photo is what you see instantly. Then the actual cake (JavaScript) arrives and you can now touch and eat it. **Hydration** is the moment the real cake arrives and matches the photo ‚Äî everything becomes interactive.

### üìä Diagram

```
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ                    SERVER                            ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  React renders components ‚Üí produces HTML string     ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  renderToString(<App />) ‚Üí "<div class='app'>..."    ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
                       ‚îÇ  HTML sent over network (fast first paint)
                       ‚ñº
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ                    BROWSER                           ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  1. Receives HTML ‚Üí paints immediately (no blank)    ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  2. Downloads JS bundle                              ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  3. React calls hydrateRoot(<App />)                 ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ     ‚îú‚îÄ Walks existing DOM (doesn't re-create it)     ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ     ‚îú‚îÄ Attaches event listeners to each node         ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ     ‚îî‚îÄ React takes control ‚Üí app is now interactive  ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

  KEY DIFFERENCE vs CSR:
  CSR: <div id="root"></div>  ‚Üí JS runs ‚Üí creates all DOM
  SSR: Full HTML from server  ‚Üí JS runs ‚Üí attaches to DOM (hydration)
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ server.js (Node/Express) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { renderToString } from 'react-dom/server';
import App from './App';

app.get('*', (req, res) => {
  // Step 1: render React tree to static HTML string on the server
  const html = renderToString(<App />);

  res.send(`
    <!DOCTYPE html>
    <html>
      <body>
        <!-- Step 2: inject server-rendered HTML into the root div -->
        <div id="root">${html}</div>

        <!-- Step 3: ship the JS bundle to the browser -->
        <script src="/bundle.js"></script>
      </body>
    </html>
  `);
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ client.js (runs in browser) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { hydrateRoot } from 'react-dom/client';
import App from './App';

// Step 4: React walks the existing DOM and attaches event listeners
// It does NOT tear down and rebuild ‚Äî it reuses every node
hydrateRoot(document.getElementById('root'), <App />);
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`renderToString`** ‚Äî React runs your component tree on the server (no browser APIs available); outputs a plain HTML string with `data-reactroot` markers.
2. **HTML shipped to browser** ‚Äî User sees real content immediately (good FCP/LCP score) before any JS runs.
3. **JS bundle downloads** ‚Äî This is the same `<App />` component code, now running in the browser.
4. **`hydrateRoot`** ‚Äî React walks the server-rendered DOM and compares it to what the virtual DOM would produce. If they match, it simply attaches event handlers. No re-painting.
5. **Interactive** ‚Äî After hydration, the app behaves like a normal CSR React app.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Metric | Value | Reason |
|--------|-------|--------|
| Time to First Byte (TTFB) | Depends on server | Server must render before sending |
| First Contentful Paint (FCP) | Fast | HTML arrives before JS |
| Time to Interactive (TTI) | Slower than pure CSR | Must wait for JS + hydration pass |
| Hydration pass | O(N) | N = number of DOM nodes |

---

## Q26: What causes a hydration mismatch and how do you fix it?

### üßí ELI5
If the cook's photo (server HTML) shows a chocolate cake but the actual cake (client render) is vanilla, there's a mismatch. React panics: "These don't match! I'll throw away the server work and rebuild from scratch." ‚Äî That wastes all the SSR benefit.

### üìä Diagram

```
  COMMON MISMATCH SOURCES
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. Date/Time:
     Server:  "Rendered at 10:00:00"
     Client:  "Rendered at 10:00:01"   ‚Üê different!

  2. window / localStorage access:
     Server:  window is undefined ‚Üí crashes or empty value
     Client:  actual window object

  3. Random values:
     Server:  Math.random() === 0.42
     Client:  Math.random() === 0.87

  4. User locale / timezone:
     Server:  running in UTC
     Client:  user in UTC+5:30

  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  REACT 18 BEHAVIOUR:
  ‚îî‚îÄ In dev: throws hydration error with diff
  ‚îî‚îÄ In prod: silently re-renders from client (defeats SSR)
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚ùå BAD ‚Äî causes mismatch
function Timestamp() {
  return <p>Loaded at: {new Date().toLocaleTimeString()}</p>;
  // Server renders "10:00:00", client renders "10:00:01"
}

// ‚úÖ FIX 1: useEffect ‚Äî run only on client after hydration
function Timestamp() {
  const [time, setTime] = useState('');   // Step 1: empty string on both server and client first render

  useEffect(() => {
    // Step 2: runs ONLY in browser, after hydration ‚Äî no mismatch
    setTime(new Date().toLocaleTimeString());
  }, []);

  return <p>Loaded at: {time}</p>;        // Step 3: consistent initial render
}

// ‚úÖ FIX 2: suppressHydrationWarning (for intentional differences)
function ServerTime({ serverTime }) {
  return (
    // Step 1: suppress React's warning for this single element
    <time suppressHydrationWarning>
      {serverTime}
    </time>
  );
  // Use sparingly ‚Äî only when you KNOW the content will differ
}

// ‚úÖ FIX 3: Next.js dynamic import with ssr:false (client-only component)
import dynamic from 'next/dynamic';

// Step 1: Next won't render this on server at all ‚Äî no mismatch possible
const ClientOnlyChart = dynamic(() => import('./Chart'), { ssr: false });

// ‚úÖ FIX 4: Explicit client-only guard
function ThemeToggle() {
  const [mounted, setMounted] = useState(false);

  useEffect(() => { setMounted(true); }, []);

  // Step 1: return null on server (no HTML for this) AND on first client paint
  if (!mounted) return null;

  // Step 2: only renders after hydration ‚Äî reads localStorage safely
  return <button>{localStorage.getItem('theme') === 'dark' ? 'üåô' : '‚òÄÔ∏è'}</button>;
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Root cause** ‚Äî Server and client execute the same render function but in different environments; any environment-specific value produces different output.
2. **`useEffect` guard** ‚Äî `useEffect` never runs on the server, so initialising state to a neutral value and setting it in `useEffect` guarantees server = client on first render.
3. **`suppressHydrationWarning`** ‚Äî Tells React "I know this element will differ, ignore it." Only applies to that element, not its children.
4. **`ssr: false`** ‚Äî Next.js skips SSR entirely for that component; it only mounts on the client. Safest for components that heavily depend on browser APIs.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Scenario | Cost | Impact |
|----------|------|--------|
| Mismatch in dev | Warning + re-render | Developer overhead |
| Mismatch in prod | Full client re-render | Loses all SSR benefit (O(N) wasted) |
| `suppressHydrationWarning` | O(1) | Skips diff for one node |
| `ssr: false` | No server render | Component not in initial HTML |

---

## Q27: What are React Server Components? How do they differ from SSR?

### üßí ELI5
SSR is like a restaurant that cooks your meal in the kitchen (server) but then ships the entire kitchen to your table so you can reheat later. RSC is like a restaurant that cooks the parts that never change in the kitchen ‚Äî and only ships the interactive parts to your table. Much lighter delivery!

### üìä Diagram

```
  TRADITIONAL SSR
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Server: renders HTML of ENTIRE app
  Ships:  HTML + FULL JS bundle (every component)
  Client: hydrates everything ‚Äî even static content

  REACT SERVER COMPONENTS (RSC)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Server Components (*.server.jsx / no "use client")
  ‚îú‚îÄ Run ONLY on server
  ‚îú‚îÄ Can be async ‚Äî await fetch(), await db.query()
  ‚îú‚îÄ Zero JS sent to client
  ‚îî‚îÄ Cannot use: useState, useEffect, event handlers

  Client Components ("use client" directive)
  ‚îú‚îÄ Can use hooks, events, browser APIs
  ‚îú‚îÄ Hydrated on client
  ‚îî‚îÄ JS IS sent to browser

  COMPOSITION:
  <Page>                      ‚Üê Server Component (0 KB to client)
    <Sidebar />               ‚Üê Server Component (0 KB to client)
    <ArticleBody />           ‚Üê Server Component (0 KB to client)
    <LikeButton />            ‚Üê Client Component (JS shipped)
    <CommentThread />         ‚Üê Server Component with async data
  </Page>

  RESULT: Only <LikeButton/> JS reaches the browser
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ app/page.tsx (Server Component ‚Äî no "use client") ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

// Step 1: This function can be async ‚Äî no useEffect needed
export default async function BlogPost({ params }) {
  // Step 2: Direct DB/API access on server ‚Äî no fetch boilerplate in client
  const post = await db.posts.findById(params.id);
  const author = await db.users.findById(post.authorId);

  // Step 3: Render ‚Äî this HTML is sent to client; component code is NOT
  return (
    <article>
      <h1>{post.title}</h1>
      <p>By {author.name}</p>
      <div dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: post.renderedMarkdown }} />

      {/* Step 4: Client Component for interactivity ‚Äî JS IS sent */}
      <LikeButton postId={post.id} initialLikes={post.likes} />
    </article>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ components/LikeButton.tsx (Client Component) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
'use client'; // Step 5: Marks this as a Client Component

import { useState } from 'react';

export default function LikeButton({ postId, initialLikes }) {
  // Step 6: useState works here ‚Äî runs on client
  const [likes, setLikes] = useState(initialLikes);

  async function handleLike() {
    setLikes(l => l + 1);          // Step 7: optimistic update
    await fetch(`/api/posts/${postId}/like`, { method: 'POST' });
  }

  return <button onClick={handleLike}>‚ù§Ô∏è {likes}</button>;
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **No `useEffect` data fetching** ‚Äî RSC can be `async`; `await` directly in the component body. No loading states needed for initial data.
2. **Zero bundle cost** ‚Äî `BlogPost` component code never reaches the browser. The only JS shipped is `LikeButton`.
3. **`"use client"` boundary** ‚Äî Everything below this boundary in the component tree is a Client Component and will be hydrated.
4. **Server Components can pass serialisable props to Client Components** ‚Äî You cannot pass functions or class instances across the boundary.
5. **RSC vs SSR** ‚Äî SSR produces HTML on server but still hydrates full app JS. RSC additionally eliminates component code from the bundle entirely.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Metric | SSR | RSC |
|--------|-----|-----|
| JS bundle size | Full app | Only client components |
| Data fetching | `getServerSideProps` + client fetch | `async` component directly |
| Interactivity | Hydrate everything | Hydrate only `"use client"` subtrees |
| Component code to client | All components | Only client-marked components |

---

## Q28: What is an Error Boundary? Why must it be a class component?

### üßí ELI5
Imagine each section of a newspaper in a separate fireproof box. If one section catches fire, the box contains it ‚Äî the rest of the newspaper is fine. An Error Boundary is React's fireproof box: it catches render errors inside it and shows a fallback instead of crashing the whole app.

### üìä Diagram

```
  WITHOUT ERROR BOUNDARY             WITH ERROR BOUNDARY
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ             ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <App>                              <App>
    <Header />      ‚úÖ                <Header />        ‚úÖ
    <Dashboard>                       <ErrorBoundary>
      <Chart />     üí• throws           <Dashboard>
        ‚Üì                                 <Chart />     üí• throws
    ENTIRE APP                              ‚Üì
    white screen                        ErrorBoundary catches it
                                        Shows <FallbackUI />
                                       </Dashboard>
                                       </ErrorBoundary>
                                    <Footer />        ‚úÖ
                                   </App>
                                   Rest of app still works!

  WHAT IT CATCHES:              WHAT IT DOES NOT CATCH:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ             ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚Ä¢ Render errors               ‚Ä¢ Event handlers (use try/catch)
  ‚Ä¢ Constructor errors          ‚Ä¢ Async code (setTimeout, fetch)
  ‚Ä¢ Lifecycle method errors     ‚Ä¢ Errors in the boundary itself
  ‚Ä¢ Errors in child tree        ‚Ä¢ SSR errors
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import React from 'react';

// Step 1: Must be a CLASS component ‚Äî no functional equivalent exists
class ErrorBoundary extends React.Component {
  constructor(props) {
    super(props);
    // Step 2: state tracks whether an error has been caught
    this.state = { hasError: false, error: null };
  }

  // Step 3: static lifecycle ‚Äî called during render phase when child throws
  // Returns new state to trigger fallback render
  static getDerivedStateFromError(error) {
    return { hasError: true, error };
  }

  // Step 4: called after render ‚Äî use for logging/reporting
  componentDidCatch(error, info) {
    // info.componentStack shows which component threw
    console.error('ErrorBoundary caught:', error, info.componentStack);
    // Report to Sentry, Datadog, etc.
    logErrorToService(error, info);
  }

  render() {
    if (this.state.hasError) {
      // Step 5: render fallback UI ‚Äî can use this.props.fallback for custom UI
      return this.props.fallback ?? (
        <div role="alert">
          <h2>Something went wrong.</h2>
          {/* Step 6: allow user to reset the boundary and retry */}
          <button onClick={() => this.setState({ hasError: false, error: null })}>
            Try Again
          </button>
        </div>
      );
    }

    // Step 7: no error ‚Äî render children normally
    return this.props.children;
  }
}

// Usage
function App() {
  return (
    <ErrorBoundary fallback={<p>Chart failed to load</p>}>
      <Chart data={data} />   {/* if this throws, boundary catches it */}
    </ErrorBoundary>
  );
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Why class?** ‚Äî Two lifecycle methods required: `getDerivedStateFromError` (sync, during render) and `componentDidCatch` (after render, for side effects). React's hooks model runs synchronously during render and cannot replicate this two-phase behaviour. As of React 19, a `use` hook-based boundary is being explored but hasn't shipped.
2. **`getDerivedStateFromError`** ‚Äî Static (no `this`), pure function; React uses its return value to update state and trigger a re-render with the fallback.
3. **`componentDidCatch`** ‚Äî Has access to `this`; used for side effects (logging). Called in the "commit" phase.
4. **Granularity** ‚Äî Wrap individual widgets, not the entire app; lets healthy parts stay functional.
5. **Libraries** ‚Äî `react-error-boundary` package provides a functional-looking API that wraps the class internally.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Reason |
|-----------|-----------|--------|
| `getDerivedStateFromError` | O(1) | Sets state flag |
| `componentDidCatch` | O(1) | Logs once per error |
| Re-render fallback | O(1) | Replaces subtree with fallback |
| Stack trace parsing | O(D) | D = component tree depth |

---

## Q29: What are React Portals? When would you use them?

### üßí ELI5
Your bedroom (React component tree) is inside a house. When you yell, your voice travels through the house's walls ‚Äî that's React event bubbling. But a Portal is like a teleporter: it places your content directly in the garden (DOM body), while your voice still travels back through the house. Content is elsewhere in the DOM, events still flow through React.

### üìä Diagram

```
  WITHOUT PORTAL:
  <App>                        DOM:
    <Modal>                    <div id="root">
      <div class="modal">        <div class="app">
        Stuck inside               <div class="modal">   ‚Üê z-index issues
        overflow:hidden            </div>               ‚Üê clipped by parent
      </div>                     </div>
    </Modal>                   </div>
  </App>

  WITH PORTAL:
  <App>                        DOM:
    <Modal>                    <div id="root">
      createPortal(              <div class="app">
        <div class="modal">,       ...no modal here...
        document.body             </div>
      )                        </div>
    </Modal>                   <div class="modal">  ‚Üê sits at body level
  </App>                         free from overflow/z-index constraints
                               </div>

  EVENT BUBBLING:
  Click inside modal
    ‚Üí bubbles up through REACT tree (App ‚Üí Modal ‚Üí ...)  ‚úÖ
    ‚Üí NOT through DOM tree (body ‚Üí ...)                  ‚úÖ
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import { createPortal } from 'react-dom';
import { useEffect, useRef } from 'react';

// Step 1: Modal component ‚Äî lives in React tree but renders outside DOM root
function Modal({ isOpen, onClose, children }) {
  const overlayRef = useRef(null);

  // Step 2: handle click-outside to close
  function handleOverlayClick(e) {
    // Only close if clicking the backdrop, not the inner content
    if (e.target === overlayRef.current) onClose();
  }

  // Step 3: close on Escape key
  useEffect(() => {
    function onKeyDown(e) {
      if (e.key === 'Escape') onClose();
    }
    if (isOpen) document.addEventListener('keydown', onKeyDown);
    return () => document.removeEventListener('keydown', onKeyDown);
  }, [isOpen, onClose]);

  if (!isOpen) return null;

  // Step 4: createPortal renders JSX into a DIFFERENT DOM node
  return createPortal(
    <div
      ref={overlayRef}
      className="modal-overlay"
      onClick={handleOverlayClick}
      style={{
        position: 'fixed', inset: 0,          // Step 5: covers full viewport
        background: 'rgba(0,0,0,0.5)',
        display: 'grid', placeItems: 'center',
        zIndex: 1000,
      }}
    >
      <div className="modal-content" role="dialog" aria-modal="true">
        {children}
      </div>
    </div>,
    document.body   // Step 6: target DOM node ‚Äî outside #root
  );
}

// Usage
function App() {
  const [open, setOpen] = useState(false);

  return (
    <div style={{ overflow: 'hidden' }}>  {/* this would clip non-portal modals */}
      <button onClick={() => setOpen(true)}>Open Modal</button>

      {/* Portal escapes the overflow:hidden parent */}
      <Modal isOpen={open} onClose={() => setOpen(false)}>
        <h2>Hello from Portal!</h2>
      </Modal>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`createPortal(children, container)`** ‚Äî First arg is JSX; second is any DOM node. React renders the JSX there instead of in the normal component location.
2. **Event bubbling** ‚Äî React events still bubble through the React component tree (not the DOM tree). An `onClick` on the portal content will bubble up through `<App>` as expected.
3. **Use cases** ‚Äî Modals, tooltips, dropdown menus, toast notifications ‚Äî anything that needs to escape `overflow: hidden`, `transform`, or `z-index` stacking contexts of ancestors.
4. **Context** ‚Äî Portals remain inside the React tree; `useContext`, Redux store, etc. still work normally.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Reason |
|-----------|-----------|--------|
| `createPortal` | O(1) | Single DOM `appendChild` |
| Event capture | O(D) | D = React tree depth (bubbling) |
| Modal render | O(C) | C = children in modal |

---

## Q30: What is the difference between SSR, SSG, and ISR in Next.js?

### üßí ELI5
**SSG** = Print a newspaper once at 6am; everyone gets the same copy.
**SSR** = Print a custom newspaper for each reader when they ask.
**ISR** = Print a newspaper at 6am, but reprint individual articles when they go stale ‚Äî without reprinting the whole paper.

### üìä Diagram

```
  SSG (Static Site Generation)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Build time:  React renders ‚Üí saves as .html files
  Request:     Serve static file from CDN (fastest!)
  Revalidate:  Only on next `next build`
  API:         getStaticProps / page.tsx with no dynamic

  SSR (Server-Side Rendering)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Build time:  Nothing pre-rendered
  Request:     Node server runs getServerSideProps ‚Üí renders HTML
  Revalidate:  Every single request (always fresh)
  API:         getServerSideProps / route with dynamic = 'force-dynamic'

  ISR (Incremental Static Regeneration)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Build time:  Pre-renders known pages (like SSG)
  Request:     Serves stale HTML; triggers background rebuild
  Revalidate:  After `revalidate` seconds (stale-while-revalidate)
  API:         getStaticProps + revalidate: N  /  next: { revalidate: N }

  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ         ‚îÇ Freshness‚îÇ  Speed     ‚îÇ Use Case             ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îÇ SSG     ‚îÇ Stale    ‚îÇ Fastest    ‚îÇ Docs, blogs, marketing‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ SSR     ‚îÇ Always   ‚îÇ Slowest    ‚îÇ User dashboards, auth ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ ISR     ‚îÇ Near-    ‚îÇ Fast + CDN ‚îÇ E-commerce, news      ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ         ‚îÇ fresh    ‚îÇ            ‚îÇ                       ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ SSG: getStaticProps (Pages Router) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Step 1: runs at BUILD TIME only; output is a static .html file
export async function getStaticProps() {
  const posts = await fetchAllBlogPosts();
  return { props: { posts } };
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ SSR: getServerSideProps (Pages Router) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Step 1: runs on EVERY REQUEST on the server
export async function getServerSideProps(context) {
  const user = await getUser(context.req.cookies.token); // Step 2: can read request
  const data = await fetchPersonalisedDashboard(user.id);
  return { props: { data } };
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ ISR: getStaticProps + revalidate (Pages Router) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
export async function getStaticProps({ params }) {
  const product = await fetchProduct(params.id);
  return {
    props: { product },
    // Step 1: after 60 seconds, next request triggers background rebuild
    // Visitor gets stale page; rebuilt page served to next visitor
    revalidate: 60,
  };
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ App Router equivalents (Next.js 13+) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

// SSG: default behaviour ‚Äî fetch is cached at build time
async function Page() {
  const data = await fetch('https://api.example.com/posts');  // cached
  // ...
}

// SSR: opt out of caching
async function Page() {
  const data = await fetch('https://api.example.com/posts', {
    cache: 'no-store',    // Step 1: fetch on every request
  });
}

// ISR: revalidate after N seconds
async function Page() {
  const data = await fetch('https://api.example.com/posts', {
    next: { revalidate: 60 },   // Step 1: stale-while-revalidate
  });
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **SSG** ‚Äî Pages are HTML files in the `.next/static` folder after build. CDN caches them forever (until next deploy). Best performance, but data can be stale.
2. **SSR** ‚Äî Every request hits your Node server. Fresh data, but adds server latency. Don't cache on CDN (content is per-request).
3. **ISR** ‚Äî Uses stale-while-revalidate: serve the cached HTML immediately, then rebuild in the background if the revalidation window has passed. Best of both worlds for content that changes occasionally.
4. **On-demand ISR** ‚Äî `revalidatePath('/blog/[slug]')` or `revalidateTag('posts')` lets you purge the cache programmatically (e.g., on a CMS webhook).

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Strategy | TTFB | Server Load | Data Freshness |
|----------|------|-------------|----------------|
| SSG | < 10ms (CDN) | O(1) per request | Stale until rebuild |
| SSR | 100‚Äì500ms | O(1) per request (but always runs) | Always fresh |
| ISR | < 10ms (CDN hit) | O(1) background only | Stale by ‚â§ revalidate seconds |

---

## Q31: How does `Suspense` work for data fetching vs code splitting?

### üßí ELI5
`Suspense` is a "loading screen" instruction. For **code splitting** it says "wait until the code file downloads." For **data fetching** it says "wait until the data promise resolves." In both cases, the parent shows a spinner (fallback) and the child appears when ready.

### üìä Diagram

```
  CODE SPLITTING
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  React.lazy(() => import('./HeavyChart'))
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº
  <Suspense fallback={<Spinner />}>    ‚Üê shows while JS downloads
    <HeavyChart />
  </Suspense>
       ‚îÇ
  JS bundle chunk requested ‚Üí downloaded ‚Üí component mounts

  DATA FETCHING (React 18 use() hook)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  const promise = fetchUser(id);       ‚Üê starts outside render

  function UserCard() {
    const user = use(promise);         ‚Üê throws promise if pending
  }                                    ‚Üê React catches the throw

  <Suspense fallback={<Skeleton />}>   ‚Üê shows while data resolves
    <UserCard />
  </Suspense>
       ‚îÇ
  Promise resolves ‚Üí React re-renders UserCard ‚Üí shows data

  NESTED SUSPENSE (waterfall avoidance)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <Suspense fallback={<PageSkeleton />}>      ‚Üê outer
    <Header />
    <Suspense fallback={<ArticleSkeleton />}> ‚Üê inner
      <Article />                              
    </Suspense>
    <Suspense fallback={<SidebarSkeleton />}> ‚Üê inner
      <Sidebar />                              ‚Üê loads in parallel
    </Suspense>
  </Suspense>
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import { Suspense, lazy, use } from 'react';

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Code Splitting with React.lazy ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

// Step 1: lazy() wraps a dynamic import ‚Äî chunk is only loaded when needed
const HeavyDashboard = lazy(() => import('./HeavyDashboard'));

function App() {
  const [show, setShow] = useState(false);

  return (
    <>
      <button onClick={() => setShow(true)}>Load Dashboard</button>

      {/* Step 2: fallback shown while JS chunk downloads */}
      <Suspense fallback={<div>Loading dashboard...</div>}>
        {show && <HeavyDashboard />}
      </Suspense>
    </>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Data Fetching with React 18 use() hook ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

// Step 1: create promise OUTSIDE the component (not inside useEffect)
// This avoids creating a new promise on every render
function fetchUser(id) {
  return fetch(`/api/users/${id}`).then(r => r.json());
}

// Step 2: cache promises to avoid re-fetch on re-render
const userCache = new Map();
function getUserPromise(id) {
  if (!userCache.has(id)) {
    userCache.set(id, fetchUser(id));
  }
  return userCache.get(id);
}

// Step 3: Component uses use() ‚Äî suspends until promise resolves
function UserCard({ id }) {
  // use() throws the promise if pending; React catches it with nearest Suspense
  const user = use(getUserPromise(id));
  return <div>{user.name}</div>;
}

// Step 4: Wrap in Suspense ‚Äî handles both loading and error states
function App() {
  return (
    <ErrorBoundary fallback={<p>Failed to load user</p>}>
      <Suspense fallback={<p>Loading user...</p>}>
        <UserCard id={42} />
      </Suspense>
    </ErrorBoundary>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Server Components + Suspense (Next.js App Router) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Step 5: async server components integrate naturally with Suspense
async function SlowData() {
  const data = await fetch('https://slow-api.example.com/data');
  const json = await data.json();
  return <pre>{JSON.stringify(json, null, 2)}</pre>;
}

export default function Page() {
  return (
    <Suspense fallback={<p>Fetching slow data...</p>}>
      <SlowData />   {/* Next.js automatically suspends async components */}
    </Suspense>
  );
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Mechanism** ‚Äî Suspense works because React catches thrown Promises in the render phase. When a component throws a Promise, React renders the nearest `<Suspense>` fallback and subscribes to the Promise. When it resolves, React re-renders the suspended subtree.
2. **Code splitting** ‚Äî `React.lazy` wraps a dynamic `import()` which returns a Promise. The first render throws this Promise; Suspense shows the fallback; when the chunk downloads, React re-renders.
3. **`use()` hook (React 18)** ‚Äî `use(promise)` is the first hook that can be called conditionally. It reads the resolved value or throws the Promise if still pending.
4. **Parallel loading** ‚Äî Nested `<Suspense>` boundaries let siblings load in parallel. Each boundary independently handles its loading state.
5. **Error handling** ‚Äî Always pair `<Suspense>` with an `<ErrorBoundary>` above it; rejected promises propagate to the Error Boundary.
6. **Old pattern (render-as-you-fetch)** ‚Äî Libraries like SWR/React Query use their own Suspense mode (`suspense: true`). Under the hood they throw cached Promises.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Scenario | Load Sequence | Complexity |
|----------|--------------|-----------|
| Sequential (no Suspense) | A then B then C | O(A+B+C) time |
| Parallel Suspense boundaries | A, B, C in parallel | O(max(A,B,C)) time |
| Code split chunk | O(bundle size / bandwidth) | Network bound |
| `use()` re-render on resolve | O(subtree size) | Minimal |

---

## End of Section: REACT ‚Äî Advanced (Q25‚ÄìQ31)

# REACT ‚Äî Ecosystem (Q32‚ÄìQ38)

---

## Q32: What is the difference between `queryKey`, `staleTime`, and `cacheTime` in React Query?

### üßí ELI5
**`queryKey`** is the name tag on a jar in the fridge ‚Äî it identifies what's inside so you can find it again. **`staleTime`** is "how long until the food is considered old" ‚Äî while fresh, nobody goes back to the shop. **`cacheTime`** is "how long the empty jar stays on the shelf before being thrown away" ‚Äî even after you stop using it, the data lingers for a while in case you need it again soon.

### üìä Diagram

