```
  queryKey: ['todos', { status: 'open', page: 1 }]
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚Ä¢ Unique cache key ‚Äî every distinct key = independent cache entry
  ‚Ä¢ Array form allows granular invalidation:
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['todos'] })
      ‚Üí invalidates ALL queries whose key starts with ['todos']

  staleTime (default: 0)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  0ms ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ fresh ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ [staleTime ms] ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ stale
  ‚Ä¢ While FRESH: component re-mount does NOT trigger a new network request
  ‚Ä¢ Once STALE: next mount / window refocus / network reconnect ‚Üí refetch
  ‚Ä¢ staleTime: Infinity ‚Üí never refetch automatically (static data, e.g. config)

  cacheTime (TanStack v5: gcTime, default: 5 minutes)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Query becomes inactive (no subscribers)
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº cacheTime timer starts
  [cacheTime ms passes]
       ‚îÇ
       ‚ñº garbage collected from cache
  
  INTERACTION:
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇstaleTime ‚îÇ cacheTime  ‚îÇ Behaviour                          ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îÇ 0        ‚îÇ 5 min      ‚îÇ Always refetch on mount, but cached‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ          ‚îÇ            ‚îÇ data shown instantly (background)  ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îÇ 30s      ‚îÇ 5 min      ‚îÇ No refetch if mounted < 30s ago    ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îÇ Infinity ‚îÇ Infinity   ‚îÇ Fetch once, never refetch/GC       ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import { useQuery, useQueryClient } from '@tanstack/react-query';

// Step 1: queryKey as array ‚Äî supports partial matching for invalidation
const { data: todos } = useQuery({
  queryKey: ['todos', { status: 'open', page: currentPage }],
  queryFn: () => fetchTodos({ status: 'open', page: currentPage }),

  // Step 2: staleTime ‚Äî consider data fresh for 30 seconds
  // Re-mounting this component within 30s won't trigger a network request
  staleTime: 30_000,

  // Step 3: gcTime (v5) / cacheTime (v4) ‚Äî keep inactive cache for 10 minutes
  // If no component subscribes for 10 min, the entry is garbage collected
  gcTime: 10 * 60 * 1000,
});

// Step 4: targeted invalidation using partial key matching
const queryClient = useQueryClient();

function invalidateAllTodos() {
  // Invalidates ['todos', { status: 'open' }] AND ['todos', { status: 'done' }]
  // because they all start with ['todos']
  queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['todos'] });
}

function prefetchNextPage() {
  // Step 5: prefetch into cache before user navigates
  queryClient.prefetchQuery({
    queryKey: ['todos', { status: 'open', page: currentPage + 1 }],
    queryFn: () => fetchTodos({ status: 'open', page: currentPage + 1 }),
    staleTime: 30_000,
  });
}

// Step 6: global defaults ‚Äî set once in QueryClient
const queryClient = new QueryClient({
  defaultOptions: {
    queries: {
      staleTime: 60_000,   // 1 min default freshness
      gcTime: 5 * 60_000,  // 5 min default GC
      retry: 2,            // retry failed requests twice
    },
  },
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`queryKey`** ‚Äî Serialised to a stable string internally. Two queries with identical keys share the same cache slot. Array format lets you group related queries by prefix for bulk invalidation.
2. **`staleTime`** ‚Äî Controls "do I need fresh data?" A high `staleTime` reduces network requests; good for reference data that rarely changes (country list, config).
3. **`gcTime` / `cacheTime`** ‚Äî Controls "how long to keep the data in memory after nobody is using it." Keeps the cache warm for quick navigation back to a page.
4. **v5 rename** ‚Äî TanStack Query v5 renamed `cacheTime` ‚Üí `gcTime` to reduce confusion (because `staleTime` and `cacheTime` were commonly mixed up).

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Reason |
|-----------|-----------|--------|
| Cache lookup by key | O(1) | Hash map internally |
| Partial key invalidation | O(K) | K = number of cached queries |
| GC sweep | O(K) | Iterates all inactive entries |

---

## Q33: How do you implement optimistic updates in React Query?

### üßí ELI5
You send a text message and your chat app shows it immediately (grey tick) before the server confirms. If the server fails, the message disappears with an error. That's an **optimistic update** ‚Äî assume success, show the result instantly, roll back on failure.

### üìä Diagram

```
  USER ACTION: "Like this post"
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. onMutate:
     ‚îú‚îÄ Cancel in-flight fetches (avoid overwrite)
     ‚îú‚îÄ Snapshot current cache value
     ‚îî‚îÄ Immediately update cache ‚Üí UI shows liked ‚ù§Ô∏è

  2. Network request fires in background

  3a. onSuccess:
     ‚îî‚îÄ Invalidate query ‚Üí refetch real server value
        (keeps cache in sync with truth)

  3b. onError:
     ‚îî‚îÄ Restore snapshot ‚Üí UI reverts to not-liked ü§ç
        Show error toast

  TIMELINE:
  t=0  ‚îÄ‚îÄ onMutate (instant UI update)
  t=50 ‚îÄ‚îÄ network request in flight
  t=200 ‚îÄ‚îÄ onSuccess ‚Üí invalidate ‚Üí background refetch
         OR
  t=200 ‚îÄ‚îÄ onError ‚Üí rollback to snapshot
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import { useMutation, useQueryClient } from '@tanstack/react-query';

function useLikePost() {
  const queryClient = useQueryClient();

  return useMutation({
    mutationFn: (postId) => fetch(`/api/posts/${postId}/like`, { method: 'POST' }),

    // Step 1: runs BEFORE the network request ‚Äî optimistic update happens here
    onMutate: async (postId) => {
      // Step 2: cancel any outgoing refetches so they don't overwrite our optimistic update
      await queryClient.cancelQueries({ queryKey: ['posts'] });

      // Step 3: snapshot the current value so we can roll back on error
      const previousPosts = queryClient.getQueryData(['posts']);

      // Step 4: optimistically update the cache immediately
      queryClient.setQueryData(['posts'], (old) =>
        old.map((post) =>
          post.id === postId
            ? { ...post, likes: post.likes + 1, liked: true }
            : post
        )
      );

      // Step 5: return snapshot as context ‚Äî onError will receive it
      return { previousPosts };
    },

    // Step 6: if mutation fails, roll back to the snapshot
    onError: (err, postId, context) => {
      queryClient.setQueryData(['posts'], context.previousPosts);
      toast.error('Failed to like post. Please try again.');
    },

    // Step 7: after success OR error, sync cache with server truth
    onSettled: () => {
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['posts'] });
    },
  });
}

// Usage in component
function PostCard({ post }) {
  const { mutate: likePost, isPending } = useLikePost();

  return (
    <button
      onClick={() => likePost(post.id)}
      disabled={isPending}  // prevent double-click
    >
      {post.liked ? '‚ù§Ô∏è' : 'ü§ç'} {post.likes}
    </button>
  );
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`cancelQueries`** ‚Äî Prevents a concurrent background refetch from stomping over our optimistic update with stale server data.
2. **`getQueryData` snapshot** ‚Äî We save what the cache looked like before our change so `onError` can restore it exactly.
3. **`setQueryData`** ‚Äî Directly writes to the cache synchronously ‚Äî no network round-trip. React re-renders immediately with the new value.
4. **`context`** ‚Äî Whatever `onMutate` returns is passed as the third argument to `onError` and `onSettled`. This is the rollback mechanism.
5. **`onSettled`** ‚Äî Always fires (success or error). Invalidating here ensures eventual consistency by fetching the real server state.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Step | Complexity | Reason |
|------|-----------|--------|
| `cancelQueries` | O(K) | K = matching active queries |
| `setQueryData` | O(N) | N = items in the list |
| Rollback | O(1) | Replace with snapshot reference |
| Refetch on settle | O(N) | Server returns full list |

---

## Q34: How does React Query handle background refetching?

### üßí ELI5
Imagine a weather app that shows yesterday's forecast while quietly checking for today's update behind the scenes. When the new data arrives, the display updates ‚Äî you never saw a loading spinner. That's background refetching.

### üìä Diagram

```
  TRIGGERS FOR BACKGROUND REFETCH:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. refetchOnWindowFocus  (default: true)
     User switches tab, comes back ‚Üí stale queries refetch

  2. refetchOnMount  (default: true)
     Component mounts and data is stale ‚Üí refetch in background

  3. refetchOnReconnect  (default: true)
     Internet comes back ‚Üí refetch stale queries

  4. refetchInterval  (polling)
     refetchInterval: 5000 ‚Üí refetch every 5 seconds

  BEHAVIOUR DURING BACKGROUND REFETCH:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Cache has stale data
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ isLoading: false  ‚Üê NOT shown (data already exists)
       ‚îú‚îÄ isFetching: true  ‚Üê background fetch in progress
       ‚îî‚îÄ data: <stale>     ‚Üê previous data shown immediately

  Refetch completes
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îî‚îÄ data: <fresh>  ‚Üê UI updates silently

  DEDUPLICATION:
  Multiple components subscribe to same queryKey
  ‚Üí Only ONE network request fires
  ‚Üí All subscribers receive the same data simultaneously
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import { useQuery } from '@tanstack/react-query';

function LiveStockPrice({ ticker }) {
  const { data, isFetching, isLoading } = useQuery({
    queryKey: ['stock', ticker],
    queryFn: () => fetchStockPrice(ticker),

    // Step 1: poll every 10 seconds for live prices
    refetchInterval: 10_000,

    // Step 2: stop polling when tab is in background (save resources)
    refetchIntervalInBackground: false,

    // Step 3: refetch on window focus ‚Äî user comes back to tab
    refetchOnWindowFocus: true,

    // Step 4: treat data as stale after 5 seconds
    staleTime: 5_000,
  });

  return (
    <div>
      <span>${data?.price}</span>

      {/* Step 5: isFetching is true during background refetch */}
      {/* isLoading is only true when there's NO cached data AND fetching */}
      {isFetching && !isLoading && (
        <span style={{ fontSize: '0.8em', color: 'grey' }}>‚Üª updating</span>
      )}
    </div>
  );
}

// Step 6: manually trigger a background refetch
function RefreshButton({ ticker }) {
  const queryClient = useQueryClient();

  return (
    <button onClick={() => queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['stock', ticker] })}>
      Force Refresh
    </button>
  );
}

// Step 7: disable background behaviour for static data
useQuery({
  queryKey: ['countries'],
  queryFn: fetchCountries,
  staleTime: Infinity,         // never go stale
  refetchOnWindowFocus: false, // never background refetch
  refetchOnMount: false,       // only fetch once
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`isFetching` vs `isLoading`** ‚Äî `isLoading` is `true` only the very first time (no cached data). `isFetching` is `true` on every network request including background ones. Show a subtle indicator during `isFetching && !isLoading`.
2. **Request deduplication** ‚Äî If 10 components mount simultaneously with the same `queryKey`, React Query fires exactly one `queryFn` and distributes the result to all 10.
3. **`refetchInterval`** ‚Äî Polling. React Query manages the `setInterval` internally and clears it when the component unmounts or the query becomes inactive.
4. **`refetchIntervalInBackground: false`** ‚Äî Pauses polling when the document is hidden (browser tab in background), resuming when the tab becomes visible again.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Feature | Cost | Reason |
|---------|------|--------|
| Request deduplication | O(1) extra | One request regardless of subscriber count |
| `refetchInterval` | O(1) timer | Single interval per query |
| Window focus listener | O(1) | One global event listener |
| Subscriber notification | O(S) | S = number of subscribed components |

---

## Q35: What is the difference between `useForm` controlled vs uncontrolled in React Hook Form?

### üßí ELI5
**Controlled** is like a puppeteer pulling every string ‚Äî React knows every keystroke. **Uncontrolled** (React Hook Form's default) is like giving the actor a script but letting them perform freely ‚Äî the form manages its own values using native DOM, React only checks in when needed (submit, validate). RHF's approach means zero re-renders per keystroke.

### üìä Diagram

```
  CONTROLLED (standard React)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types "A" ‚Üí onChange fires ‚Üí setState("A")
  ‚Üí React re-renders ‚Üí input shows "A"
  User types "B" ‚Üí onChange fires ‚Üí setState("AB")
  ‚Üí React re-renders ‚Üí input shows "AB"
  ...every keystroke = 1 re-render

  UNCONTROLLED (React Hook Form default)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  User types "AB" ‚Üí native DOM holds value
  ‚Üí NO React re-renders during typing
  User submits ‚Üí RHF reads DOM values via ref
  ‚Üí validates ‚Üí returns errors / data

  register() returns:
  { name, ref, onChange, onBlur }
  ‚îî‚îÄ onChange: only triggers internal RHF validation
  ‚îî‚îÄ ref: RHF reads value directly from DOM node

  RE-RENDER COMPARISON:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Form with 10 fields, user types 50 chars:
  Controlled:   ~500 re-renders
  RHF default:  ~1-5 re-renders (only on error state change)
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import { useForm, Controller } from 'react-hook-form';
import { zodResolver } from '@hookform/resolvers/zod';
import { z } from 'zod';

// Step 1: define validation schema with Zod
const schema = z.object({
  email: z.string().email('Invalid email'),
  password: z.string().min(8, 'Password must be at least 8 characters'),
  age: z.coerce.number().min(18, 'Must be 18+'),
});

function LoginForm() {
  const {
    register,       // Step 2: uncontrolled ‚Äî attaches ref + onChange to native input
    control,        // Step 3: for controlled third-party components
    handleSubmit,
    formState: { errors, isSubmitting },
  } = useForm({
    resolver: zodResolver(schema),   // Step 4: RHF calls Zod on validate
    defaultValues: { email: '', password: '', age: '' },
    mode: 'onBlur',   // Step 5: validate on blur (not on every keystroke)
  });

  // Step 6: handleSubmit only fires if schema validation passes
  const onSubmit = async (data) => {
    await loginUser(data);
  };

  return (
    <form onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}>

      {/* Step 7: register() ‚Äî UNCONTROLLED: no useState, no value prop */}
      <input
        {...register('email')}  // spreads: name, ref, onChange, onBlur
        placeholder="Email"
      />
      {errors.email && <p>{errors.email.message}</p>}

      <input
        {...register('password')}
        type="password"
        placeholder="Password"
      />
      {errors.password && <p>{errors.password.message}</p>}

      {/* Step 8: Controller ‚Äî CONTROLLED: for custom/third-party inputs */}
      {/* Use when the component needs a value prop (e.g. Select, DatePicker) */}
      <Controller
        name="age"
        control={control}
        render={({ field }) => (
          // field = { value, onChange, onBlur, ref }
          <CustomAgeSelect {...field} />
        )}
      />
      {errors.age && <p>{errors.age.message}</p>}

      <button type="submit" disabled={isSubmitting}>
        {isSubmitting ? 'Logging in...' : 'Login'}
      </button>
    </form>
  );
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`register()`** ‚Äî Returns `{ name, ref, onChange, onBlur }`. Spreaded onto a native `<input>`, RHF tracks the value via the `ref` (DOM reference), not React state. Zero re-renders while typing.
2. **`Controller`** ‚Äî Wraps components that require a `value` prop (controlled). RHF internally manages state for that field. Use it for custom UI libraries (MUI, Radix, etc.).
3. **`mode`** ‚Äî Controls when validation runs: `'onSubmit'` (default), `'onBlur'`, `'onChange'` (expensive), `'onTouched'`, `'all'`.
4. **`zodResolver`** ‚Äî `@hookform/resolvers/zod` bridges RHF and Zod. On submit/validate, RHF passes values to Zod's `parse`, errors are mapped back to field names.
5. **`watch()`** ‚Äî When you need to observe a field value reactively (e.g. conditional fields), `watch('fieldName')` returns the current value but does trigger a re-render for that field.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Scenario | Re-renders | Reason |
|----------|------------|--------|
| Typing in `register()` field | 0 | DOM ref, no state update |
| Typing in `Controller` field | 1 per keystroke | Controlled, RHF state update |
| Blur validation (error appears) | 1 | `formState.errors` changes |
| `handleSubmit` call | 1 | Updates `isSubmitting` state |

---

## Q36: How do you share Zod schemas between frontend validation and API validation?

### üßí ELI5
You write the rules for a board game once and put them in the box. Both players (frontend and backend) read from the same rulebook. If you change a rule, everyone plays by the new rule automatically ‚Äî you don't have to hand-write two separate copies.

### üìä Diagram

```
  WITHOUT SHARED SCHEMA:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Frontend:  Yup schema { email: required, min 5 }
  Backend:   Joi schema { email: required, min 3 }   ‚Üê diverged!
  Result:    Frontend says valid, backend rejects ‚Üí user confused

  WITH SHARED ZOD SCHEMA (monorepo / shared package):
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  packages/shared/src/schemas/user.ts
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îú‚îÄ Frontend imports ‚Üí useForm + zodResolver
         ‚îÇ   Client-side validation: instant feedback
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îî‚îÄ Backend imports ‚Üí zod.parse() in API route
             Server-side validation: authoritative check
             TypeScript types inferred from same schema
  
  FLOW:
  User fills form ‚Üí Zod validates (frontend) ‚Üí submit
       ‚Üí API receives data ‚Üí Zod validates (backend)
       ‚Üí if server rejects ‚Üí error response to client
  
  INFERRED TYPES:
  type UserInput = z.infer<typeof userSchema>
  ‚Üí same type used in React component props AND Express handler
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ packages/shared/src/schemas/user.ts ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { z } from 'zod';

// Step 1: define schema ONCE in a shared location
export const createUserSchema = z.object({
  email: z.string().email('Invalid email address'),
  password: z
    .string()
    .min(8, 'At least 8 characters')
    .regex(/[A-Z]/, 'Must contain uppercase')
    .regex(/[0-9]/, 'Must contain a number'),
  age: z.coerce.number().int().min(18, 'Must be 18 or older'),
});

// Step 2: infer TypeScript type from schema ‚Äî used in both FE and BE
export type CreateUserInput = z.infer<typeof createUserSchema>;

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Frontend: React + React Hook Form ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { useForm } from 'react-hook-form';
import { zodResolver } from '@hookform/resolvers/zod';
import { createUserSchema, type CreateUserInput } from '@myapp/shared';

function RegisterForm() {
  // Step 3: resolver automatically validates against shared schema
  const { register, handleSubmit, formState: { errors } } = useForm<CreateUserInput>({
    resolver: zodResolver(createUserSchema),
  });

  const onSubmit = async (data: CreateUserInput) => {
    // Step 4: data is fully typed ‚Äî CreateUserInput from shared schema
    await fetch('/api/users', {
      method: 'POST',
      body: JSON.stringify(data),
      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
    });
  };

  return (
    <form onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}>
      <input {...register('email')} />
      {errors.email && <p>{errors.email.message}</p>}
      {/* ...other fields */}
    </form>
  );
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Backend: Express API route ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { createUserSchema } from '@myapp/shared';

app.post('/api/users', async (req, res) => {
  // Step 5: parse on server ‚Äî rejects malformed/malicious payloads
  const result = createUserSchema.safeParse(req.body);

  if (!result.success) {
    // Step 6: ZodError maps to structured field errors
    return res.status(400).json({
      errors: result.error.flatten().fieldErrors,
    });
  }

  // Step 7: result.data is fully typed as CreateUserInput
  const user = await db.users.create(result.data);
  res.status(201).json(user);
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Single source of truth** ‚Äî Schema lives in a shared package (`@myapp/shared`). Both sides import it. Any change to validation rules propagates to both environments automatically.
2. **`z.infer<typeof schema>`** ‚Äî Extracts the TypeScript type from the schema. No need to write a separate interface ‚Äî the type is always in sync with validation constraints.
3. **`safeParse` vs `parse`** ‚Äî `parse` throws on failure; `safeParse` returns `{ success, data, error }` ‚Äî better for API routes where you want to return 400, not crash.
4. **`error.flatten()`** ‚Äî Converts nested Zod errors into `{ fieldErrors: { email: ['Invalid email'] }, formErrors: [] }` ‚Äî easy to map back to form fields.
5. **Next.js Server Actions** ‚Äî With RSC, you can call `createUserSchema.parse(formData)` directly inside a server action, sharing the same schema with the `<form>` component in the same file.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Complexity | Reason |
|-----------|-----------|--------|
| `z.parse()` | O(F) | F = number of fields |
| `z.infer` type extraction | O(0) | Compile-time only, no runtime cost |
| `error.flatten()` | O(E) | E = number of validation errors |

---

## Q37: When would you choose Zustand over Redux Toolkit?

### üßí ELI5
**Redux Toolkit** is a city's traffic control centre ‚Äî powerful, centralised, great for complex intersections, but you need a whole team to run it. **Zustand** is traffic lights on a quiet road ‚Äî simple, gets the job done, no bureaucracy. Both move traffic; you pick based on how complex your roads are.

### üìä Diagram

```
  ZUSTAND
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚Ä¢ ~1KB bundle
  ‚Ä¢ No providers, no boilerplate
  ‚Ä¢ Single store or multiple stores
  ‚Ä¢ Direct mutation via immer (optional)
  ‚Ä¢ React hooks only ‚Äî no connect(), no mapStateToProps
  ‚Ä¢ No actions/reducers ‚Äî just functions in the store

  const useStore = create((set) => ({
    count: 0,
    increment: () => set(state => ({ count: state.count + 1 })),
  }));

  REDUX TOOLKIT (RTK)
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚Ä¢ Larger bundle, but battle-tested
  ‚Ä¢ DevTools with time-travel debugging
  ‚Ä¢ RTK Query = built-in data fetching + caching
  ‚Ä¢ Standardised: slices, actions, reducers, selectors
  ‚Ä¢ Better for large teams needing conventions
  ‚Ä¢ Middleware ecosystem (redux-thunk, redux-saga)

  DECISION MATRIX:
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ Scenario                   ‚îÇ Zustand ‚îÇ  RTK    ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îÇ Small/medium app UI state  ‚îÇ   ‚úÖ    ‚îÇ overkill‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Time-travel debugging      ‚îÇ   ‚ùå    ‚îÇ   ‚úÖ    ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Large team, many devs      ‚îÇ   ‚öÝÔ∏è   ‚îÇ   ‚úÖ    ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Server state (API data)    ‚îÇ  RQ*    ‚îÇ RTK Q   ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Minimal boilerplate        ‚îÇ   ‚úÖ    ‚îÇ   ‚ùå    ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Complex async workflows    ‚îÇ   ‚öÝÔ∏è   ‚îÇ   ‚úÖ    ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Bundle size matters        ‚îÇ   ‚úÖ    ‚îÇ   ‚öÝÔ∏è   ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
  * Use React Query for server state with either option
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ ZUSTAND ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { create } from 'zustand';
import { immer } from 'zustand/middleware/immer';
import { persist } from 'zustand/middleware';

// Step 1: define store with state + actions in one object
const useCartStore = create(
  persist(                    // Step 2: persist to localStorage automatically
    immer((set, get) => ({    // Step 3: immer enables direct mutation syntax
      items: [],
      total: 0,

      addItem: (product) => set((state) => {
        // Step 4: immer draft ‚Äî looks like mutation, produces immutable update
        const existing = state.items.find(i => i.id === product.id);
        if (existing) {
          existing.quantity += 1;
        } else {
          state.items.push({ ...product, quantity: 1 });
        }
        state.total = state.items.reduce((s, i) => s + i.price * i.quantity, 0);
      }),

      removeItem: (id) => set((state) => {
        state.items = state.items.filter(i => i.id !== id);
        state.total = state.items.reduce((s, i) => s + i.price * i.quantity, 0);
      }),

      clearCart: () => set({ items: [], total: 0 }),
    })),
    { name: 'cart-storage' }  // localStorage key
  )
);

// Step 5: subscribe to only what you need ‚Äî component only re-renders
// when items.length changes, not on any state change
function CartIcon() {
  const itemCount = useCartStore(state => state.items.length);
  return <span>üõí {itemCount}</span>;
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ REDUX TOOLKIT (for comparison) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
import { createSlice, configureStore } from '@reduxjs/toolkit';

// Step 6: RTK slice ‚Äî much more structured, better for teams
const cartSlice = createSlice({
  name: 'cart',
  initialState: { items: [], total: 0 },
  reducers: {
    addItem: (state, action) => {  // immer built-in to RTK
      const existing = state.items.find(i => i.id === action.payload.id);
      if (existing) existing.quantity += 1;
      else state.items.push({ ...action.payload, quantity: 1 });
    },
  },
});

// Step 7: explicit action creators ‚Äî easy to trace in DevTools / tests
export const { addItem } = cartSlice.actions;
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Choose Zustand when** ‚Äî you want minimal boilerplate for UI state (modals, themes, wizard steps, shopping cart). Small-medium apps, or when you're already using React Query for server state.
2. **Choose Redux Toolkit when** ‚Äî you need time-travel debugging, have a large team that benefits from enforced conventions, you're maintaining a legacy Redux codebase, or need RTK Query's advanced caching features.
3. **Don't use either for server state** ‚Äî React Query / SWR handle async data fetching better than either. Global state should only hold client-side state (auth token, UI preferences, shopping cart).
4. **Zustand selector granularity** ‚Äî Pass a selector function to `useStore(selector)` to prevent re-renders when unrelated state changes.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Zustand | Redux Toolkit |
|-----------|---------|---------------|
| Bundle size | ~1KB | ~10‚Äì40KB |
| Boilerplate lines for a slice | ~10 | ~30‚Äì50 |
| Selector re-render | O(1) per selector | O(1) per selector |
| Middleware pipeline | Optional | Built-in (thunk) |

---

## Q38: How do you handle global error state in React Query?

### üßí ELI5
Instead of putting a fire alarm in every room of your house, you have one central alarm panel. In React Query, instead of writing `if (isError) toast(error)` in every component, you register one global error handler that fires for any failed query or mutation.

### üìä Diagram

```
  COMPONENT-LEVEL ERROR HANDLING:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  <UserProfile>   ‚Üí if (isError) showToast()   ‚Üê repeated in every component
  <PostList>      ‚Üí if (isError) showToast()
  <Comments>      ‚Üí if (isError) showToast()

  GLOBAL ERROR HANDLING:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  QueryClient (onError callback)
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ Any query fails ‚Üí global handler fires
       ‚îú‚îÄ Any mutation fails ‚Üí global handler fires
       ‚îî‚îÄ Logs, toasts, redirects (e.g. 401 ‚Üí login)

  GRANULARITY OPTIONS:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. QueryClient defaultOptions.queries.onError   ‚Üê all queries
  2. QueryCache / MutationCache callbacks          ‚Üê recommended in v5
  3. useQuery({ onError })                         ‚Üê per-query override
  4. ErrorBoundary above <QueryClientProvider>     ‚Üê uncaught render errors
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
import {
  QueryClient,
  QueryClientProvider,
  QueryCache,
  MutationCache,
} from '@tanstack/react-query';
import toast from 'react-hot-toast';

// Step 1: attach global error handlers at QueryCache / MutationCache level
// This is the recommended approach in TanStack Query v4/v5
const queryClient = new QueryClient({
  queryCache: new QueryCache({
    // Step 2: fires whenever ANY query errors ‚Äî receives error + query metadata
    onError: (error, query) => {
      // Step 3: only show toast for non-silent errors
      // use query.meta to pass contextual flags from useQuery
      if (query.meta?.silent) return;

      if (error.status === 401) {
        // Step 4: redirect to login on unauthorised
        window.location.href = '/login';
        return;
      }

      // Step 5: show user-friendly toast for other errors
      const message = error.message ?? 'Something went wrong';
      toast.error(message);
    },
  }),

  mutationCache: new MutationCache({
    // Step 6: fires whenever ANY mutation errors
    onError: (error, variables, context, mutation) => {
      if (mutation.meta?.silent) return;

      toast.error(error.message ?? 'Action failed. Please try again.');
    },
  }),

  defaultOptions: {
    queries: {
      retry: (failureCount, error) => {
        // Step 7: don't retry 4xx errors ‚Äî they won't fix themselves
        if (error.status >= 400 && error.status < 500) return false;
        return failureCount < 2;
      },
      staleTime: 60_000,
    },
  },
});

// Step 8: wrap app with provider
function App() {
  return (
    <QueryClientProvider client={queryClient}>
      <Router />
    </QueryClientProvider>
  );
}

// Step 9: per-query opt-out ‚Äî mark as silent so global handler skips it
function useOptionalUser(id) {
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: ['user', id],
    queryFn: () => fetchUser(id),
    meta: { silent: true },       // global onError will skip this
    onError: (err) => {
      // handle locally instead
      setUserError(err);
    },
  });
}

// Step 10: combine with ErrorBoundary for render-phase errors
function Root() {
  return (
    <ErrorBoundary fallback={<GlobalErrorPage />}>
      <QueryClientProvider client={queryClient}>
        <App />
      </QueryClientProvider>
    </ErrorBoundary>
  );
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`QueryCache` / `MutationCache`** ‚Äî The correct place for global error handling in v4/v5. The `onError` at `defaultOptions` level was deprecated in v5 because it ran per-observer (once per `useQuery` call), not per query ‚Äî leading to duplicate toasts.
2. **`query.meta`** ‚Äî A freeform object you can attach to any query via `meta: { ... }`. Useful for flagging queries as silent, or tagging with a category for analytics.
3. **HTTP status-based routing** ‚Äî `401 ‚Üí login redirect`, `403 ‚Üí permission denied page`, `500 ‚Üí generic error toast`. Centralise this logic instead of duplicating it.
4. **`retry` function** ‚Äî Don't retry client errors (4xx). Retry server errors (5xx) up to N times with exponential backoff (built-in to React Query).
5. **Double coverage** ‚Äî React Query's error handling catches async errors. Wrap with `<ErrorBoundary>` to catch synchronous render errors that slip through.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Scenario | Cost | Reason |
|----------|------|--------|
| Global `onError` fires | O(1) | Single callback per failed request |
| Duplicate toast prevention | O(1) | `meta.silent` flag check |
| Retry logic | O(R) | R = number of retry attempts |
| Error boundary catch | O(1) | Single error per boundary |

---

## End of Section: REACT ‚Äî Ecosystem (Q32‚ÄìQ38)

---

# NODE.JS ‚Äî Core (Q39‚ÄìQ47)

---

## Q39: Explain the Node.js event loop. What is the order of execution between `setTimeout`, `Promise.then`, and `process.nextTick`?

### üßí ELI5
Imagine a chef with several incoming orders labeled by urgency. `process.nextTick` orders go to the top of the pile right now, before the chef finishes the current dish. `Promise.then` orders go to a "hot queue" checked after each dish. `setTimeout` orders sit in a separate tray checked once per trip to the pass. The chef (event loop) clears the hot queue completely before going to the next tray.

### üìä Diagram

```
  NODE.JS EVENT LOOP ‚Äî one tick
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  START
    ‚îÇ
    ‚ñº
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê  nextTick queue drained first (recursive = stack overflow risk!)
  ‚îÇ nextTick Queue‚îÇ  ‚Üê process.nextTick() callbacks
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
          ‚îÇ empty
          ‚ñº
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê  microtask queue (Promises)
  ‚îÇ Microtask Q   ‚îÇ  ‚Üê Promise.then / .catch / .finally / await
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
          ‚îÇ empty
          ‚ñº
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ PHASES (macro tasks)                                ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ                                                     ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  timers      ‚Üí setTimeout / setInterval callbacks  ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  pending I/O ‚Üí deferred I/O callbacks               ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  idle/prep   ‚Üí internal                             ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  poll        ‚Üí wait for I/O events (blocks here     ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ                if nothing else pending)             ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  check       ‚Üí setImmediate callbacks               ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ  close       ‚Üí socket.on('close') etc.              ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
          ‚îÇ
          ‚îî‚îÄ after EACH phase: drain nextTick + microtask queues

  PRIORITY ORDER:
  process.nextTick  >  Promise.then  >  setImmediate  >  setTimeout(0)
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// Step 1: synchronous code runs first ‚Äî always
console.log('1 sync');

// Step 2: nextTick queued ‚Äî runs before any I/O or timer
process.nextTick(() => console.log('2 nextTick'));

// Step 3: Promise microtask ‚Äî runs after nextTick queue is empty
Promise.resolve().then(() => console.log('3 Promise.then'));

// Step 4: setTimeout scheduled in timers phase ‚Äî runs AFTER microtasks
setTimeout(() => console.log('4 setTimeout'), 0);

// Step 5: setImmediate fires in check phase ‚Äî after poll phase
setImmediate(() => console.log('5 setImmediate'));

// Step 6: more sync ‚Äî still part of current call stack
console.log('6 sync');

// OUTPUT ORDER:
// 1 sync
// 6 sync
// 2 nextTick       ‚Üê nextTick queue drained before microtasks
// 3 Promise.then   ‚Üê microtask queue
// 4 setTimeout     ‚Üê timers phase (may swap with setImmediate outside I/O)
// 5 setImmediate   ‚Üê check phase

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ DANGER: recursive nextTick starves the event loop ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function starveLoop() {
  process.nextTick(starveLoop);  // ‚ùå NEVER DO THIS ‚Äî infinite nextTick
}                                //    I/O, timers, Promises never run

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ ASYNC/AWAIT = Promise.then under the hood ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
async function example() {
  console.log('A sync inside async');
  await Promise.resolve();
  console.log('B after await');  // runs in microtask queue
}
example();
console.log('C sync after call');
// Output: A ‚Üí C ‚Üí B
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Synchronous code** ‚Äî Runs to completion on the call stack before the event loop checks any queue.
2. **`process.nextTick`** ‚Äî Queued in the "nextTick queue", drained completely after the current operation AND after each individual phase transition. Higher priority than Promises.
3. **Promise microtasks** ‚Äî Drained after the nextTick queue is empty, before any macro-task phase.
4. **Timers phase** ‚Äî `setTimeout(fn, 0)` fires here, but "0" means "at least 0ms" ‚Äî the actual minimum is ~1ms. Phase runs its queued callbacks then moves on.
5. **Check phase** ‚Äî `setImmediate` fires here, always after poll. Inside an I/O callback, `setImmediate` reliably fires before `setTimeout(0)`.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Queue | Priority | Draining |
|-------|----------|----------|
| `process.nextTick` | Highest | Fully drained before microtasks |
| Promise microtasks | High | Fully drained before macro phases |
| `setImmediate` | Medium | One per check phase |
| `setTimeout(0)` | Medium | One per timers phase |
| I/O callbacks | Low | Poll phase |

---

## Q40: What is the difference between `setImmediate` and `setTimeout(() => {}, 0)`?

### üßí ELI5
Both say "do this soon, but not right now." `setImmediate` says "do this after you finish checking your inbox (I/O)." `setTimeout(0)` says "do this after at least 0 milliseconds ‚Äî check the clock first." When you're already inside an I/O callback, `setImmediate` always wins. Outside I/O, the order is unpredictable.

### üìä Diagram

```
  EVENT LOOP PHASES (simplified):
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  timers ‚Üí I/O ‚Üí poll ‚Üí CHECK ‚Üí close
     ‚Üë                    ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ                    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ setImmediate fires here
     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ setTimeout(0) fires here

  INSIDE I/O CALLBACK:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  fs.readFile() callback fires (poll phase)
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îú‚îÄ setTimeout(0) ‚Üí back to timers phase (NEXT loop)
       ‚îî‚îÄ setImmediate  ‚Üí check phase (THIS loop, comes NEXT)
  
  ‚Üí setImmediate ALWAYS fires before setTimeout(0) inside I/O

  OUTSIDE I/O (top level):
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  setTimeout(0) and setImmediate race:
  ‚Üí Order is NON-DETERMINISTIC (depends on OS timer resolution)
  ‚Üí May see either order in practice
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
const fs = require('fs');

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ OUTSIDE I/O ‚Äî order is non-deterministic ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
setTimeout(() => console.log('setTimeout'), 0);
setImmediate(() => console.log('setImmediate'));
// Could print either order ‚Äî don't rely on this!

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ INSIDE I/O ‚Äî setImmediate always wins ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
fs.readFile(__filename, () => {
  // Step 1: we are now inside the poll phase (I/O callback)
  setTimeout(() => console.log('timeout inside I/O'), 0);
  setImmediate(() => console.log('immediate inside I/O'));
  // Always prints: "immediate inside I/O" then "timeout inside I/O"
  // because check phase comes before timers in the SAME loop iteration
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ PRACTICAL RULE ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Use setImmediate when you want to:
// - Schedule work after the current I/O events are processed
// - Break up CPU-heavy work without blocking I/O
// - Ensure code runs in the check phase (predictable in I/O context)

// Use setTimeout(0) when you need:
// - Compatibility with browser environments (setImmediate is Node-only)
// - A minimum delay (even if effectively 0)

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Breaking up CPU work with setImmediate ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function processLargeArray(items, callback) {
  let index = 0;

  function processNext() {
    // Step 2: process a batch of 100 items
    const end = Math.min(index + 100, items.length);
    for (; index < end; index++) {
      heavyComputation(items[index]);
    }

    if (index < items.length) {
      // Step 3: yield to event loop via setImmediate ‚Äî allows I/O between batches
      setImmediate(processNext);
    } else {
      callback();
    }
  }

  processNext();
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Phase positions** ‚Äî `setTimeout` fires in the **timers** phase (first), `setImmediate` fires in the **check** phase (after poll). But the loop starts at timers ‚Äî so outside I/O, which fires first depends on when the loop starts relative to timer registration.
2. **Inside I/O** ‚Äî The current loop is already past the timers phase when the I/O callback runs. The next opportunity for timers is the *next iteration*, but check phase is *this iteration* ‚Üí `setImmediate` always wins.
3. **CPU work chunking** ‚Äî Using `setImmediate` between batches of heavy work lets the event loop process pending I/O between batches, keeping the server responsive.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Scenario | When fires | Deterministic? |
|----------|-----------|---------------|
| Top-level `setImmediate` | Check phase | vs setTimeout: no |
| Top-level `setTimeout(0)` | Timers phase | vs setImmediate: no |
| `setImmediate` inside I/O | Check phase (same iteration) | Yes ‚Äî before setTimeout |
| `setTimeout(0)` inside I/O | Timers phase (next iteration) | Yes ‚Äî after setImmediate |

---

## Q41: What are Streams in Node.js? Explain all 4 types.

### üßí ELI5
Imagine water flowing through pipes. You don't fill a giant tank first ‚Äî you let water flow continuously from source to destination. Node.js Streams are the same: process data in chunks as it arrives, not all at once. This saves memory when handling large files, network responses, or database results.

### üìä Diagram

```
  4 STREAM TYPES:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ

  1. READABLE  ‚Äî produces data (you consume it)
     Source ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ [chunk][chunk][chunk] ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ your code
     Examples: fs.createReadStream, http.IncomingMessage, process.stdin

  2. WRITABLE  ‚Äî consumes data (you write into it)
     Your code ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ [chunk][chunk][chunk] ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ Destination
     Examples: fs.createWriteStream, http.ServerResponse, process.stdout

  3. DUPLEX    ‚Äî both readable AND writable (independent channels)
     Data ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ [  DUPLEX  ] ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ Data
              [          ]
     Examples: net.Socket (TCP socket), WebSocket connection

  4. TRANSFORM ‚Äî duplex where output is derived from input
     Input ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ [TRANSFORM] ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ Modified Output
     Examples: zlib.createGzip (compress), crypto.createCipher (encrypt),
               csv-parser, through2

  PIPELINE:
  ReadStream ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ Transform (gunzip) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ Transform (parse) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ WriteStream
  file.gz   ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ decompress          ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ uppercase         ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ file.txt
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
const fs = require('fs');
const zlib = require('zlib');
const { Transform, pipeline } = require('stream');
const { promisify } = require('util');

const pipelineAsync = promisify(pipeline);

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ 1. READABLE: custom readable stream ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const { Readable } = require('stream');

// Step 1: create a readable that emits numbers 1‚Äì10
const numberStream = new Readable({
  objectMode: true,  // allows non-Buffer chunks
  read() {}          // no-op; we push manually
});

for (let i = 1; i <= 10; i++) {
  numberStream.push(i);
}
numberStream.push(null);  // Step 2: null signals end of stream

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ 2. WRITABLE: custom writable stream ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const { Writable } = require('stream');

const logWriter = new Writable({
  objectMode: true,
  // Step 3: _write called for each chunk
  write(chunk, encoding, callback) {
    console.log('Received:', chunk);
    callback();  // Step 4: MUST call callback to signal "ready for next chunk"
  },
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ 3. TRANSFORM: uppercase transformer ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const { Transform } = require('stream');

const upperCase = new Transform({
  // Step 5: receives input chunk, pushes transformed output
  transform(chunk, encoding, callback) {
    this.push(chunk.toString().toUpperCase());
    callback();
  },
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ 4. Full pipeline: read file ‚Üí gzip ‚Üí write ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
async function compressFile(input, output) {
  // Step 6: pipeline handles backpressure AND cleans up on error
  await pipelineAsync(
    fs.createReadStream(input),    // Readable
    zlib.createGzip(),             // Transform (compress)
    fs.createWriteStream(output),  // Writable
  );
  console.log('Compression complete');
}

compressFile('large.log', 'large.log.gz');

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ 5. Consuming a readable stream ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
async function readLines(filePath) {
  const rl = require('readline').createInterface({
    input: fs.createReadStream(filePath),  // Step 7: stream, not readFileSync
    crlfDelay: Infinity,
  });

  for await (const line of rl) {  // Step 8: async iteration over stream
    console.log(line);
  }
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Readable internal modes** ‚Äî Flowing mode (data events push chunks automatically) and paused mode (you call `.read()` manually). `pipe()` and `for await` use flowing mode.
2. **`callback()`** ‚Äî In `_write` and `_transform`, calling `callback()` signals "I'm done processing this chunk, send the next one." Not calling it = stream stalls (backpressure mechanism).
3. **`objectMode: true`** ‚Äî By default streams operate on Buffers/strings. Object mode allows any JS value as a chunk ‚Äî useful for streaming database rows.
4. **`pipeline` vs `pipe`** ‚Äî `pipeline` (Node 10+) automatically destroys all streams and handles errors. Raw `pipe` leaks streams on error. Always prefer `pipeline`.
5. **Memory efficiency** ‚Äî Reading a 10GB file with `createReadStream` uses ~64KB at a time. `readFileSync` loads all 10GB into RAM.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Time | Space |
|-----------|------|-------|
| Stream 1GB file | O(N) | O(chunk) ‚âà O(1) |
| `readFileSync` 1GB | O(N) | O(N) ‚Äî whole file in RAM |
| Transform per chunk | O(C) | O(C) ‚Äî C = chunk size |
| Pipeline setup | O(1) | O(1) |

---

## Q42: What is backpressure in streams and how does `.pipe()` handle it?

### üßí ELI5
Imagine filling bottles on a conveyor belt. If bottles arrive faster than you can cap them, they pile up and eventually fall off. Backpressure is the signal: "slow down, I'm full!" `.pipe()` is a smart conveyor controller that automatically pauses the source when the destination is overwhelmed and resumes when it catches up.

### üìä Diagram

```
  WITHOUT BACKPRESSURE HANDLING:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ReadStream (fast) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ WriteStream (slow)
  Reads 100MB/s         Writes 10MB/s
       ‚îÇ
       ‚îî‚îÄ internal buffer fills up ‚Üí memory bloat ‚Üí OOM crash

  WITH BACKPRESSURE (.pipe() / pipeline):
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ReadStream ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ .pipe() ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñ∂ WriteStream
      ‚îÇ              ‚îÇ
      ‚îÇ   writable.write() returns false (buffer full)
      ‚îÇ              ‚îÇ
      ‚îÇ   .pipe() calls readable.pause() automatically
      ‚îÇ              ‚îÇ
      ‚îÇ   writable emits 'drain' (buffer flushed)
      ‚îÇ              ‚îÇ
      ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ .pipe() calls readable.resume() automatically

  MANUAL write() return value:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  const ok = writable.write(chunk);
  if (!ok) {
    readable.pause();                    // stop reading
    writable.once('drain', () => {
      readable.resume();                 // safe to continue
    });
  }
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
const fs = require('fs');
const { pipeline, Transform } = require('stream');
const { promisify } = require('util');

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ .pipe() ‚Äî handles backpressure automatically ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Step 1: .pipe() wires up 'drain' and 'pause' internally
fs.createReadStream('huge-file.txt')
  .pipe(new Transform({
    transform(chunk, enc, cb) {
      // simulate slow processing
      setTimeout(() => { this.push(chunk); cb(); }, 10);
    }
  }))
  .pipe(fs.createWriteStream('output.txt'));

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ pipeline() ‚Äî preferred: handles errors AND backpressure ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const pipelineAsync = promisify(pipeline);

async function processFile() {
  await pipelineAsync(
    fs.createReadStream('huge-file.txt'),
    new Transform({
      transform(chunk, enc, cb) {
        this.push(chunk.toString().toUpperCase());
        cb();
      },
    }),
    fs.createWriteStream('output.txt'),
  );
  // Step 2: all streams destroyed on completion or error ‚Äî no leaks
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ MANUAL backpressure (for custom streams) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function safeCopy(readable, writable) {
  readable.on('data', (chunk) => {
    // Step 3: write returns false when internal buffer is full
    const ok = writable.write(chunk);

    if (!ok) {
      // Step 4: pause the source ‚Äî stop producing data
      readable.pause();

      // Step 5: once writable drains its buffer, resume reading
      writable.once('drain', () => {
        readable.resume();
      });
    }
  });

  readable.on('end', () => writable.end());
  readable.on('error', (err) => writable.destroy(err));
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ highWaterMark ‚Äî controls buffer size ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Step 6: increase buffer for high-throughput scenarios (default: 16KB)
const readStream = fs.createReadStream('file.txt', {
  highWaterMark: 64 * 1024,  // 64KB chunks
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`highWaterMark`** ‚Äî Each stream has an internal buffer. When it exceeds `highWaterMark`, `write()` returns `false` ‚Äî the backpressure signal.
2. **`.pipe()` magic** ‚Äî Listens for `writable.write()` returning `false`, calls `readable.pause()`. Listens for `drain`, calls `readable.resume()`. This keeps memory bounded.
3. **`.pipe()` error problem** ‚Äî If a stream in the middle of a chain errors, `.pipe()` doesn't automatically destroy the other streams ‚Äî you get leaks. `pipeline()` fixes this.
4. **`pipeline`** ‚Äî Node 10+ utility that wires up error handling AND backpressure for all streams in the chain. Always use `pipeline` over `.pipe()` for production code.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Scenario | Memory | Reason |
|----------|--------|--------|
| No backpressure handling | O(N) | Buffer grows unbounded |
| `.pipe()` / `pipeline` | O(highWaterMark) | Bounded buffer |
| `highWaterMark: 64KB` | ~64KB peak | Fixed ceiling |

---

## Q43: What is the difference between Buffers and Streams? When would you use each?

### üßí ELI5
A **Buffer** is a bucket ‚Äî you fill the whole bucket, carry it, and pour it out. A **Stream** is a hose ‚Äî water flows continuously from tap to destination without filling a giant bucket first. Use a bucket for small amounts; use a hose for large volumes.

### üìä Diagram

```
  BUFFER
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  fs.readFile('movie.mp4', (err, data) => {
    // 'data' is a Buffer ‚Äî entire 4GB file in RAM!
    process(data);
  });

  Memory: [====4GB====]  ‚Üê entire file loaded

  STREAM
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  fs.createReadStream('movie.mp4').pipe(res);
  // 64KB at a time flows from disk ‚Üí network
  
  Memory: [=64KB=]  ‚Üê only current chunk in RAM

  BUFFER USE CASES:           STREAM USE CASES:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ             ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚Ä¢ Small files (<10MB)       ‚Ä¢ Large files (video, logs)
  ‚Ä¢ Binary data manipulation  ‚Ä¢ Real-time data (audio, video)
  ‚Ä¢ Crypto (hash, HMAC)       ‚Ä¢ HTTP responses (piped to client)
  ‚Ä¢ Network protocol parsing  ‚Ä¢ Database result sets
  ‚Ä¢ Image thumbnails          ‚Ä¢ File transformations
  ‚Ä¢ JSON payloads             ‚Ä¢ Compression / encryption pipeline
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ BUFFER: binary data manipulation ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const crypto = require('crypto');

// Step 1: Buffer.from ‚Äî create from string, array, or ArrayBuffer
const buf = Buffer.from('Hello, World!', 'utf8');
console.log(buf);           // <Buffer 48 65 6c 6c 6f ...>
console.log(buf.length);    // 13 bytes
console.log(buf.toString()); // 'Hello, World!'

// Step 2: Buffer.alloc ‚Äî fixed-size zeroed buffer (safe, use over allocUnsafe)
const safeBuf = Buffer.alloc(16);  // 16 bytes, all zeros

// Step 3: Buffer for crypto ‚Äî HMAC needs binary data
function signPayload(payload, secret) {
  return crypto
    .createHmac('sha256', secret)
    .update(Buffer.from(JSON.stringify(payload)))
    .digest('hex');
}

// Step 4: Buffer for image processing
const sharp = require('sharp');
app.post('/thumbnail', async (req, res) => {
  // Buffer OK here ‚Äî thumbnail is small enough to hold in memory
  const thumbnail = await sharp(req.body)
    .resize(200, 200)
    .toBuffer();      // Step 5: returns Buffer with processed image
  res.send(thumbnail);
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ STREAM: large file serving ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const fs = require('fs');

// Step 6: stream file directly to HTTP response ‚Äî never loads into RAM
app.get('/video/:id', (req, res) => {
  const { range } = req.headers;
  const videoPath = `./videos/${req.params.id}.mp4`;
  const stat = fs.statSync(videoPath);

  if (range) {
    // Step 7: range request for video seeking
    const [start, end] = range.replace('bytes=', '').split('-').map(Number);
    const chunkSize = (end || stat.size - 1) - start + 1;

    res.writeHead(206, {
      'Content-Range': `bytes ${start}-${end || stat.size - 1}/${stat.size}`,
      'Content-Length': chunkSize,
      'Content-Type': 'video/mp4',
    });

    fs.createReadStream(videoPath, { start, end: end || stat.size - 1 }).pipe(res);
  } else {
    res.writeHead(200, { 'Content-Length': stat.size, 'Content-Type': 'video/mp4' });
    fs.createReadStream(videoPath).pipe(res);  // Step 8: stream, don't buffer
  }
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **`Buffer.alloc` vs `Buffer.allocUnsafe`** ‚Äî `alloc` zeroes memory (safe, slight perf cost). `allocUnsafe` skips zeroing ‚Äî old memory contents may be readable. Never use `allocUnsafe` for user-facing data.
2. **Buffers in crypto** ‚Äî Hash/HMAC functions operate on raw bytes. `Buffer.from(string)` converts to UTF-8 bytes which is what crypto expects.
3. **Streams for HTTP responses** ‚Äî `res.pipe()` lets Node write chunks as they're read from disk. Client starts receiving data immediately. No RAM penalty regardless of file size.
4. **When buffers are fine** ‚Äî Anything under a few MB that needs random access (indexing into bytes) or must be passed to an API requiring a complete buffer (most crypto, image APIs).

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Buffer | Stream |
|-----------|--------|--------|
| Memory for 1GB file | O(N) = 1GB RAM | O(chunk) ‚âà 64KB |
| First byte to client | After full read | Immediate |
| Random byte access | O(1) | Not supported |
| Transformation | Copy needed | In-place per chunk |

---

## Q44: How does the Node.js Cluster module work? How does it differ from Worker Threads?

### üßí ELI5
**Cluster** is like opening multiple identical restaurants on the same street ‚Äî each is a full independent restaurant (process), and a manager (master) sends customers to whichever restaurant is free. **Worker Threads** is like one restaurant with multiple chefs at different stations ‚Äî they share the same kitchen (memory) but work in parallel on different dishes.

### üìä Diagram

```
  CLUSTER MODULE
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Master Process (PID 1000)
  ‚îú‚îÄ Listens on port 3000
  ‚îú‚îÄ Distributes connections round-robin
  ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ Worker 1 (PID 1001) ‚Äî full Node.js process
  ‚îú‚îÄ Worker 2 (PID 1002) ‚Äî full Node.js process
  ‚îú‚îÄ Worker 3 (PID 1003) ‚Äî full Node.js process
  ‚îî‚îÄ Worker 4 (PID 1004) ‚Äî full Node.js process (= CPU cores)

  Communication: IPC (inter-process communication) ‚Äî slow for big data
  Memory: SEPARATE ‚Äî each worker has its own heap
  Crash: One worker crash doesn't affect others

  WORKER THREADS
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Main Thread
  ‚îú‚îÄ SharedArrayBuffer ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê shared memory (fast!)
  ‚îÇ                      ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ Worker Thread 1 ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îú‚îÄ Worker Thread 2 ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îî‚îÄ Worker Thread 3 ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

  Communication: postMessage (structured clone) or SharedArrayBuffer
  Memory: CAN SHARE via SharedArrayBuffer/Atomics
  Use: CPU-bound tasks (image processing, crypto, ML)
  
  CHOOSING:
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ                  ‚îÇ Cluster         ‚îÇ Worker Threads   ‚îÇ
  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
  ‚îÇ Best for         ‚îÇ I/O-bound HTTP  ‚îÇ CPU-bound tasks  ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Memory           ‚îÇ Isolated        ‚îÇ Shareable        ‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Crash isolation  ‚îÇ ‚úÖ              ‚îÇ ‚ùå (crashes main)‚îÇ
  ‚îÇ Setup complexity ‚îÇ Simple          ‚îÇ More complex     ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ CLUSTER: HTTP server across all CPU cores ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const cluster = require('cluster');
const os = require('os');
const http = require('http');

if (cluster.isPrimary) {
  const numCPUs = os.cpus().length;  // Step 1: one worker per CPU core
  console.log(`Primary PID ${process.pid} ‚Äî forking ${numCPUs} workers`);

  for (let i = 0; i < numCPUs; i++) {
    cluster.fork();  // Step 2: spawn worker processes
  }

  // Step 3: respawn crashed workers
  cluster.on('exit', (worker, code, signal) => {
    console.log(`Worker ${worker.process.pid} died ‚Äî restarting`);
    cluster.fork();
  });

} else {
  // Step 4: each worker runs the same HTTP server code
  // Cluster OS distributes incoming connections across workers
  http.createServer((req, res) => {
    res.end(`Handled by worker PID ${process.pid}`);
  }).listen(3000);

  console.log(`Worker ${process.pid} started`);
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ WORKER THREADS: CPU-bound task ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// worker.js
const { workerData, parentPort } = require('worker_threads');

// Step 5: CPU-intensive task runs in separate thread (doesn't block event loop)
function computeHash(data) {
  const crypto = require('crypto');
  return crypto.createHash('sha256').update(data).digest('hex');
}

parentPort.postMessage(computeHash(workerData));  // Step 6: send result back

// main.js
const { Worker } = require('worker_threads');

function hashInWorker(data) {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    // Step 7: spawn worker for CPU work ‚Äî main event loop stays free
    const worker = new Worker('./worker.js', { workerData: data });
    worker.on('message', resolve);
    worker.on('error', reject);
    worker.on('exit', (code) => {
      if (code !== 0) reject(new Error(`Worker exited with code ${code}`));
    });
  });
}

// Step 8: main thread stays responsive during hashing
app.post('/hash', async (req, res) => {
  const hash = await hashInWorker(req.body.data);
  res.json({ hash });
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Cluster for I/O-bound** ‚Äî HTTP servers spend most time waiting for I/O. Multiple processes each with their own event loop = linear throughput scaling across cores.
2. **Worker Threads for CPU-bound** ‚Äî Image resizing, video encoding, ML inference, or heavy cryptography blocks the event loop. Offload to a thread pool via Worker Threads.
3. **Memory isolation** ‚Äî Cluster workers are separate processes with separate heaps. A memory leak in one worker won't affect others. Worker Threads share the V8 heap ‚Äî a bug can corrupt shared state.
4. **`SharedArrayBuffer`** ‚Äî Worker Threads can share a raw memory buffer. Use `Atomics` for synchronisation to avoid race conditions.
5. **PM2** ‚Äî In production, PM2's cluster mode wraps Node's `cluster` module with monitoring, log aggregation, and graceful reloads.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Cluster | Worker Threads |
|-----------|---------|----------------|
| Spawn time | ~50‚Äì200ms (fork process) | ~5‚Äì20ms (thread) |
| IPC message | O(M) copy | O(M) structured clone or O(1) shared buffer |
| Memory per unit | Full heap (~50MB) | Shared heap + stack |
| Max parallelism | CPU count | CPU count |

---

## Q45: What is `process.nextTick`? Why is it higher priority than Promises?

### üßí ELI5
`process.nextTick` is like tapping a coworker on the shoulder right now ‚Äî before they can start their next task. Promise callbacks are like passing a note to be read after the current task finishes. The tap always gets attention faster than the note.

### üìä Diagram

```
  CURRENT OPERATION (call stack)
         ‚îÇ
         ‚îÇ  completes
         ‚ñº
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ  nextTick queue         ‚îÇ  ‚Üê ALL nextTick callbacks drained first
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
         ‚îÇ  empty
         ‚ñº
  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
  ‚îÇ  Promise microtask queue‚îÇ  ‚Üê then all Promise.then callbacks
  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
         ‚îÇ  empty
         ‚ñº
  next event loop phase (timers ‚Üí I/O ‚Üí poll ‚Üí check ‚Üí close)

  WHY nextTick > Promises:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  Historical: nextTick existed before Promises in Node.js
  Design: nextTick is a "same-phase epilogue" ‚Äî runs before phase transition
  Promises are ECMAScript microtasks ‚Äî added later as a separate queue
  Node chose to keep nextTick higher-priority for backward compatibility
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// Step 1: demonstrate priority ordering
Promise.resolve().then(() => console.log('Promise 1'));
process.nextTick(() => console.log('nextTick 1'));
Promise.resolve().then(() => console.log('Promise 2'));
process.nextTick(() => console.log('nextTick 2'));

// Output:
// nextTick 1
// nextTick 2
// Promise 1
// Promise 2

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ VALID USE CASE: emit event after constructor returns ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
const { EventEmitter } = require('events');

class MyEmitter extends EventEmitter {
  constructor() {
    super();
    // Step 2: if we emitted 'ready' synchronously here, callers who register
    // listeners AFTER construction would miss it
    // nextTick defers emission until after construction completes
    process.nextTick(() => this.emit('ready'));
  }
}

const emitter = new MyEmitter();
// Step 3: listener registered AFTER constructor ‚Äî still catches 'ready'
emitter.on('ready', () => console.log('emitter is ready'));

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ VALID USE CASE: ensure async callback consistency ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
function readData(id, callback) {
  if (cache.has(id)) {
    // Step 4: without nextTick, this is synchronous ‚Äî inconsistent behaviour
    // callers might experience both sync and async code paths
    process.nextTick(() => callback(null, cache.get(id)));  // always async
    return;
  }
  db.find(id, callback);
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ DANGER: accidental recursion ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Step 5: recursive nextTick starves the event loop
// NEVER do this:
function badRecurse() {
  process.nextTick(badRecurse);  // ‚ùå I/O never runs
}

// Use setImmediate for recursive deferral instead:
function goodRecurse(items, index) {
  if (index >= items.length) return;
  process(items[index]);
  setImmediate(() => goodRecurse(items, index + 1));  // ‚úÖ yields to I/O
}
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Two queues** ‚Äî Node.js maintains two microtask-like queues: the nextTick queue (internal V8/libuv) and the Promise queue (ECMAScript spec). The nextTick queue is drained first.
2. **Consistency pattern** ‚Äî Use `process.nextTick` to make a callback always asynchronous when it may sometimes be synchronous (cached value). This prevents "Zalgo" ‚Äî the bug where a function is sometimes sync, sometimes async.
3. **EventEmitter pattern** ‚Äî Deferring `emit` to nextTick ensures all listeners can register before the event fires.
4. **Avoid deep nextTick recursion** ‚Äî Each nextTick callback is processed before any I/O. Recursive nextTick = starvation. Use `setImmediate` for iteration that should yield to I/O.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Queue | Drains | Notes |
|-------|--------|-------|
| nextTick | Before microtasks | Can starve if recursive |
| Promise microtask | After nextTick | Also drains fully each phase |
| Combined queues | Before each macro phase | Both checked after each I/O event too |

---

## Q46: How do you handle `uncaughtException` and `unhandledRejection` in production?

### üßí ELI5
`uncaughtException` is your app's last-chance smoke alarm ‚Äî it fires when something exploded and nobody caught it. `unhandledRejection` is when a Promise fails and nobody listened to the failure. Both need a proper response: log the disaster, alert someone, and exit safely ‚Äî don't silently ignore them or your app will be in an unknown, corrupted state.

### üìä Diagram

```
  uncaughtException
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  throw new Error('oops')   ‚Üí no try/catch around it
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  process.on('uncaughtException', handler)
         ‚îÇ
  handler runs  ‚Üí  log  ‚Üí  notify  ‚Üí  process.exit(1)
  ‚öÝÔ∏è  App state is CORRUPT ‚Äî exit is mandatory after complex errors

  unhandledRejection
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  fetchData()   // returns Promise
  // no .catch() and no await in try/catch
         ‚îÇ
         Promise rejects
         ‚îÇ
         ‚ñº
  process.on('unhandledRejection', handler)
         ‚îÇ
  In Node 15+: process exits with code 1 automatically
  In Node 14-: just a warning (dangerous ‚Äî silent failures)

  BEST PRACTICE:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  uncaughtException ‚Üí log ‚Üí graceful shutdown ‚Üí exit(1)
  unhandledRejection ‚Üí log ‚Üí optionally exit(1)
  Both ‚Üí alert on-call (PagerDuty, Datadog, Sentry)
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
const Sentry = require('@sentry/node');

Sentry.init({ dsn: process.env.SENTRY_DSN });

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ uncaughtException ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
process.on('uncaughtException', (error, origin) => {
  // Step 1: log with full context ‚Äî error might reveal compromised state
  console.error('UNCAUGHT EXCEPTION:', { error: error.message, origin, stack: error.stack });

  // Step 2: report to error tracking before we exit
  Sentry.captureException(error);

  // Step 3: attempt graceful shutdown ‚Äî close DB connections, HTTP server
  // Wrap in timeout in case the shutdown itself hangs
  gracefulShutdown().finally(() => {
    // Step 4: MUST exit ‚Äî process state is unknown after uncaught exception
    // Do NOT continue running ‚Äî this is the dangerous anti-pattern
    process.exit(1);
  });
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ unhandledRejection ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
process.on('unhandledRejection', (reason, promise) => {
  // Step 5: reason is the rejection value; promise is the rejected Promise
  console.error('UNHANDLED REJECTION:', { reason, promise });
  Sentry.captureException(reason);

  // Step 6: in Node 15+ this exits automatically; be explicit for clarity
  process.exit(1);
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ Graceful shutdown helper ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
async function gracefulShutdown() {
  // Step 7: stop accepting new connections
  await new Promise((resolve) => server.close(resolve));

  // Step 8: drain in-flight requests (timeout after 5s)
  await Promise.race([
    drainConnections(),
    new Promise((_, reject) => setTimeout(() => reject(new Error('Shutdown timeout')), 5000)),
  ]);

  // Step 9: close database pool
  await db.end();
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ PREVENTION: avoid unhandledRejection in the first place ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// Always await with try/catch or attach .catch():

// ‚ùå BAD ‚Äî fire and forget (unhandled rejection if this fails)
sendEmail(user);

// ‚úÖ GOOD
sendEmail(user).catch((err) => {
  logger.warn('Email send failed, queuing for retry', err);
  emailQueue.add(user);
});

// ‚úÖ GOOD ‚Äî Express async error handling
app.get('/user/:id', async (req, res, next) => {
  try {
    const user = await db.findUser(req.params.id);
    res.json(user);
  } catch (err) {
    next(err);  // Step 10: pass to Express error middleware
  }
});
```

### üîç Step-by-Step Explanation

1. **Do NOT recover from `uncaughtException`** ‚Äî The process state is unknown. Memory may be corrupted. Attempting to continue is a security and reliability risk. Log, notify, and exit.
2. **`unhandledRejection` is a code bug** ‚Äî Every Promise in production code must have error handling. Node 15+ was changed to exit on unhandled rejections to force developers to handle them.
3. **Graceful shutdown** ‚Äî Before exiting, stop accepting new connections, finish in-flight requests, and close DB pools. This prevents data corruption.
4. **Restart with a process manager** ‚Äî PM2, systemd, or Kubernetes will restart the process after `exit(1)`. This is the correct recovery mechanism ‚Äî not catching and ignoring.
5. **`origin` in `uncaughtException`** ‚Äî The second argument (`'uncaughtException'` or `'unhandledRejection'`) helps distinguish the source.

### ‚è±Ô∏è Complexity

| Operation | Cost | Notes |
|-----------|------|-------|
| `process.on` handler | O(1) | Single event listener |
| Sentry capture | O(1) async | Non-blocking HTTP report |
| Graceful shutdown | O(C) | C = in-flight connections |
| `process.exit(1)` | O(1) | Immediate OS-level termination |

---

## Q47: What causes a memory leak in Node.js? How do you detect and fix it?

### üßí ELI5
Memory leaks are like never throwing away old mail. Over time, your desk (RAM) fills up. In Node.js, old mail = objects that are no longer needed but still have a reference somewhere, so the garbage collector can't throw them away. The garbage truck (GC) can't take what's still "claimed."

### üìä Diagram

```
  COMMON LEAK SOURCES:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  1. Global variables / growing caches
     global.cache = {};
     setInterval(() => cache[Date.now()] = heavyObject, 1);
     ‚Üí cache grows forever, never cleared

  2. Event listeners not removed
     emitter.on('data', handler);   // added on every request
     // handler holds closure over large object
     // never emitter.off() ‚Üí handler count grows

  3. Closures over large objects
     function createLeak() {
       const bigArray = new Array(1000000).fill(0);
       return () => bigArray[0]; // closure retains bigArray
     }

  4. Timers not cleared
     setInterval(fn, 1000);  // created per request, never clearInterval'd

  5. Circular references (less common ‚Äî GC handles most)

  DETECTION TOOLS:
  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  ‚Ä¢ node --inspect ‚Üí Chrome DevTools heap snapshot
  ‚Ä¢ clinic.js doctor (npm i -g clinic)
  ‚Ä¢ heapdump package
  ‚Ä¢ process.memoryUsage() monitoring
  ‚Ä¢ Datadog / New Relic APM
```

### üíª Code Example

```javascript
// ‚îÄ‚îÄ LEAK 1: unbounded cache ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚ùå BAD ‚Äî cache grows forever
const cache = {};
app.get('/data/:id', async (req, res) => {
  if (!cache[req.params.id]) {
    cache[req.params.id] = await fetchExpensiveData(req.params.id);
  }
  res.json(cache[req.params.id]);
});

// ‚úÖ FIX ‚Äî use LRU cache with size limit
const LRU = require('lru-cache');
const cache = new LRU({ max: 500, ttl: 1000 * 60 * 5 }); // 500 items, 5min TTL

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ LEAK 2: event listeners ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚ùå BAD ‚Äî new listener added every time, never removed
class DataProcessor extends EventEmitter {
  start() {
    externalEmitter.on('data', this.processData.bind(this)); // grows per call!
  }
}
// Step 1: save reference to bound handler so it can be removed
class DataProcessor extends EventEmitter {
  constructor() {
    super();
    this._handler = this.processData.bind(this); // Step 2: stable reference
  }
  start()  { externalEmitter.on('data', this._handler); }
  stop()   { externalEmitter.off('data', this._handler); } // ‚úÖ remove on stop
}

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ LEAK 3: timer not cleared ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
// ‚ùå BAD ‚Äî interval created per WebSocket connection, never cleared
wss.on('connection', (socket) => {
  setInterval(() => socket.send(JSON.stringify(getMetrics())), 1000);
  // socket closes but interval keeps firing, holding reference
});

// ‚úÖ FIX
wss.on('connection', (socket) => {
  const id = setInterval(() => socket.send(JSON.stringify(getMetrics())), 1000);
  socket.on('close', () => clearInterval(id)); // Step 3: clean up on disconnect
});

// ‚îÄ‚îÄ DETECTION: memory usage monitoring ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
setInterval(() => {
```
